The Secret Beneath The Crystal Surface


    Prologue

      Dear Tilden, 

      First off, how are you doing? I hope you have been able to find some time to relax, even though I know you well enough to assume that you've probably signed up for all the summer classes you could fit in a day.
      It's been a while since I've written letters by hand. Don't laugh! Can't you tell that I've been working on my handwriting? Anyway, you don't have to worry about me. Ba and Ma don't have me grounded anymore, and I have plenty of free time to wander. They've given me my phone back, but I wanted to write this one final letter. So how do I put this? Some things are better said on paper. But of course I'm going to text this to you too anyway-I'll have long returned home by the time this letter will even get to you.
      I'm still angry at our parents for dragging me to Ba's business meeting in Hawaii without any input, but all that initial frustration has subsided now, because guess what? This is a summer I'll never forget! I've been spending all my time outside on the beaches, and you'll never believe who I met.
      I met a merman.

      I hope you'll visit us back in San Francisco soon. I want to tell you everything in person.
      Your sister, Ruby

      P.S.
      Singsing is a puppy, not a replacement sibling. Ba and Ma still love you.

      P.P.S
      Who is San???!!!

    Chapter 1
One Month Before

	"Ruby Zhang?"
	"Present!" Ruby waved her hand in the air as she shot up from her seat.
	"Alright, then." A little taken aback at the girl's enthusiasm, a slight frown flickered across the substitute teacher's face. "Your teacher says that all of you can use this period as a study hall. He hopes that you'll make good use of your time and quietly review whatever you want."
	Ruby sat back down and rummaged under the desk for her backpack.
	"Ruby," a voice whispered. "Do you have an extra pencil?" It was Grace, one of Ruby's best friends.
	Ruby turned to look at her table mate after plopping her AP Physics book down on the table and flipping it open. Colored sticky notes stuck out from the pages, each one covered in nearly illegible scrawl. "What happened to yours?" Ruby inquired in equal quiet as she passed a pencil to her friend. "You bring that sparkly pencil case of yours everywhere."
	Grace dropped her gaze. "I do, but Everett asked me again during first period if he could borrow a pencil."
	"Everett." Ruby folded her arms over her chest, and her expression was distasteful as she wrinkled her nose. "Grace, you can't just keep letting him take your stuff like that. Tell him that if he doesn't return your pencils, you won't lend them to him anymore."
	"He's just borrowing it-"
	"But has he ever returned any of them?"
	"Well, no. But-"
	"Tell him that he's nearly an adult, and it's his responsibility to take care of his own stuff. I know you don't like to argue with people, but you have to stand up for yourself. Otherwise this will just keep happening."
	"You're right." Grace let out a sigh as she swiveled around to rummage in her backpack for her own textbook. "Tomorrow when he asks again, I'll just tell him that I don't have any more pencils."
	Ruby grinned. "That's the spirit."
	"If only I could borrow your confidence," Grace lamented as she ran a hand through her poofy hair.
	"What's going on over here?" The two girls whirled around to find the substitute teacher looking down his nose at them. "No talking."
	"We're sorry," Grace quickly apologized as she looked at him guiltily.
	"Did you know there was going to be a sub today?" Ruby whispered once the substitute teacher walked out of earshot.
	Grace shook her head as she pulled her textbook toward her. She peeled off the sticky notes she had neatly placed on one of the pages to review her notes.
	Ruby shrugged as she pulled her own book toward her as well. "I guess it doesn't really matter. But we should let Tomas and your brother know anyway."
	"AP tests are less than a month away," Grace said hopelessly, tugging at her hair as if suddenly struck by the realization. "Can you see the bags under my eyes? There's not nearly enough house in a day to study!"
	Ruby placed a reassuring hand on her friend's shoulder. "You've got this. You're doing fine, remember? On the practice test, the only person who scored higher than you in our class period was me."
	"I thought I nicely asked you girls to be quiet." The substitute teacher was back.
	Grace winced and buried her nose in her book.
	Ruby tilted her head to the side, and her shoulder-length hair swished with the movement. "We're sorry. But we're not the only ones talking. What about all of those guys at the back of the classroom?"
	The substitute teacher's frown deepened, but he turned and shuffled away to scold the boys in the back.
	Grace slipped Ruby a lavender post-it. Tye still scored better than me on the practice test, the note read.
	Only by a handful of points, Ruby scribbled back before sticking it back on her friend's book.
	Grace just sighed as she got to work reviewing the pages. Ruby turned back to her own book, tapping her chin with the end of her pencil. AP tests were coming up soon, and the anticipation was starting to set everyone on edge. But testing wasn't the only thing coming up-there was just one final push until summer. Summer was right around the corner.
	It wasn't summer vacation that Ruby was looking forward to the most; it was the end-of-year variety show that took place on the last day of school, right after finals.
	The bell rang at long last, signaling the end of the period. After quickly packing their bags, Ruby and Grace hurried out of the physics classroom to join the throng of students hoping to beat the hallway rush.
	"Do you see my brother?" Grace had to raise her voice over the chatter that was rapidly filling the hallways.
	"There!" Ruby stood on her tiptoes as she pointed into the sea of faces.
	"Ruby, Grace," Tye said in a way of greeting as he came to a stop in front of them. He had successfully made his way through the ocean of students between them. Like his sister, Tye was thin with dark skin and a quiet voice. The two of them were twins, but even though Grace was the elder sibling, Tye was at least a head taller than his sister, which made him very easy to spot in a crowd.
	"There's a sub in physics," Ruby told him loudly as the three of them set off together down the hallway.
	"What?" Tye mouthed, cupping a hand to his ear in an attempt to hear over the voices echoing off the hallway walls.
	"There's a sub-" Ruby tried again, then sighed and shook her head. "You know what, I'll tell you later."
	It was lunch, and the three of them made their way up the stairs to the third floor. At this point, the students had cleared out of the halls in their hurry to claim all the good spots outside to eat. Grace stood on her tiptoes to peer out the windows at the end of the long hallway. "Fog, again. I had hoped that by lunch it would have cleared up."
	Tye leveled his sister a look. "Fog is every season."
	"I had been hoping this would be the year I'd get to wear all those cute summer dresses. Just wait until I'm in New York. I'll be sending you pictures of the blue skies every day!"
	"New York." Tye just shook his head.
	Grace latched onto her brother's arm. "Come on, Tye. You gotta dream big."
	The three of them came to a stop in front of a classroom door, and Ruby pushed it open. The girl standing in front of the projector immediately looked up. Her eyes lit up, and a smile bloomed on her face as she waved.
	"Mari!" Ruby hurried over to her other friend.
	"Ruby!" Mari beamed. Her bleached hair was styled in its signature twin braids, topped off with a bright pink beanie. "You guys are early today. But Tomas still beat you to it."
	Ruby looked over to where a boy with dark hair and a crisp button-down shirt was already sitting at the desk next to the window, silently watching their exchange. He quickly looked away when he noticed the two of them looking at him.
	"Have a seat." Mari motioned for Ruby and the others to join the dark-haired boy at the back of the classroom. "I'm almost done setting up for the presentation. Feel free to listen. Or not." A soft ding cut through the air. Mari pulled out her phone. As she checked her messages, Ruby, Grace, and Tye walked over to sit around Tomas.
	Ruby took a seat next to Tomas, and Grace and Tye pulled up chairs to sit opposite them. "There's a sub in physics. Just thought you guys might want to know."
	"Is there a lesson plan?" Tomas asked mildly.
	Ruby shook her head. "It's just a study hall."
	"I think the sub had it out for Ruby and me," Grace said as she lowered her voice. "We were talking very quietly at the start of class, and he scolded us while completely ignoring the boys playing on their phones in the back."
	Ding! Ruby's own phone vibrated in the pocket of her shorts. Ruby pulled out her phone to find that she had been sent an image. After tapping into the text window, Ruby squinted down at the picture. It was a piece of sheet music, and the notes flying all over the staff were getting progressively lighter until they were nearly illegible. I think I'll really need glasses after this, the follow-up message read.
	Ruby let out an amused laugh before typing back, I think you just need to buy some new ink for the printer.
	"What's that?" Tomas glanced over at Ruby's phone.
	"It's Tilden." Ruby passed the phone over. "I bet he's already done with his classes for the day."
	"Well of course he is," Grace said matter-of-factly. "He's in college. And he lives in New York."
	"Tilden?" Tye looked up from the textbook he had just set on the desk in front of him. "May I see?"
	Tomas passed the phone to Tye. Tye lifted his glasses as he peered down at the message. "What's your brother up to these days, Ruby?" he asked as he looked at the image.
	"I'm not too sure," Ruby said as she rummaged through her backpack for her lunch. "He sends me pictures like these every now and then, but I think he's pretty busy himself."
	"Tilden was a cool guy," Tye remarked as he passed Ruby's phone to Grace. "It's too bad he won't be able to see us play at the variety show."
	Tomas nodded in agreement. "Will he really not come back to visit?"
	Ruby sighed. "You know what happened between him and my parents. He chose music, and ever since he left, my parents like to pretend like he doesn't exist."
	"Still?" Grace asked sadly as she set the phone down in front of Ruby. "It's been what, almost two years now?"
	It was Tomas's turn to sigh. "We were only freshmen when Tilden was a senior. I'm glad we still keep in contact. Last year, he was a big help with my AP Music Theory class."
	Tye looked up at Tomas in respect. "That's right! You took that class as a sophomore."
	"Even though my teachers said I was ready for it, I should have waited at least another year before taking it," Tomas admitted. "I know you want to take AP Theory and Composition next year, but I was so stressed out on the day of the test that my classmates said I looked like a zombie."
	"But you ended up doing great," Grace pointed out. "I still don't get why you want to take AP Music Theory"-Grace turned to look up at her brother-"you'll have less time for all those stem APs you keep saying you want to take."
	"What can I say?" A faint smile played on Tye's face. "They're fascinating. And a good challenge. And I want to get some extra college credits."
	"Look"-Tomas gestured in the direction of the desks in front of them-"everyone's here now. Mari will start her presentation soon."
	"Hello everyone!" Mari called from the front of the classroom as if on cue. "Thank you for coming to my club meeting. Today, we're going to take a look at what our school's Title IX policy has to offer, where it's still lacking, and how we can bring these issues up with the administration."
	Once Mari finished her presentation and leading the discussion that came after, she sauntered over to join Ruby, Tomas, and the twins at the back of the classroom.
	"What did you think?" Mari asked breathlessly as she pulled up a seat next to Grace. "I spent all of last night finalizing my notes."
	Tomas smiled faintly. "I thought it was very good. You presented it in a way where the information was very interesting and easy to understand too. I bet all your club members will be telling their friends about it in their afternoon classes."
	Mari laughed. "I don't know about that. I'm glad you thought it was interesting, though." Then she turned to Ruby and the twins. "What about you guys? Any thoughts?"
	"I didn't catch all of it," Ruby admitted as she gestured to the stack of textbooks in front of her. "But from what I did see, your audience was very keen on what you had to say." Grace and Tye exchanged a guilty look as they nodded along.
	Mari smiled in an attempt to ease the awkwardness. "Don't worry about it. I know you're busy studying for your tests. Feel free to keep using the club room as a place to eat lunch-it's much nicer here than the cafeteria, after all. So, uh, I think I heard something about Tilden. Did he finally send a picture of San?"

~

      "I really can't run anymore," Mari panted as she clutched a stitch in her side.
      "You've got this," Ruby encouraged her friend as she jogged beside her.
      Mari quickened her pace to keep up with Ruby. "You didn't have to do this. You've already finished your mile. You could be resting on the grass with the rest of the class."
      Ruby smiled. "You're almost done. Just one more lap. Let's give it one last push and sprint to the finish line!"
      "Alright." Mari took after Ruby, and the two of them raced along the track. When they finished, Mari staggered and collapsed onto the grass in a daze.
      "You did it!" Ruby took a seat next to her friend as the class waited for the last couple of stragglers to arrive.
      "I did it," Mari repeated as she slowly sat up. Bits of grass stuck to her hair. "Some people are just naturally sporty, and others-like me-are not. You're the only reason why I'm not failing this class completely, Ruby."
      Ruby clapped her friend on the shoulder. "You're doing fine. We've got less than a month left, and then we don't have to do PE again."
      "We're so close"-Mari shook her head tiredly as she flopped back onto the grass-"and yet still so far . . . "
      The sound of a whistle cut through the air, signaling that everyone could make their way back to the locker rooms to change. It was the last class of the day, and Ruby was already anticipating the final bell. It was also a Thursday, which meant that Tomas would be meeting them at the front gate.
      "At least we don't have PE first period," Mari lamented as she followed Ruby into the locker room. "All my energy for the rest of the day would be completely spent."
      The bell finally rang, and all the students flooded toward the doors.
      "I've got homework in all my classes again," Ruby frowned as she rummaged through her backpack while they stood off to the side of the school's front gates. "Well, I guess PE doesn't count, but it sure took too much of my energy. Kind of want a nap, but I'll probably have to settle for coffee or tea instead."
      "Tomas has lots of tea at home," Mari said distractedly as she scanned the sea of faces. "You know how Isabelle practically runs on caffeine."
      "Ha!" Ruby pointed to the gate and waved vigorously. "There he is!"
      "Are we ready to go?" Tomas asked as he joined the two of them. "Tye has after-school labs today for another half hour, so he won't be leaving campus until after four-thirty."
      Ding! Mari reached for her phone, but Tomas suddenly pointed in the direction of the school gates. "Is that Grace?"
      "Grace?" Mari paused and stood on her tiptoes to look over the slowly thinning crowd. "But doesn't she always leave through the back entrance to go to her ballet class?"
      "Ruby," Grace said breathlessly as she skidded to a stop in front of them. "Here, I forgot to return your pencil."
      Ruby blinked. "Don't you have to go to dance class? I have more pencils at home. You could have just returned it to me tonight."
      "Oh, right! All these classes are driving me crazy, I swear. I-I'll see you guys tonight!" Ruby looked on as Grace turned on her heel and took off around the block.
      "The stress is really getting to all of us." Mari sighed as the three of them began to make their way in the opposite direction. "I don't know how all of you do it. "I'm only taking two APs this year, and I'm already overwhelmed. The rest of you are taking what, four, five?"
      As they made their way to Tomas's house, the three of them made a stop at Ruby's house for her to quickly run in and retrieve her guitar. The moment Ruby opened the door, a white ball of fur zoomed over to greet her.
      "Singsing, I can't play right now." Ruby knelt down to give the puppy's head a quick pat before taking off up the stairs to her room.
      When she returned with her guitar case in hand, Ruby found the puppy sitting next to the door. Mari and Tomas had both crouched down as they took turns stroking Singsing's curly fur. Singsing let out a whine as the two of them rose to their feet.
      "Be good." Ruby knelt back down one final time to take the puppy's face in between her hands. She looked Singsing in the eyes. "Your big sister will be back later." After carefully shutting the door, Ruby and the others continued on their way to Tomas's house. The sidewalk slowly began to slant upward as they started to climb the hill.
      Even though Tomas and Ruby only lived a couple of blocks away from each other, the first time Ruby met Tomas was during their freshman year of high school. The two of them had coincidentally shared a lot of the same classes that year and quickly bonded over their shared love of music. On the other hand, Ruby had befriended Grace and Tye in middle school. The three of them had indulged in a friendly competition to see who could be the best student in the grade, which led everyone else to dub them crazy nerds. But their classmates respected them all the same. And Mari . . . Mari was Ruby's old friend from elementary school.
      "Here we are." Tomas knocked on the door to his house, and it was opened a moment later by a woman in her late forties.
      "Welcome," the woman said warmly, stepping aside to let the three of them cross the threshold.
      "Mama." Tomas smiled in a way of greeting as his mother ruffled his hair.
      "Hi, Ms. Quevedo," Mari said brightly.
      "How's everything going recently?" Ruby asked as Ms. Quevedo shut the door behind her.
      Ms. Quevedo offered Ruby a smile. "Not terrible. But not great either. Are you two staying for dinner tonight? I do enjoy cooking for all of you."
      "If you don't mind," Tomas said, looking over at his mom as he started walking to the kitchen to wash his hands. "And if you two don't mind staying," he added with a nod in Ruby and Mari's direction.
      "The twins will be here later too, I assume?" Ms. Quevedo asked as she followed her son into the kitchen.
      "Yeah!" Mari nodded enthusiastically as she and Ruby trailed after them to take their turn at the sink. "Tye should show up in half an hour or so, and you know how Grace gets here after seven because of ballet."
      When they finished washing their hands, the three of them left Ms. Quevedo in the living room and made their way down the short hallway to Tomas's bedroom.
      "Yo, Ruby, Mari," a dark-haired figure called out from one of the doors they passed on the way.
      "Hi, Isabelle." Mari gave a friendly wave as a young woman appeared in the doorway.
      "How was school today for you kids?" Isabelle asked, and her long hair tumbled all the way to her hips as she leaned against the doorframe. She held her wireless headphones in one hand and a still-steaming mug in the other. Whenever Ruby came to Tomas's house, Isabelle was always in her room. Ruby had once managed to peek inside, but she hadn't been able to see much of anything. Tomas's sister always kept the curtains drawn over the windows, and the only light inside was the dull blue glow of her computer screen. Isabelle was an art student and in the middle of doing her college courses online.
      "School's fine." Ruby looked back at her. "But 'kids,' really? You're only three years older than us."
      "Which makes me an adult." Isabelle's eyes twinkled as she smiled.
      Once inside Tomas's room, the three of them took a seat on the floor and set their backpacks down to rummage around for their homework. Studying together was the usual routine until Grace got back from ballet.
      They didn't have to wait long before Tye arrived at the house and joined them in Tomas's room. "Long time no see," Tye said jokingly.
      Mari hopped over to him. "You arrived just in time. Could you help me with our history homework?"
      "Sure." Tye took a seat on the carpeted floor and set his own backpack down.
      The wall of the neighboring house outside the window was beginning to fade as the sun slowly but steadily dropped from the sky. And as the light continued to fall, Tomas stood up to turn on the lights.
      Ruby set her books down for a moment and clasped her arms behind her back to roll out her stiff neck. She paused as she looked up at all the posters that covered the walls of Tomas's room. The faces of famous musicians stared back at her, and all of them held their musical instruments proudly.
      Of all of Ruby's friends, Tomas was the most serious about music. He played multiple instruments and was currently in both the school's zero-period orchestra as a cellist and the after-school jazz band as a saxophonist. And in their own little band, Tomas was their keyboardist and was teaching Tye how to play the bass guitar.
      There were multiple after-school jazz ensembles, and Tomas was part of the most advanced one. It met on Mondays and Wednesdays, so on those days, Ruby would head home by herself. On the other days of the week, the five of them would go to Tomas's house to practice their own song. This song was the one they were going to debut at the school's end of year variety show, which took place on the final Friday of the year.
      When six o'clock rolled around, Tomas's mother called them out for dinner. "Eat as much as you want," Ms. Quevedo said warmly. She tugged her gray-streaked hair out of its bun as she joined them at the table. "It's fun having you kids here. It makes me feel young again."
      "What are you talking about?" Ruby laughed. "You're not even close to old, Ms. Quevedo."
      Tye took a seat next to Ruby. "I hope you don't mind if I join you all at the table. Grace and I will be eating dinner at home with my parents tonight once they get back from work."
      "No worries, dear." Ms. Quevedo began dishing out food onto Ruby, Mari, and Tomas's plates. "I made extra vegetables just in case, but now there's more for the rest of us."
      Halfway through their meal, the jingling of keys sounded from outside, and the door opened a moment later to reveal a woman in an office suit.
      Tomas looked up from his food. "Mami's back."
      "Hi, Ms. Fernandez." Mari waved.
      "Hi, everyone. I had to work overtime again tonight." Ms. Fernandez shook her head as she tugged off her high heels. She winced at the angry red skin showing through her tights. "If I wasn't in a possession where I could get promoted any day now, I'd start looking for other jobs."
      Tomas slid his chair over to make room for Ms. Fernandez at the already cramped table. "You don't have to keep working there. None of us will blame you if you quit. You should report your boss. I think people would listen."
      "Don't worry," Ms. Fernandez said tiredly. "It's not like that. He didn't do anything to me today."
      "Even if he didn't do anything to you today," Mari spoke up worriedly, "that doesn't mean he didn't do anything to you all those other times! And who can say what will happen tomorrow?"
      "I'm about to get promoted." Ms. Fernandez closed her eyes for a brief moment as she pinched the bridge of her nose as if to ward off a headache. "I can't leave now."
      Ms. Quevedo frowned. "Your boss has been saying that he's about to promote you for the last few months now. Everyone else who's been working at that company has already been promoted. He just has it out for you."
      Ms. Fernandez just sighed again as she reached for the plate of vegetables.
      There was a knock on the door, and everyone looked up. Tomas rose to his feet and quickly pulled it open. Grace stood in the doorway, her hair still pulled back in a neat bun. "Hi!" she said in an excited whisper.
      "Grace!" Ruby jumped to her feet and beckoned her friend inside.
      "We just finished eating," Mari informed her. "Ready to work on our song?"
      "We'll meet you downstairs." Tomas returned to the table to pick up his plate. Ruby and Mari followed his lead and placed their own plates in the kitchen sink. Tomas turned to the two of them. "Don't worry-I can wash the dishes after you leave."
      Leaving the small kitchen, Tye joined them in the living room and handed Ruby her guitar case. Tomas pushed open the door to the basement and stood aside to let the rest of them through. Grace was already sitting behind the drum set, and Ruby got to work taking her guitar out of its case as Tomas took his place behind the keyboard. Mari picked up the guitar already patiently waiting on its stand on the far side of the room, and Tye picked up the bass guitar next to it.
      "I just finalized the harmonies." Tomas passed a piece of sheet music to Ruby. "Here's your copy. I hope they will do your lyrics justice."
      Ruby scanned the page and nodded her head.
      "Shall we try it, then?" Tye smiled, and the sound of his guitar being plugged into its amp popped in the soundproofed room.
      "We all ready?" Grace asked from the drum set. When everyone nodded, Grace raised her drumsticks. "Five, six, seven, eight!"
      
~

	"You didn't have to walk me back." Ruby looked over at Tomas as they made their way back to the base of the small hill where her house was located.
	"Isabelle would think poorly of me if I didn't," Tomas said knowingly. His quiet voice seemed louder than usual in the stillness of the night. Light spilled out of the windows they passed and illuminated their figures in a warm glow. "I worry about Mari, though. Grace and Tye get off the bus a few stops before her. She's always walking back alone in the dark."
	Ruby blinked. "Doesn't her dad pick her up from the bus stop and drive her home?"
	"No." A faint frown crossed Tomas's face. "Mari's your best friend, isn't she? I thought you would know. But anyway, after what happened to my sister all those years ago, it's better not to go anywhere alone."
	Ruby fell silent. When Isabelle was still in high school, she was walking home one night after a club meeting when two men jumped her just a block away from home. They had stolen her backpack and even ripped off the plastic jewelry she was wearing that day. Isabelle had been completely shaken by the experience, and ever since that day, Ruby had never seen her wear any sort of jewelry again.
	Ruby turned to look at Tomas as the two of them stopped in front of the door to her house. "I'll see you tomorrow, then."
	Tomas raised a hand in farewell. Ruby set her guitar case down to rummage through her backpack for her keys. After pushing the door open, Ruby stepped inside and gave one final wave to Tomas.
	"Ruby," a voice called from the dining room. Ruby froze and turned to find her parents sitting at the table. The two of them seemed to have just finished their dinner. Her dad was rarely at home, so to find him here tonight was a surprise.
	"Ba, Ma." Ruby slid off her flip-flops and set her guitar case on the floor next to the door before walking over to greet them.
	"Each night you're getting home later and later." Ruby's mom looked up at her daughter. "Are you sure you're studying? Are they feeding you well there?"
	"Yes, Ma." Ruby sighed as she slid into one of the empty seats across from her parents. There were four chairs at their rectangular table, and the one next to Ruby had remained unoccupied ever since her brother left.
	"Your other friends were there too, is that right?" Ruby's dad looked over at her, and a crease formed between his brows. "I don't know how to feel about you staying so late at a boy's house all by yourself."
	"Tomas?" Ruby leaned back in her chair and folded her arms across her chest. "He's my friend."
	"Right. Friend." Ruby's dad continued to frown, unconvinced. Then his eyes fell on the guitar case still lying next to the front door.
	"I have more studying to do." Ruby quickly rose from her seat. "I'll go head up to my room."
	Ruby slipped out of the dining room and quietly entered the living room to find Singsing asleep on the couch. The puppy was a furry white ball of warmth. Ruby let out a soft sigh as she retrieved her guitar case and walked it up the stairs to her room.
      When she reached the landing, she paused momentarily next to the closed door that was her brother's room. Even though she hadn't been inside since her brother left, she had secretly seen her mom go in a number of times. When Ruby occasionally peeked inside, the room was always tidy and dust-free.
      Ruby continued on her way to her own room and kicked the door open with a foot. The room was dark, and the light streaming in from the window was the only source of light. Ruby stood there in the darkness for a long moment.
	Even though they didn't say it, her parents weren't thrilled about her musical hobbies. When she was younger, they had paid for both her and her brother's music lessons. But ever since Tilden declared that he wanted to pursue a career in music . . . There was no saying when Tilden would come back-if he would ever come back.
	After changing out of her jean shorts and t-shirt, Ruby made quick work of pulling on her pajamas before crawling into bed. There was a lot to think about right now. AP tests were coming up. The end of the year was also coming up. But most importantly, the auditions for the variety show were coming up the following Monday, and Ruby couldn't wait. It was going to be the first time she and her friends would get to play together on an actual stage.
	Ruby rolled over in her bed and hugged one of her stuffed animals to her chest. She smiled into its fur. Then coughing from the dust that had settled into the fibers, Ruby rolled back around to set her alarm clock.
	Sometime in the middle of the night, Ruby was woken by the sound of footsteps climbing the stairs. The footsteps made their way down the hall and hesitated outside her room for a moment. Ruby cracked an eye open to watch her dad quietly walk over the window at the back of her room and draw the blinds over it.
	When her dad left the room, Ruby found a faint smile playing on her lips. And then snuggling under the covers, Ruby let sleep wash over her once again.

    Chapter 1.5

SYSTEM: MariMariMari!! is now online.

Tomas Quevedo: Hi Mari. Can't sleep?

MariMariMari!!: No

MariMariMari!!: Well... yes. Maybe??

MariMariMari!!: Hi Tomas.

Tomas Quevedo: Are you sleeping with your phone on the nightstand next to you again?

MariMariMari!!: Yeah... probably not my best idea. Tomorrow I'll lock it away downstairs!

MariMariMari!!: Oh, what are you doing up so late, by the way?

Tomas Quevedo: I was suddenly struck with inspiration for a new song, and I had to quickly go and note it down. You should try and get some sleep.

MariMariMari!!: I know I should probably try and go back to sleep, but I think I'm just better off staying up the whole night now. I'm not sure if I can go back to sleep now.

Tomas Quevedo: Is everything alright?

MariMariMari!!: Of course!

MariMariMari!!: Thanks for thinking about me. Really. But I'm fine.

    Chapter 2

	Grace sat in class with her hands clasped together under the desk. She could feel the gaze of the boy sitting next to her, but she stared straight ahead, keeping her eyes glued to her teacher standing at the front of the classroom.
	"Grace." Everett leaned forward. "Grace."
	Grace instinctively flinched and leaned away.
	"Why are you ignoring me, Grace?" Everett was so close now that Grace could feel his breath on the side of her face. "I need a pencil today too."
	"I don't have pencils anymore," Grace said as she stiffened. "You took the last of my extra ones, and unless you return them, I don't have any more to give out. Please, I'm trying to listen to Ms. Bryn."
	"What about the one you're using right now?"
	"What-? This one is mine!"
	"Grace, Everett." Ms. Bryn frowned as she paused her lecture. "What's going on? Is there a problem?"
	Grace fell silent, and her mind whirled as she debated what she should say. But before she could think of anything, Everett pointed an accusing finger at her. "I only wanted to borrow a pencil, but she won't give me one!"
	"I've already told you," Grace said, her voice a breathy whisper, "I don't have any spares!"
	"You could have just asked me, you know," Ms. Bryn said in exasperation. "Here, Everett. I hope the two of you can keep the talking to a minimum as I finish this lesson."
	Grace nodded her head as she clenched her hands together. She closed her eyes for a brief moment to center herself. She lacked confidence, as she was told time and time again by her brother. Ruby had told her too that she needed to stand up for herself. But when it came to arguing with people, Grace always felt as if she was too soft-spoken to get her point across.
	She was a dancer. A ballerina. Dancers didn't need to use words to express themselves. But here at school, she wasn't a dancer. Instead she was a fish out of water. But even at the dance studio . . . The studio was a place she had spent so many years of her life. It was perfect. And that was why she kept returning to it. If only she could muster the confidence to ask her teacher if, just once, she could dance one of the bigger roles. Grace was sure she could fill the role if given the chance. But so far, that chance was not something she had been offered yet.
	Grace knew that she would have to ask for it herself. Maybe her teacher would say yes and allow Grace to audition. Or maybe she would say no and say that Grace wasn't ready. Or maybe she'd just laugh and ask why Grace even wanted it in the first place-say that she was asking for too much.
	All of those reactions had happened in the past, and after the latter, Grace wasn't sure if she even could convey her wishes to her teacher again. Tye repeatedly told Grace that while ballet itself wasn't hurting her, her teachers were messing with her head. But each time, Grace vigorously shook her head. She had to keep dancing. It was what she loved most of all . . . right? After high school, she would go to New York to study dance and become a professional dancer. That had been her dream ever since she was a little girl.
	Grace sighed softly as she copied down the important points her teacher had drawn a box around on the whiteboard. When it came to talking to people outside her friend group, she never knew what she should say and how they would react. For a period of time, Tye had the same issue when it came to speaking, but recently he had gotten quite good at reading people's faces and body language. Grace, on the other hand, would rather stare at her own feet instead of looking up long enough to meet someone's eye.
	On stage, though, she was different. On stage, she didn't have to be Grace anymore. On stage, she was able to melt into the characters she was portraying and lose herself in the dancing.
	The bell rang, drawing Grace back to reality as she quickly packed away her books and binders. She hurried out of the classroom in the hopes that she could beat the hallway rush.
	"Hey!" a voice called from behind her. Grace's head snapped up as she looked over her shoulder to see Everett walking toward her.
	Grace quickened her pace and scurried away from him. Oh no, what does he want now?
	After ducking into the crowd of students spilling out of the doors lining the hallway, Grace let the crowd carry her to her next class. Everett was quickly lost in the waves.

	"What's wrong?" Ruby asked as Grace took a seat next to her in their physics class. Her friend could instantly sense that something was off. "Did Everett bother you again?"
	"Not really." Grace shook her head tiredly as she set her textbooks down on the desk. "He made us attract the teacher's attention, that's all."
	"Isn't that a good thing? That way you can tell the teacher what the situation is."
	Grace shook her head again.
	"I can go find Everett for you," Ruby offered. "I can tell him off."
	Grace gave Ruby a weak smile. "I appreciate the offer, but let's not give him any more reasons to cause me trouble."
	The class period seemed to drag by and fly past all at the same time. Before Grace knew it, the lunch bell rang, and the two of them were filing into the hallway to meet up with Tye.
	"I've been meaning to ask for a while," was the first thing Tye said when he reached them in the middle of the crowded hallway, "Ruby, how do you survive wearing flip-flops all day? I've never seen you in any other kind of shoes. I decided to wear flip-flops to school for the first time today, and I already need two hands to count the number of times my feet have been stepped on."
	"It's an art form," Ruby said knowingly. "What made you decide to wear flip-flops?"
	"There's supposed to be clear skies later today," Tye informed them as they made their way toward Mari's clubroom. "We'll find out soon whether the weather forecast was right or not."
	The three of them arrived at Mari's clubroom and joined Tomas at the back of the room.
	"I saw your exchange with Mari on the group chat yesterday." Tye lowered his voice. "Do you think everything is alright with Mari?"
	Tomas's brows were furrowed. "She claimed that everything was fine, but something tells me otherwise. I'm planning to ask her again once she finishes with her group discussion today."
	"Did something happen to Mari?" Grace blinked as she pulled out her own phone. She had disabled notifications for the sake of getting a good night's sleep and hadn't checked her messages yet.
	Ruby pulled her phone out as well and was now scrolling through the previous night's conversation. "It looks like Mari's stressed out again."
	"Is someone talking about me?" Mari joined them at the back of the classroom. She placed her hands on the back of Ruby's chair to lean over and look at her friends in turn.
	Ruby twisted around to look up at her friend. "Is everything alright, Mari?"
	"What?" Mari blinked before she broke out into a smile. "Of course!"
	"See?" Ruby turned to Tomas with a smile. "You don't have to worry."
	"Are you guys going to join the discussion today?" Mari asked as she twirled one of her bleached braids between her fingers.
	"Sorry, Mari," Grace said regretfully. "I've still got homework to finish."
	"No worries," Mari reassured her. "What about the rest of you?"
	Tomas rose from his seat. "I can join."
	Mari clapped her hands together. "Sweet!"
	Ruby sighed. "I've got work."
	"Me too." Tye offered Mari an apologetic smile.
	Mari smiled. "No worries. I'll leave you to your work, then." She turned and made her way back to the front of the classroom with Tomas.
	"Look!" Grace jumped to her feet and excitedly hurried over to the window. The fog had begun to clear, and the blue of the sky was showing through the gray.
	"Yes!" Ruby cheered as she joined Grace at the window. "I knew that if I kept wearing shorts and flip-flops, the sky would eventually show up!"
	"I don't know how you do it," Tye said, and Grace turned to find him shaking his head. "Even in the winter, you're still in shorts."
      Grace laughed. "Ruby's immune to the cold."
      Tye leveled his sister a look. "You're always wearing those summer dresses of yours all year round."
      Grace looked down at her lavender dress. "They're easy to change out of. And they're cute."
      Ruby turned away from the window. "Let's hope the sun stays out long enough that we can see it again when school lets out. Oh," she added as an afterthought, "whose name did we sign up for the audition under? Was it yours or Tye's?"
      "It was mine," Tye answered. "They're going alphabetically by last name, so we'll be toward the beginning."
      "It must be nice to have a last name starting with B," Ruby lamented as she flipped open her textbook. "I'm always last if we go by last name, and still almost at the end if we go by first name."
      Grace smiled faintly. "It makes you special." Ruby was special. Grace wasn't sure what she would have done if she hadn't met Ruby in middle school. While Tye had always been there, for the longest time, he was just as introverted as Grace was. It was only in the most recent years that Tye had forced himself out of his comfort zone. During their freshman year, he signed up for the school's debate team and had become a lot better at speaking.
      This group was kept together by Ruby and had been brought together by Ruby. Grace, Tye, Tomas, and Mari were all introverts drawn to and now hovering around Ruby like moths to a glowing lamp.
      The audition was coming up on Monday, and Grace was beginning to feel that pre-performance giddiness. At the end of the school day, Grace was out the door as soon as the final bell sounded. Her ballet studio was a twenty-minute walk away from the high school, and if she didn't dawdle, she'd have a good ten minutes to change into her leotard, tights, and stretch before pulling on her pointe shoes. This would be Grace's fifth year on pointe.
      Ever since she had started ballet, she had envied the girls who got to twirl on the tips of their toes. They were effortless and beautiful like swans and fairies. Once she had gotten older herself, that illusion had been quickly broken when she bought her first pair of pointe shoes.
      Even though Grace didn't mind the discomfort as much as when she first started, the blisters and sores that came with the shoes were always present. Grace had gone through her fair share of broken nails as well, and nothing anyone could say would convince her to wear open-toed shoes in public.
      Grace reached the dance studio and paused outside the doors to look at the sky reflected in the tinted glass. Then after taking a deep breath, Grace pushed the door open. She made quick work of signing in before walking briskly to the dressing room in the back.
      "Grace!" Her classmates were already in the dressing room, and they looked up as she walked in.
      "Hi." Grace offered them a small smile before setting her bag down in the corner of the room. After sliding off her shoes, she pulled her tights on under her summer dress. The dress acted as a makeshift curtain and offered her a small amount of privacy.
      She pulled on her leotard and finally stepped out of her dress. Grace moved to the mirrors next. She brushed her poofy hair back and shaped it into a neat bun. After sticking in a number of bun pins and finishing it off with her hairnet, Grace joined her classmates on the floor as they taped their toes in preparation for class.
      "How was school today?" Grace asked her classmates in the hope to make small talk.
      "I'm sorry?" One of them blinked as she looked over at Grace. "Did you say something?"
      "How was school?" Grace asked again, but she could feel her confidence dwindling.
      "Fine." The girl offered Grace a polite smile before turning back to her shoes.
      Grace let out a soft sigh. Maybe today would be the day when she would ask her instructor about auditioning for a leading role in their next production.
      When the clock struck four-thirty, Grace and the others made their way into the studio and took their respective places at the bars that lined the room. They didn't have to wait long before their instructor stepped into the room.
      "Good afternoon." Ms. Beaufort looked at each of her students in turn. "You know the routine."
      That familiar music sounded through the room and Grace let her muscle memory guide her through the movements she had done hundreds of times before.

	When the class ended, the sun had dropped from the sky outside. The city lights replaced it as they blazed against the dark, forever keeping the night and stars at bay. Grace found herself lingering outside the door to the studio. She paced back and forth. Once, twice, three times. But her nerves got the best of her, and she scurried into the dressing room. So much for asking Ms. Beaufort about auditions.
	After Grace changed back into her dress, she left the building and glanced down at her phone. The screen flickered to life, and the light spilled over her as she squinted at the time. One of her classmates stepped outside to join her a few minutes later. The two of them went in the same direction and normally ended up walking together in silence.
      Walking to Tomas's house from the dance studio took a little over thirty minutes, and Grace picked up her pace. She was already tired from dancing, but she was excited to work on their song. Grace hurried along the streets brightly illuminated by the rows of streetlights. Her classmate was absorbed in her own phone, and the light from the screen gave her eyes a glazed appearance. 	"Ruby!" Grace said excitedly.

	"I can stay longer too." Mari looked up from where she was scrolling through her phone on the living room couch. "My dad says he can pick me up directly from here as well."
	"Hey." Tye walked up to Grace and extended his fist to her. Grace met it with her own as her brother offered her a smile.
	In the basement, Grace took a seat behind the drum set as her friends got to work setting up their instruments. Grace absently ran her hand over the smooth wood of the drumsticks. She had been in middle school when she started learning how to play the drums. When she mentioned to people that she played the drums, their reactions would always be that of surprise. Grace understood where they were coming from-Tye had told her many times before that she came off as shy to people. Being loud or taking center stage just wasn't something they could imagine her doing. But that was just because they didn't know her.
	Drum lessons had been very fun, and Grace took them all through middle school. But once she had gotten to high school, ballet once again had become more demanding with its hours. Drum lessons weren't the only thing Grace had given up in the past. She had also given up her position on her middle school's soccer team. Dance was her life. She needed to stay devoted to it. Only in that way could she become the professional dancer she had always dreamed to be.
	She let out a breath. Summer would be here soon. There was just one final push left until summer. She could do this.
	"Ready?" Ruby turned to look over her shoulder from where she was standing at the front of their setup. The music started, and Ruby's voice filled the room. Mari's followed next in perfect harmony. When the song ended, Ruby walked around to each of them and gave them a high five. "We're ready for the audition on Monday," Ruby declared confidently. "Do we just want to run it again?"
	"Sure." Tomas nodded from his keyboard. "If we want an audience, we could try and drag my sister out of her room."
	Ruby laughed. "Let's let Isabelle study in peace. If anything, we could ask your moms instead."
	Before Grace knew it, it was already nine o'clock, and the five of them returned to Tomas's bedroom to wait for Mari's dad to arrive.
	"Watch your back!" Mari called. She was staring intently at the screen of her laptop, and her fingers flew over the keys. "The boss teleported again!"
	"I see it now!" Tomas called back. "I'll use a freezing spell to try and keep it in place."
	"You should use a wind and fire combo." Ruby leaned over as she watched Tomas's screen. Grace and Tye were sitting on either side of Mari. "That should temporarily slow its movements."
	"Yeah." Mari nodded along as her eyes narrowed in concentration. "Once it's slowed, I can trap it in the magic wind net."
	"You should join us sometime, Ruby," Tomas said without taking his eyes off his screen. "You and Mari both used to be pretty well known on the server."
	Ruby laughed. "That was years ago."
	"But you still know the strategies."
	"And the boss is down!" Mari cheered. "You can pick up the gear and crystals it drops. We can sell them later at the marketplace for a good price."
	Suddenly, the sound of the doorbell ringing floated into the room from down the hall. Mari quickly shut her laptop and tucked it back into her backpack. Now that it was time for Mari to go, Grace and Tomas would head out as well to catch their bus.
	Tomas shut his own laptop. "I can sell them at the marketplace later. Try and get some sleep tonight."
	After Grace and Tye collected their belongings, they walked with Ruby, Mari, and Tomas to the front door. Mari gave one final wave before she hurried outside to follow her dad to his car. Grace and Tye said their goodbyes to Ruby and Tomas before they started their trek up the hill to the bus stop. Ruby and Tomas went in the opposite direction.
	Tye glanced up at the sky. "Looks like the fog's back."
	When they reached the bus stop, Grace took a seat on the bench and pulled one of her binders from her backpack.
	Tye looked over at her. "If you need help, just let me know and I can see what I can do."
	Grace nodded as she turned back to her work. Out of the corner of her vision, the glow of a phone screen flickered to life as Tye scrolled through unread messages. Ten minutes later, the bus arrived. It was almost completely empty when Grace and Tye climbed into it, and the two of them walked to the middle of the bus before taking their seats.
	As the buildings outside the windows became a blur of light, Grace continued to work on her homework. "Do you know what's for dinner?" she asked after a while, finally looking up to give her straining eyes a break.
	"Dad and Mom said that they were going to get takeout for us tonight from some vegan place close to campus," Tye informed her. Grace nodded her head. Their parents were both professors at the university on the other side of the bay. In fact, they had first met on campus as new teachers and were still teaching there to this day.
	It was ten o'clock when the two of them finally arrived at their apartment. Their parents still weren't home, and Grace flopped onto the couch to do more of her homework while Tye set the table.
	"Having trouble?" Tye looked over at Grace and took note of the grimace on her face.
	"No." Grace exhaled through her nose. "This is just busy work. Why do they give us so much homework anyway?"
	"They want us to suffer, obviously."
	"Of course, of course. I forgot about that part."
	There was the sound of jingling keys from outside the apartment door. The twin's parents stepped inside, and the light from the hallway outlined their figures in a soft glow.
	"You're back!" Grace exclaimed excitedly. She set her homework down and rushed over to greet her parents.
	"How was school?" Grace's mom asked as she embraced her daughter. "How was the music at Tomas's house?"
	"We're auditioning next Monday," Grace explained as she followed her mom into the kitchen. She waited for her to wash her hands before continuing. "The auditions are during lunch, so they won't conflict with dance."
	"How's dance going?" Grace's dad placed a plastic bag on the kitchen counter, opened it, and took out a series of to-go boxes.
	"Dance is going fine," Grace said distractedly as her stomach let out a rumble at the food. It had been many hours since she had last eaten something.
	"Let's take these to the table." Tye joined them in the kitchen. Nodding, Grace helped her brother move the boxes to the table. When they finished, they took a seat around the table with their parents, and the city lights glowed outside their window as they ate.

	Grace held her breath as she entered her first-period classroom and she tiptoed over to her seat. She quietly sat down with one eye on the empty seat next to her and the other on the door. Was it too much to hope that Everett wouldn't show up today?
	When the bell rang, signaling the start of class, there was still no sign of Everett. Grace exhaled and set her textbooks on the table in front of her. She still had the audition for the variety show later with the rest of her friends. Maybe this was a sign of good luck-a sign of a lucky day.
	Lunch finally rolled around. After meeting up with Tye in the hallway, instead of making their way to the club room, they made their way to the school's auditorium. Ruby had brought her own guitar for the occasion and carefully held her case in an attempt to keep it from hitting the people walking next to them in the hallway. When Tye signed them up, he had made sure to request a set of drums and a keyboard from the school's band room. Tomas was going to bring the bass guitar to the school.
      Tomas and Mari were already waiting for them in the seats in front of the stage, and the latter waved them over the moment they walked through the doors.
      "How are we feeling right now?" Ruby asked as she took her guitar out of her case to check if her strings were still in tune.
      "Nervous." Mari tugged on one of her twin braids. "But also excited."

      "Turns out we're going to be the second group on stage today," Tomas informed them. "The first group is going to be a dance number."
      The five of them sat down in the chairs in front of the stage. The other students waiting for their turns slowly filled in the rest of the front row and then scattered through the rows behind them. The teachers who were going to act as the judges filed into the auditorium shortly after, and then the auditions started.
      When the group of freshman girls going before them finished their dance to a popular Korean song, Grace applauded them with the rest of the small crowd. And once they exited the stage, Ruby rose to her feet and led Grace and the others up the steps.
      The drumset was already on the stage, and Grace took her place behind it as her friends set up their instruments. Looking out at the faces of her classmates sitting in the audience, Grace could feel that giddy excitement that came along with the thrill of performing. Even if their audience was small, this was going to be their first time playing on an actual stage together.
      "Ready?" Ruby looked over her shoulder from where she stood in the middle of the stage.
      Grace nodded as she looked from Tomas, to Mari, to Tye, and the three of them nodded as well. Grace took a deep breath as she smiled out at the audience. "Five, six, seven, eight!"

    Chapter 3

	Tye leaned back in his chair. He lifted his head to look out the line of windows next to his desk. The fog in the air outside was as prominent as ever. After taking off his glasses, Tye rubbed his eyes. Some things in life were just as predictable as the fog. His tiredness, for example, and how it never went away, as well as the fact that he couldn't rely on caffeine to keep it at bay.
	Tye put his glasses back on, then turned back to the textbook in front of him. He squinted down at the text and frowned as the words blurred. Tye blinked, once, twice. The words cleared up and melted back into a series of now legible letters.
	Turning his gaze to the page of notes he had been taking, Tye absently looked at his handwriting. The words were starting to blur together too.
	When the bell finally rang, Tye packed up his books and let the flood of students spilling into the hallway carry him to his next class. Tye frowned as the faces of the students in front of him blurred in and out of focus. He couldn't go on like this. But school had taken over his life yet again.
	It had finally struck Tye a matter of months ago that he had almost no interests outside of school itself. He had no hobbies-nothing to do for himself. Grace had dance, but Tye? The only time he wasn't focused on schoolwork was when he got to play the bass guitar for a good forty-five minutes. Playing the bass guitar was the one thing he really looked forward to. It was something different-a splash of vibrant color to the rest of his monochrome life. Each day was classes and deadlines, homework and stress. The same old routine.
	School was something Tye excelled at. But he was starting to wonder, at what cost? He wasn't unhappy . . . but he wasn't exactly happy either. He was trying to prove himself, Tye had concluded when he first gave it some amount of thought. But prove himself to who? His parents? His family? Himself?
	Tye sat down in his next class and set his backpack down under his desk. He took out his textbooks. The backpack was always a constant weight on his back even when he wasn't wearing it. Everything he needed was inside it. His books, his binders, his notes, the keys to his future. And yet even though he brought it everywhere with him, it was weighing him down.
	"Hey." Tye's deskmate greeted him as he sat down.
      "Hey," Tye acknowledged him with a nod in his direction. All of Tye's classmates were essentially like himself. Stressed and tired, that was.
      AP tests were only days away, and something told Tye that he wasn't going to get any sleep this week. The sleep itself was a problem. Even when Tye finished all of his homework, he still found himself too worried to sleep.
      During each test he took, he always aimed for the highest grade and the best scores possible. While Grace had told him time and time again that he was being unrealistic in thinking every single thing he did had to be perfect, it was a constant problem Tye was still trying to come to terms with. Grace was right. It was unrealistic. But Tye always found himself unconsciously striving toward it anyway.
      "Tye." Tye's deskmate nudged him in the shoulder. "How do I answer this question?"
      "Let me see." Tye set his own work aside to take a look at his classmate's. It was interesting how they always assumed that he knew the answer.
      Sometimes Tye wondered what would happen to him once he graduated high school. Once he graduated college. Schoolwork was all he knew how to do. It was all he had ever known.
      "Have you read the page in the textbook?" Tye looked down at the question. "There's a formula toward the bottom of the page. I know, they were sneaky this time. It was hidden pretty well."
      "Thanks, man. Appreciate it."
      When the bell for lunch rang, Tye met up with Ruby and Grace in the hallway, and the three of them walked together to Mari's club room. When they arrived, Mari hurried up to greet them. "Do you know if we made it in?" Mari asked hopefully. "Have they mailed you the results yet?"
      "I don't think they would have mailed it out that quickly." Tye pulled out his phone to check his mail anyway. He had checked in the morning and even went as far as glancing at it every couple of minutes on the way to school. That was until he remembered that the auditions themself were going to run through Wednesday to accommodate everyone who wanted a shot at it. "Nope, still nothing."
      "Figures." Mari sighed. She stepped aside to let the three of them move to the back of the room where Tomas was already sitting at one of the desks.
      "AP tests start on Wednesday," Tomas said in a way of greeting as the three of them took their seats. Something about his quiet voice made the statement sound something more like a death sentence. "Everyone ready?"
      "This is what we've been working the entire year towards." Grace stared down at the table in front of her and clasped her hands together on top of its smooth surface.
      Ruby nodded. "That's right. We worked hard, and we're going to keep working hard. We'll do just fine."
      "I don't know if you're the type who will really settle for 'just fine,'" Tye said knowingly as he sat down as well.
      "And are you?" Ruby's inky hair whispered over her bare shoulders as she looked over at him. She was wearing a tank top and shorts, and the fog outside the windows behind her made the outfit look very out of place. "But what am I even saying? Of course you're going to do fine. You're going to get fives on everything. I already know it."
      Tye just gave her an exasperated look before taking off his glasses to rub his eyes for at least the fifth time already.
      "Don't pressure him," Grace said with a sigh. "We're all going to try our best. What happens will happen, and then we have the end-of-year variety show to look forward to. We're getting in. All the teachers looked like they were enjoying our performance." Then Grace turned to look up at where Mari was setting up her presentation for the day. "I'm surprised Mari's still doing stuff for the club. She's still got AP tests to study for herself."
      "I think most of her members are freshmen," Ruby pointed out. "Upperclassmen tend to be too busy to attend a club that happens every day. You can also see that she gets different members on different days."
      Tomas looked over at Mari. "I think it's great that she has so many people interested in what she has to say."
      "Of course." Ruby nodded along. "We should study. Time's already slipping away from us."
      Nodding, Tye blinked the tiredness from his eyes as he returned to the lines of text and equations covering the pages in front of him.
