	"Tye," Grace said worriedly, "are you sure you're okay?"
	Tye blinked, and his room blurred as he looked around. As he squinted in the direction of Grace's voice. Tye blinked again and quickly found his glasses laying on the surface of his desk in front of him. He put them on and stared at the book he had been using as a pillow. Had he fallen asleep?
	That was right-since AP tests were starting this week, they had decided that it would be better to go home and study instead of heading to Tomas's house. Tye grimaced at the stack of textbooks on the desk in front of him. When had he fallen asleep? How long had he been sleeping?
	"Dad and Mom got home early tonight." Grace stepped into the room and bent over to pick up a notebook that had slid onto the floor. "It's time for dinner."
	Tye turned to look out the window. It was already dark outside, and the lights of the city were shining behind the reflection of his face in the glass. Food would help. Hopefully. So Tye rose from his seat and followed Grace to the dining room table.

~

	"It's three in the morning." Grace pushed open the door to Tye's room. "Even Dad and Mom have already gone to sleep."
	"What are you still doing awake?" Tye asked without looking up from the notes he was pouring over. The lights in his room were still on, and the brightness was starting to give him a headache.
	Grace placed her hands on her hips. "You need to sleep. What happens if you're so tired to the point that you can't go to school tomorrow? What happens if you're so tired you fall down a flight of stairs and hurt yourself?"
	Tye shook his head in amusement. "I'm not going to hurt myself."
	Grace frowned. "You won't even be able to take the AP tests if you're laying there in a hospital bed."
	Tye paused at that and quietly set his notebook down. "What are you doing awake this late anyway?"
	"I was worried about you. Next year, don't take so many AP classes. Just take what's appealing to you."
	"But-"
	"Can't you see what it's doing to your health? Is it worth it?"
	"What about you, though?" Tye asked tiredly. "You're taking almost as many AP classes yourself."
	"I might be taking the classes"-Grace walked over to lean against the windowsill-"but I'm not focusing on getting the best possible grades and test scores. I know that you're a perfectionist, and I am too. But some things are just not worth risking your health for. Just do your best. No matter how badly you do, you will pass."
	"It's true that it's very difficult to get a five on every single test." Tye closed his eyes for a brief moment. He opened them again as his tiredness crashed into him.
	"Exactly!" Grace nodded her head. "You need to set your sights a little lower for your own sake. Besides, getting a four on the tests is all you really need."
	Tye let out a sigh, and a silence fell in the room between them. "I should go to sleep," he finally said as he rose to his feet. His legs were stiff, and his neck was even stiffer.
	"Yes, you should."
	After taking off his glasses, Tye walked over to his bed. Grace turned out the lights before stepping out of the room and gently closed the door behind her.
      Tye was asleep the moment his head hit the pillow, and the tests plagued his dreams as he tossed and turned uneasily until morning.

~

	The day he had been waiting for all year had finally arrived. It was the first day of AP testing.
      Tye and Ruby stood next to each other as they waited outside the doors to the school's gym. The testing was going to take place inside.
	"Relax." Ruby clapped Tye on the shoulder. "We're going to get this over with, and then before you know it, you'll be walking out of those doors with a proud smile on your face."
      Tye continued to eye the doors, even though Ruby's reassuring touch and the familiar scent of her mint chapstick had already started to calm his nerves. "That would be the best-case scenario."
	"Come on." Ruby was smiling, but she too seemed giddier than usual. "You've got this, and you know it." The doors to the gym opened, and the students in the testing slot before them filed out. "Here we go." Ruby inhaled sharply as her own nervousness surfaced. "Best of luck."
	Tye nodded, suddenly feeling more confident than he had moments ago. "You too."

~

	A week had passed, and Tye had just finished the last of his AP tests. Everything went by so quickly that he barely even had time to process how many days passed.
	"It's over!" Mari cheered as Tye, Ruby, and Tomas followed along behind her. "I think this calls for a celebration."
	Tye sighed. "Now we just have to wait for our scores."
	"Don't think about that right now," Ruby said. "It's over for the time being."
	"I know it's done." Tye lifted his glasses to pinch the bridge of his nose. "But I just can't stop thinking about what I did wrong and what I could have done better. I think it's going to take me a few days to really accept that it's over. It's just something I worked so hard for all year, and now that it's over, I don't really know what to do with myself."
      "There's still finals." Mari's smile faded as she slowed her pace to let the others catch up. "Studying isn't over just yet."
      When they reached Tomas's house, the four of them found to their pleasant surprise that Ms. Quevedo had made juice popsicles for them to celebrate.
      "It was Isabelle's idea," Ms. Quevedo explained as she passed them out. "Remember to thank your sister later."
      While it was still slightly too cold and foggy outside for popsicles, the four of them enjoyed them nonetheless. When they were done, the five of them made their way to Tomas's room. There, Mari and Tomas sat down on either side of Tye in an attempt to teach him how to play their favorite computer game.
      "There's a reason why I don't play video games." Tye shook his head as his in-game character died again to a low-level monster. But he was smiling. This was a well needed distraction.
      "I just got a text from my brother," Ruby said suddenly.
      "Tilden?" Tye leaned over as Ruby held out her phone to show him.
      Ruby grinned. "He's congratulating us on finishing our testing."
      Congrats on testing! Tilden's message read. And as Tye looked on, a new message popped up to follow it. I just so happen to have the day off, so I just came back from a walk around the city with San.
      Mari looked over at the message before taking the phone from Ruby and typed back, Who is San???!!!!
      Looks like San is calling me, Tilden's response came almost immediately. Got to go! Have a lovely evening!
      Mari handed the phone back to Ruby. "He's so irritating sometimes. How long has it been now since he's met San? It's been at least a year now, and he refuses to share any pictures."
      Ruby frowned as she scrolled through her messages. "All we know is that San's a friend of his."
      "Friend?" Tye gave Ruby a knowing look. "He's obviously obsessed."
      Mari turned to Tye. "You also think San is his girlfriend? Boyfriend? Theyfriend?"
      "Tilden's having a lot of fun keeping us in the dark," Tomas remarked. "He's not going to reveal who San is any time soon."
      Mari let out a sigh. "You can't blame me for being at least a little curious about who exactly is keeping him from contacting us as much as he used to. Whoever San is, the two of them are probably an adorable couple."
      Tye nodded along in agreement. During their freshman year, Tilden had practically been like an older brother to all of them. He had been the one who suggested that Tye try out the bass guitar. He had been the one who initially started teaching him, but when he got bogged down with schoolwork, Tomas took over.
      During the first year after he had left, Tilden had still kept in touch with them and made sure to send pictures of his new life in New York to their group chat. When Tilden was accepted into his dream music school, he had excitedly gone to his parents with the news. Except the reaction Tilden had been met with was far from the one he had hoped for. Tye still didn't know all of the details of the event. Tilden didn't talk about it, and Ruby tried to avoid the topic as much as possible.
      Toward the end of Tilden's first year at college, he met San. Tye was happy that Tilden had found someone to keep him company on the east coast, and now whenever Tilden would mention San (which he did a lot), all of them would playfully bombard him with questions about San's mysterious identity.
      "Enough about my brother." Ruby set her phone down as she turned back to Tye. "Let's see if you can get past the boss this time."
      "I've already tried twice before." Tye sighed as he resurrected his in-game character. "Bold of you to assume that I'll be able to clear the dungeon this time."
      Mari grinned. "Third time's a charm. Come on, Tomas and I will walk you through it."
      "Alright." Tye focused on the screen in front of him. "I'm starting to think I should have gone with a magic-wielding class instead."
      "I used to play a non-magic class," Ruby pointed out as she leaned in to watch Tye's screen over Tomas's shoulder. "For some period of time there, I was one of the top players on the server. Mari and I had worked our way to the top, and even though it only lasted for a couple of months, we were quite formable opponents, if I do say so myself."
      "We were a great team," Mari said wistfully. "You should join me again one day, Ruby."
      Ruby laughed. "Maybe one day."
      After an hour of struggle and frustration, Tye had successfully cleared the dungeon by himself. There was something very satisfying about the way the boss vanished in a puff of smoke and left a loot chest in its wake.
      "Open it!" Mari urged, and Tye clicked the chest. A big number six flashed across the screen as his character leveled up.
      "And what level are you, Mari?" Tye asked as he collected everything in the chest.
      "Ninety-nine," Mari said distractedly.
      "That's the max level." Tye let out a sigh. "I'm not even surprised. What level are you, Tomas? I remember you only started about two years back."
      "I just reached ninety-five a few weeks ago," Tomas recalled. "Leveling gets exponentially more difficult the further you go along. And if you want to play a different class, you'll have to level it from the beginning all over again."
      "It looks like I'm sticking with the blade master, then." Tye checked the stats of the new gear he had just gained from the loot chest, not quite sure what any of the stars and bars in the description meant.
      "Hello." Grace appeared in the doorway.
      "Grace!" Mari jumped to her feet to wave Grace over. "We were just showing your brother how to clear the level five dungeon. Would you like to have a go?"
      Grace offered Mari a tired smile. "I think I'll have to pass. Ms. Quevedo is calling all of you for dinner."
      The five of them made their way out of Tomas's room and crowded around the dinner table. Ms. Fernandez arrived right after they had sat down, and Ms. Quevedo jumped up to greet her. 
      "I need a new job," Ms. Fernandez said irritably as she kicked off her high heels.
      "Yes," everyone at the table said, and Ms. Fernandez looked up at them, blinking as if she had just realized that they were sitting there.
      Ms. Fernandez sighed. "I think I'm going to call in sick for a couple of days." She walked into the kitchen to wash her hands before joining them at the table. "I really have to do some serious thinking about whether or not I should resign."
      "You just said it yourself." Tomas looked up at his mom. "What's keeping you there? I know the pay is good, but Mama is working too. We've got more than enough to coast on while you look for a new job."
      "My boss is practically forcing me to quit." Ms. Fernandez closed her eyes as she pinched the bridge of her nose. "When I asked him about getting promoted today, he just laughed and said he'd promote me if I joined him at his apartment after work for a drink."
      "You need to file a complaint." Mari's expression was horrified. "I still remember you mentioning how during breaks he'd even follow you to the restroom!"
      Ms. Fernandez sighed again. "Right now, I have no evidence. The camera footage keeps mysteriously disappearing. I can't accuse him of anything either. Even though he does follow me around, he hasn't physically touched me. It's my word against his. He'll just say that I'm slandering him."
      "What did you tell him in response to his proposal?" Tomas asked with a crease between his brows.
      "I was actually scheduled to work overtime again." Ms. Fernandez leaned back in her chair. "But after I went to ask him about a promotion and he gave me his response, I told him that I suddenly didn't feel well and was going to go home. And then I left."
	"Good." Tomas set his fork down on his plate. "You should call in sick for the next couple of days."
	Ms. Fernandez nodded her head. "I'll stay at home. I think it's about time I got a new job."
	Tye frowned. "You should still try and report him. And now he's even asking you to go home with him even though he knows you're already married."
	"He has no respect." Ruby grimaced, and Grace and Mari nodded in agreement.
	"I could try writing a piece about your situation," Mari offered. "I won't use your names of course, but I do have a blog with a good number of followers. I'm not sure how much it would do, but if I can help even a little bit, I'd like to try."
	"I appreciate it." Ms. Fernandez smiled faintly. "How has your blog been going recently?"
	"I haven't touched it in a few weeks due to studying for our AP exams," Mari admitted. "But once I get home tonight, I plan to upload the latest powerpoints I made for my club."
	As the conversation changed direction, the mood in the room lightened, and Tye found himself thinking about how Ms. Fernandez's situation was a problem where the solution was tricky to obtain. It was a problem with many steps-one that had to be picked apart and thoroughly examined before one could finally piece it back together and draw its conclusion.
	"Tye." Grace's voice drew Tye from his thoughts. "Have you finished eating? We're going to head downstairs to rehearse our song."

~

      "Look, look, look!" Tye rushed into Grace's room, and the screen of his phone glowed as he held it out to his sister.
      "It's not even six in the morning." Grace sat up in bed. She rubbed the sleep from her eyes as she squinted at the screen. "We still have another fifteen minutes until our alarms go off."
      "Look!" Tye shook his head, unable to contain his excitement. "We made the audition, Grace! We get to perform at the variety show!"
      "Really?" Grace blinked, suddenly wide awake as she snatched the phone from Tye and scrolled through the email. "This is wonderful! Have you told Ruby and the others yet?"
      "Not yet." Tye sat down next to Grace. "I'll tell them the news at seven. I know for a fact that Mari practically sleeps with her phone, and I don't want to wake her up this early if I don't have to."
      Grace elbowed Tye accusingly. "You didn't have to wake me up this early."
      "I just got the news. Who else was I supposed to share it with?"
      "I think this calls for a big celebration," Grace said determinedly. "We can celebrate the end of AP testing and our acceptance into the variety show."
      "Let's talk about it with the others during lunch today. I was pretty confident that we were going to make the auditions, but this news was still the best thing I've heard in a while."
      "What are we waiting for?" Grace jumped to her feet. "Let's get ready for school."

~

      "Hurray!" Mari pumped her fist in the air after Grace had presented the idea of a celebration. It was lunchtime, and Ruby, Grace, and Tye had just arrived at the club room.
      "I knew we could do it." Tomas joined them at the doorway, smiling faintly. "How do we want to celebrate?"
      "Are the four of you free over the weekend?" Ruby looked at all of them in turn. "We could go out to eat somewhere. How about that one Chinese restaurant we used to go to?"
      "Perfect!" Mari clapped her hands together. "I've missed that place. It feels like forever since we've been back."
      "It's only been a year give or take," Grace recalled. "Oh, if each of us brings ten dollars, I think we'll have more than enough to split some dishes."
      Since there was no more studying for AP tests, Tye and the others joined the discussion Mari and the other members of her club were having about bringing attention to unfair treatment in work environments. And for someone who was normally very quiet, Tomas had quite a lot to say about the topic.
	When the weekend came around, Grace and Tye took the bus to the restaurant to find Ruby and Mari already waiting outside. Tomas arrived shortly after, and the five of them eagerly headed inside.
	After being led to a table on the far side of the restaurant, the five of them looked over the menu for a good five minutes before ordering the same dishes they used to in the past. Their options had always been limited given the fact that Mari didn't eat pork, and Tye and Grace were both vegans.
	"Are we excited for the variety show?" Ruby leaned forward after they had ordered.
	There was a smile on Tye's face as he nodded his head along with the others. It was exciting to actually have something to look forward to. Tye didn't have any particular passions or hobbies the way his other friends did. He didn't play even a fraction of the instruments Tomas did, nor blog like Mari, or dance like Grace. And Ruby . . . Ruby was brilliant at everything she did. She had been the one to bring the five of them together. Maybe one day very soon, Tye would find his own passion. There was always music-music was calling to him.
      Tye's smile grew as he watched his friends chat away, and he laughed along with their light-hearted banter. He didn't need to think too hard about it right now. He still had another year, after all.
    


    Chapter 3.5

    Chapter 4

	"We've got one week until finals," Grace said in a worried whisper.
	Ruby flashed her a smile. The two of them were sitting next to each other in physics class. "Think about it this way: we've got two weeks until summer."
	"Summer," Grace said wistfully. "Summer couldn't arrive any faster."
	Ruby nodded in agreement. Even though she was still a junior in high school, everything was starting to feel like it was dragging out. When Ruby had mentioned this to her brother over a call, Tilden had laughed and said that that feeling was supposed to be saved for senior year.
	When the bell rang, Ruby and Grace made their way to Mari's club room only to find that the blonde-haired girl wasn't there. Tomas was standing at the front of the classroom instead, loading a presentation on his laptop.
	"Where's Mari?" Grace asked as the two of them walked over to him.
	"Mari says that she's sick." Tomas turned to face them, and he looked around the room as he rolled up the sleeves of his button-down shirt. "Where's Tye?"
	"Tye's returning a textbook," Grace informed him. "But we just saw Mari yesterday. She seemed fine then."
	Ruby walked over to their usual corner and took a seat at one of the desks. "It's possible to come down with a cold very quickly. If it's a common cold, Mari should be fine in a couple of days."
	A few minutes later, the door to the clubroom opened, and Tye stepped inside. When he spotted Tomas at the front of the classroom, he walked over to ask the same question about Mari. "I'll be taking over for her today," Tomas explained with a sigh. "I just hope Mari's alright."
	Ruby looked up from her stack of textbooks. "What's wrong with Mari? Is there something other than a cold going on that I don't know about?"
	"Mari, she-" Tomas started, but then he shook his head as he fell silent.
	Ruby gave him a suspicious look but turned back to her books all the same.
	PE class later that day felt a little odd without Mari there. Once the bell rang, Ruby pulled out her phone and opened their group chat. As she scrolled through the message, she found that Mari had been silent for a few more days than she usually was.
	Ruby put her phone away as Tomas appeared among the crowd of students flowing out of the front entrance. Since Mari was sick today, they decided it would be better to wait until she was back to meet at Tomas's house. There was still rehearsing to do for the variety show, and if Mari wasn't there, it would be difficult to concentrate. Or that had been Tomas's conclusion at least. Ruby waved Tomas over, and together, the two of them began their walk home.
	
~

	"Your dad's coming home early tonight," Ruby's mom informed her when Ruby walked through the front door. "He has something important he wants to tell us."
	"Alright." Ruby set her backpack down and walked over to Singsing. The puppy jumped up and down before eagerly running in circles around Ruby. After crouching down and patting Singsing on the head, Ruby went upstairs to start her homework.
	As she worked, she found her mind wandering. What was this imporant thing her dad wanted to tell her? All her dad ever did was work. He had always worked late and long hours, but ever since Tilden had left, Ruby rarely saw him around anymore.
	Her dad was part of a rapidly growing snack food company, and recently, from the ranting he had done one night to Ruby's mom, he was competing against one of his co-workers for the position of CEO. Ruby's dad had been working at the company since it opened, and it had been over ten years now.
	Ruby still remembered when the company had first started, it had been a tiny shop with no more than five employees. But now, their products were being sold in every major market. Ruby's grandparents had disapproved of her dad's company for the longest time, especially at the beginning when it seemed like it was fated to crumble quickly. As the son of immigrants, Ruby's dad wanted to make a name for himself in the world of business. Now he was a big name, but Ruby's Yeye and Nainai had passed away before they could see the glory their son had finally obtained.
	Ruby was happy for her dad. Except . . . Ruby sighed as she glance out the window at the darkening sky. Her dad was hardly present in her life anymore, and something felt missing without him around.
	A soft whimpering sounded at her feet, and she looked down to find Singsing sitting next to her chair. The puppy looked up at her with large eyes.
	"Do you miss Ba too?" Ruby asked as she reached down to scoop the puppy onto her lap. She swiveled her chair around to look at her guitar, propped up on its stand in the corner of her room.
	Music was something she lived for. Writing songs, playing her guitar, performing. Ruby wasn't sure what she'd do without it. Music had been everything her brother had lived for too, but where had it gotten him? It had gotten him kicked out of the house.
	Her parents had always seemed so proud of the way Tilden practiced his violin for hours on end, and even prouder when they attended his concerts. Ruby had never expected them to react the way they did when Tilden decided to major in it. She still remembered her mom arguing that musicians didn't make any money, and her dad saying that if Tilden chose to continue with music, he would never become successful in life. Tilden had tried to reason with them, but things escalated and ended with a full-out shouting match that left everyone in tears. Tilden had then packed his bags and stormed out the following morning.
	Looking back, Ruby wished she could have done more to argue on her brother's behalf. She knew that her parents only wanted what was best for their children, but they could at least give Tilden a chance. Ruby knew her parents and their parents had all sacrificed a lot to get to where they were today, but now, Ruby and her brother were in different positions from them.
      Ruby absently ran her hands through Singsing's curly fur. Her dad was coming home early tonight. Ruby blinked as it suddenly occurred to her that she hadn't told her parents about the variety show yet. She would let them know tonight. Her dad wouldn't be able to make it to the show given his work hours, but maybe her mom would be able to go. And maybe, when her mom saw how much work and passion Ruby and her friends had put into their song, she'd come to understand music-understand where Tilden had been coming from.
	"Ruby." A knock sounded on the door to Ruby's room, and it opened a moment later to reveal her mom. "Time to eat."
	Ruby nodded, and Singsing jumped off her lap as she rose from her seat. After taking her seat at the dining room table, Ruby looked from her mom to her dad and then back again.
	Ruby's dad finally broke the silence. "Shall we eat first and then listen to my announcement, or hear the announcement first?"
	"What's the announcement?" Ruby asked.
	Ruby's dad clasped his hands together on the table. "It's regarding my company and our summer plans. We're going to have a meeting to decide who will get the promotion to CEO. This meeting will take place in Maui, Hawaii."
	"Hawaii?"
	"Hawaii is one of the locations where we have a large stretch of farmland," Ruby's dad explained. "We all agreed to hold our annual meeting on Maui this year so we could check the farm and go on a retreat at the same time. And I . . . " he trailed off as he reached up to run a hand through his thinning hair. "I thought it would be nice for you and your mom to come along this year. The three of us could go as a family. It's been too long since the last time we've done something together as a family."
	"I-" Ruby just stared at him, at a loss for words.
	"We'll be picking you up on Friday right after your last final," her dad continued. "We wouldn't want to miss our flight."
	"Wait." Ruby shook her head, still trying to process his words. "We're going to Hawaii over the summer. And we're leaving the last Friday of the school year?"
	"That's right."
	"I-" Ruby started again, "would it be possible for me to stay home?"
	"Stay home?" Her mom blinked. Then her expression melted into a frown. "We're finally trying to do something together as a family, and you want to stay home?"
	"My friends and I are going to perform in our school's variety school." Ruby clasped her hands together in her lap, and her nails dug into her palms. "It's also on the last day of school. My friends and I spent so long working on our performance, and this will be the first time we ever perform on stage together."
	Ruby's mom sighed. "I know you've been missing your dad. I have too. And now he's finally giving us an opportunity to spend time together."
	"This isn't up for negotiation," Ruby's dad said sternly. "I've already paid for your ticket."
	"I'm old enough now to stay home by myself," Ruby tried even as that hopeless feeling began to sink in. "My friends worked just as hard as I did on our song."
	"Ruby." Her dad frowned. "It's just a song."
	"Over the years"-Ruby shook her head as she rose from her seat-"I've done everything you've wanted me to. I've taken all the classes you wanted me to take. I've kept my grades where you wanted them to be. Up until ninth grade, I went to Chinese school every day. Why can't I just have this one performance? Ba"-Ruby desperately turned to her dad-"it's the same with your work. You've put so much time, energy, and effort into it. But then right before you make a breakthrough, you're told you have to give it all up?"
	"How are those two things the same?" Ruby's mom asked in exasperation.
	Ruby turned to her. "Ma, you were the one who encouraged me to take all those guitar classes with Mari during elementary school. If you would just come to one of our practice sessions at Tomas's house to see what we've been working on-"
	"I encouraged you to take guitar lessons because I wanted you to be a well-rounded child," Ruby's mom said shortly. "If I knew what it would do to you and your brother, I would have never signed you up."
	"Tilden's living his best life in New York," Ruby tried one last time. "He's been contacted by a number of big orchestras waiting to take him in once he graduates. Just how famous does he have to become for you to see it?"
	"There's no room for negotiation here." Ruby's dad put his foot down.
	After looking hopelessly from her mom to her dad and then back again, Ruby turned on her heel and rushed up the stairs to her room.
	She flopped onto her bed and lay there for a while before rolling over onto her back. Her eyes stung as she blinked back angry tears. Ruby reached for her phone but stopped. She let her hand fall back to her side. She'd have to tell her friends that she could no longer perform with them at the variety show.
	This was partially Ruby's fault, though. If only she had told her parents about the variety show earlier . . . Ruby wasn't quite sure if that would have changed anything. She closed her eyes for a brief moment and opened them to find Singsing sitting on the bed next to her.
	"I let my friends down," Ruby told the puppy as she rolled over to stare up at the blank ceiling above her. "We weren't ready for the variety show last year, and this year when we finally got in, I can no longer be part of it."

~

	"You can't perform?" Mari's eyes were large as she stared at Ruby. "Then I'm not going to perform either."
	"Mari"-Ruby shook her head tiredly-"you don't need to step down just because I'm not going to be on stage with you."
	Tye exchanged a glance with Grace. "We won't perform either. You worked so hard on the song-you and Tomas both. It wouldn't feel right performing it without you there."
	"Exactly." Tomas nodded his head. "We can just sign up again next year."
	"But next year is our last year," Ruby tried as she looked from friend to friend. "What if we don't make it?"
	"Then we don't make it," Mari said simply. "We either do this together, or we don't do it at all."
	"I'm sure we'll make it next year," Grace added.
	"And if we don't," Tye finished for his sister, "I'm sure we could find a different place to perform."
	Ruby shook her head. "This is my fault for not telling my parents about the variety show sooner. Maybe if I told them earlier, they would have been more accommodating."
	"You don't know that for sure." Mari tugged on one of her braids. "They could have scheduled that flight regardless."
	Tye offered Ruby a smile. "You're going to Hawaii. I've never been to Hawaii. I bet you'll have a great time there. Take lots of pictures for us, will you?"
	Ruby gave Tye an exasperated look as she slumped down against the window at the back of Mari's clubroom. "It's not the same as performing with all of you. It came about so suddenly that I can't bring myself to feel excited about it either."
	Grace placed a hand on Ruby's shoulder. "Now that it is happening, all you can do is try and enjoy yourself. It is a vacation, after all."
	"You guys aren't mad at me?" Ruby asked.
	Mari smiled. "Of course not. We still have next year. It wasn't as if this was our only opportunity to perform together."
	"I still can't help but feel bad, though." Ruby turned to watch a single bird dive in and out of the fog outside the window. "I'll go with my parents to Hawaii, but I still want to spring a surprise on them the same way they did to me. Grace"-Ruby suddenly turned to face her friend-"I just had the perfect idea, and I'll need your help.

~

	When the final bell rang, instead of making her way to the front entrance as usual, Ruby headed to the back one. Grace was already waiting for her by the time she arrived, and the two of them set off together.
	"Are you sure you want to wait around outside?" Grace asked timidly when the two of them arrived at the doors to her dance studio. "There are a few shops in the area you could hang out at."
	"It's fine." Ruby offered her friend a smile. "I don't mind waiting outside."
	Grace nodded before pushing the dark-tinted doors open. Once Grace vanished, Ruby made her way over to one of the benches set up near the doors and pulled out her phone to check the time. She spent the first hour on her homework and then spent the rest of the time scrolling through her phone.
	When Grace reemerged, the sun had set, and the city lights blazed through the night, signaling its true awakening. Grace led the way through the maze of streets and lights. "Since we're not going to Tomas's house today, the bus stop this way is much more convenient."
	On the bus, Ruby watched the city lights blur by in silence. These lights had been all she had ever known. The reds and greens of the traffic lights, and the yellows and whites of the lamps and houses. There was something about the reds and grays of the city that made it beautiful. But it was the same pallet of reds and grays that made it dreary.
	"Here we are." Grace rose from her seat as the bus slowed to a stop. "It's been a while since you've been to my place. It's a few blocks away from the bus stop."
	Tye was waiting for them when they arrived at the door of the twins' apartment.
	"Hi, Ruby," Tye greeted them as he stepped aside to let them in. "I got everything set up in Grace's room."
	Grace sat Ruby down on the stool they had placed next to her desk, and three boxes of hair dye sat on the wooden surface in front of her.
	"All that's left is for you to choose your color." Tye gestured to the boxes.
	"You've never opened these before?" Ruby reached for one of the boxes, on which the cover model sported brilliant purple locks.
	"You know I can't dye my hair because of ballet," Grace said guiltily. "But it can't stop me from fantasizing anyway."
	Ruby set the purple box down and picked up the remaining two boxes of yellow and red.
	Tye leaned in. "I vote for red."
	"Red," Ruby decided as she nodded in agreement. "It has to be red."
	"Then red it is." Grace smiled, and her eyes lit up. "This is going to be fun! I've always wanted to dye hair before. I know that Tye offered to let me dye his hair, but he's this close to not having any hair." Grace held out her thumb and forefinger for emphasis.
	Tye held up his hands in defense. "Mom's the one who decides on that. I've got no say in the matter."
	"We don't need to bleach your hair for this red to show up," Grace explained as she got to work running a brush through Ruby's inky hair. "It will just show up as a shade of dark red. Ruby-red."
	Ruby looked into the mirror that Tye had set up on Grace's desk. "Fitting, isn't it?"
	Tye nodded. "Very."
	"Ready?" Grace asked as she pulled on a pair of disposable gloves. "Comfortable? This might take a while. Don't worry, though, I've watched enough videos to have at least some idea about what I'm doing."
	As Grace applied the dye to Ruby's hair, she paused for a moment, almost lost in thought.
	"Everything alright?" Ruby inquired.
	"Do you remember that boy in my first-period class?" Grace said mildly.
	"Everett?"
	"Yeah . . . he confessed to me today."
	Tye stared at Grace in disbelief. "He did what?"
	Grace got back to work on Ruby's hair. "I told him to stay away from me. Turns out the reason why he kept all my pencils was because he supposedly had a crush on me."
      Tye wrinkled his nose. "Eww."
	"Hey, I rejected him, didn't I?"
	"If he continues to bother you, definitely let your teacher know," Ruby said sympathetically. "Or let me know. I can tell him off."
	Before she knew it, Grace had finished with Ruby's hair. After washing and blow drying it, Ruby leaned forward to admire her new red hair in the mirror. "Wow, Grace! I'm impressed with how good it came out."
	"Don't act so surprised," Grace said proudly. "You came to me of all people for a reason. Anyway, it's getting late. You should probably head home before your parents start to worry."
	"Thank you again." Ruby turned to face her friends as she stood in the hallway in front of their apartment.
	"Send us a text when you get home," Grace called as Ruby started off.
	Ruby waved one final time before she made her way down the flights of stairs, down the block, and all the way back to the bus stop. Her mom was not going to be happy when she got back sporting deep-red hair. But that had been the whole point, wasn't it?
      Ruby let out a sigh. Angering her parents wasn't something she normally went out of her way to do, or even something she thought about doing. And maybe she was being a little unreasonable . . .
	Ruby closed her eyes for a brief moment as she stood at the bus stop. The glow of the advertisements cast her in a pale blue light. A light wind picked up, making Ruby momentarily question her choice of flip-flops, shorts, and a tank top.
      Ignoring the sudden chill, Ruby pulled out her phone and let the light from the screen illuminate her face. She scrolled through the messages she had last sent to her brother. Tilden hadn't responded yet.
      The bus arrived a few minutes later, and Ruby climbed on to find it was empty inside. Ruby took a seat in the middle of the bus and set her backpack down beside her. As the bus rolled into motion, Ruby snapped a picture of her red hair and sent it to her brother.
      Before long, Ruby found herself standing in front of her house. She sent a quick text to Grace to let her know she had made it home safely. Then after taking a deep breath of the night air, Ruby fumbled for her keys and pushed the door open.
      "Ruby!" her mom exclaimed, her head snapping up from where she had been sitting on the living room couch watching TV. Her eyes widened as they went straight to Ruby's red hair.
      "Good evening," Ruby said as casually as she could. She slipped off her shoes and made her way toward the stairs.
      "Stop right there!" her mom commanded, and Ruby froze with her foot hovering over the first step.
	Slowly lowering her foot, Ruby turned to face her. "Ma." Ruby held her mom's gaze. "I just want you and Ba to know that I was serious about that performance. I wished you could have respected that. After this year, my friends and I will only have one more chance to perform together in front of a crowd like that. All I had hoped was that you would be happy for me-that you would have been happy for Tilden."
	"Wash out that dye immediately!"
	Ruby folded her arms over her chest. "It's permanent. It doesn't wash out."
	Ruby and her mom just stared at each other for a long moment before her mom held out her hand, palm facing up. "Give me your phone. You're grounded."
	Ruby handed her phone over without any protest, and her mom made quick work of pocketing it. She had known this was coming.
	"You're not allowed to go play with your friends after school," her mom continued. "Until the end of the school year, you're to come home right away. Until finals have passed, I want you in your room studying."

~

	The days seemed to drag without being able to spend the evenings at Tomas's house with the others. Ruby still got to see her friends during lunch, but their time was cut short by the studying that had fallen upon them yet again.
      And then finals arrived, and just like that, it was the last day of school.
	Ruby sat in the back of her dad's car, staring absently out the window as they drove toward the airport. Three weeks. They were going to stay in Maui for three weeks. Ruby's suitcase of clothes was in the trunk of the car along with her guitar. When she had placed it in the trunk, her parents hadn't said anything in protest. So maybe they did feel a little bad after all, Ruby concluded.
	The flight lasted around five hours, and when they finally landed, the tiredness Ruby had felt while sitting on the plane faded as she stepped into the airport. Through the large glass windows, the sky was a brilliant shade of blue without a cloud to be seen. The world was full of vibrant greens and rich blues, and the ocean in the distance was infinite. The air was warm, and Ruby wanted to just stand there and breathe it in. During the flight, Ruby had done her best not to think about the variety show that had been going on. And now that she was here . . . 
	The drive to the house they would be staying was no more than thirty minutes, and before long, Ruby was unpacking her suitcase in one of the guest bedrooms on the second floor. It was a nice house, and the beach and ocean were practically their backyard.
	When Ruby finished unpacking, she opened her window and leaned on the windowsill. She watched the ocean waves lazily lapping at the powdery sand. There was just so much to take in: the blueness of the sky, the warmth of the sun, the crystal-like waters. A breeze picked up and set Ruby's deep-red hair dancing.
	Ruby stood there by the window as the sky slowly changed color. The sunset washed over the island as it gave way to nightfall, and once the sky had darkened completely, the stars steadily emerged to sparkle over the ocean. Only then did Ruby finally turn away from the window and take a seat at the desk on the far side of the room.
	Ruby had brought her stationery kit with her, and she placed one of the papers in front of her. She twirled her pencil between her fingers. It had been a while since she wrote a letter to anyone. She still didn't have access to her phone, and this way, she could write to her brother and friends. Obviously, when she sent out her letters, her friend's responses wouldn't be immediate. But that was fine. It still helped her feel connected to them anyway.
      Her first letter was addressed to Tilden, informing her brother that she had just arrived in Maui. She also told him about the house provided by their dad's company. When she finished the letter, Ruby started drafting one for Grace. But halfway through, Ruby felt her exhaustion overtake her. Even if there was only a three-hour time difference, Ruby was starting to feel it. Tomorrow, Ruby decided. She would finish her letters tomorrow.
	
~

	By the time Ruby woke up in the morning, her dad had already left to meet his co-workers, and her mom had gone out too. She had left a note on the dining room table explaining that she had gone to pick up groceries and added that Ruby still wasn't allowed to have her phone back.
	After frowning at the note, Ruby made her way to the front door and slipped on her flip-flops. She would go for a walk.
      She made her way to the stretch of beach behind the house and walked along the water's edge. The ocean itself was a deep blue in contrast to the bright one of the sky. Ruby hummed to herself as she walked, and her deep-red hair whipped around her face. As she walked further, her humming turned into the song she had written with her friends.
      Suddenly, something glittery caught Ruby's eye, and she blinked. The sun was reflecting off something in the distance. Ruby squinted, trying to block out the sun's glare with her hand as she looked out over the water.
	And then her eyes widened. Her eyes had to be playing tricks on her. No. It couldn't be. Could it?
	Ruby blinked rapidly, but by the time she looked again, the figure had vanished beneath the waves.

    Chapter 5

	Had he been spotted?
      Aouli swam deeper into the turquoise waters, away from the sandy beach and the girl with the deep-red hair. He happened to hear the faint sound of someone singing. He was drawn to it, and he followed the sound all the way to the beach.
	Sunlight spilled through the surface of the water and scattered over the colorful floors of the ocean. Aouli swam between the flocks of colorful fish, his tail propelling him through the water with ease. He had to tell his sister about the girl with the red hair. Maybe his sister would like to see her too.
	It was true that he had swam a little too far this time. He had gone too close to the shore. But when he heard the sound of singing in the breeze, his curiosity got the better of him.
	Humming a tune of his own, Aouli finally arrived at his sister's residence. As of now, his sister had the second-largest living space in their village. His father, the high chief, still had the largest one, but his sister would soon inherit it when she became the new village chief in twenty days' time. In twenty days, their father would be sixty summers old. And at sixty, it was tradition for the high chief to step down and live comfortably without having to worry about village affairs.
	Aouli's older sister, Healani, had always been next in line to be the village's high chief, and she was diligently learning everything she needed. Aouli had never once thought about becoming the high chief himself. He didn't want to stay in the village all day; he'd rather be out exploring the oceans and basking in the warm rays of the sun.
	Aouli brushed aside the curtain of kelp as he eagerly swam into Healani's residence. "I have something to tell you."
	"Aouli?" Healani was sitting on the smooth rock where she spent her days studying texts. But she wasn't alone. A female with green hair sat next to her as the two of them poured over the stack of stone tablets piled on the floor.
	"Your little brother's here," the green-haired female said. "Interpreting work again, I see."
      Healani's sea-glass hair billowed out in the water around her as she tiredly set down the tablet she was holding. "Is something wrong?"
      "There's a human girl with red hair on the beach," Aouli explained quickly. "If we hurry, she might still be there."
      "A human?" Healani inhaled sharply before motioning with a hand for the green-haired female to leave them. Healani waited until the female had vanished before swimming over to Aouli. There was something quizzical flickering behind her deep-brown eyes. "What were you doing so close to the shore? What if you were seen?"
      "I didn't get that close." Aouli's long hair drifted through the water as he shook his head. "I'm careful."
      Healani just gave him an exasperated look.
      "We need to move fast." Aouli turned, but then stopped when his sister didn't move.
      Healani held his gaze. "I'm not going. It would be better for all of us if we stayed away from the humans." She sighed as she took Aouli's hands in her own. "Humans are dangerous, and I don't want anything to happen to you. Father feels the same way. After we lost Mother . . ."
      "I-" Aouli started. His sister was right, though. He had been too rash. Too adventurous. "I'm sorry."
      "I'm just glad you're safe." Healani pulled Aouli into an embrace. "Now be good, will you? I need to get back to work and can't watch over you. Do me a favor and stay in the village today. Oh, that reminds me of something."
      Aouli just blinked as Healani swam to one of the shelves built into the single rocky wall. She ran her hand over the assortment of colorful bottles that covered it.
      "This." Healani swam back to Aouli with a familiar plain-looking one in hand. "I just finished my prescription last night. I'd go ask her myself, but you know I'm going to be busy. And she likes you better," Healani added as an afterthought.
      It was Aouli's turn to sigh as he took the empty bottle from his sister. "Take care, then." After brushing aside the curtain of kelp, Aouli made his way into the village. Youngsters were swimming among the vibrant corals that covered the ocean floor, and they all stopped to wave at Aouli as he swam past. Aouli waved back and offered them a friendly smile.
      "Aouli!" One of them came over to swim beside him. "Will you come and play with us?"
      "I can't right now," Aouli told the boy regretfully. "I need to go to the far side of the village to run an errand for my sister."
      The boy's eyes grew larger. "You're off to see the sea witch! My mother always tells me to beware of the sea witch!"
      "This isn't my first time going to see her," Aouli reassured the boy. "She's not nearly as bad as everyone claims she is."
      "Beware of the sea witch!" the other children chorused as they swam over to join their friend. "Beware of the sea witch!"
      Before long, Aouli found himself in front of the cave's all too familiar entrance. Lifting a hand, he brushed aside the curtain of kelp covering the opening. It was dark inside. He withdrew his hand and let the curtain fall back in place. Was anyone even here?
      Looking back at the cave entrance, Aouli's eyes fell on the sign engraved on the stones. Welcome! The stone read. Selling Medicine and Fortunes Inside.
      Shaking his head, Aouli pushed the kelp aside for a second time and cautiously swam into the darkness beyond. The moment the kelp curtain closed behind him, total silence fell. Aouli blindly swam through the dark, and he squinted as something zipped past his ear.
      "Boo!" a voice sang from behind him.
      Aouli whirled around as the cave was suddenly illuminated with a number of glowing lights. A young female floating in the center of the brightness.
      "I'm sorry!" The female giggled, and her long hair flowed as she doubled over from laughing. "I couldn't help it-I don't get many visitors these days."
      "Ulani," Aouli greeted her. "I tried to tell the village children that you aren't nearly as horrible as they've been led to believe, but maybe I shouldn't have tried to defend you."
      Ulani stopped laughing to look up at Aouli with milky-white eyes. "You stood up for me?" Then she busted out into a new fit of giggles. "This has to be my lucky day! The son of the high chief stood up for me!"
      Aouli just shook his head in exasperation. There was a reason why the villagers warned him to stay away from the sea witch-she was always a handful to deal with.
      "My sister sent me," Aouli explained. "She needs another bottle."
      "Oh." Ulani came to a stop in front of Aouli. "Your sister sent you. Of course."
      "The people in the village don't really like to associate with you. I've told you before that if you'd like to see me more often, I can meet up with you beyond the reef. But you won't leave your cave."
      "Beyond these walls is danger," Ulani warned. "Beyond these walls are humans. And the humans are responsible for the passing of our previous chief."
      Aouli handed the bottle to Ulani. "I didn't come here to talk about my mother."
      Ulani took the bottle from him. "You're not nearly cautious enough as you should be. Now, how much should I charge you this time for the prescription? Since you're my handsome childhood friend, I'll give you a discount . . . "
      "How much does the prescription cost this time?" Aouli asked.
      "The coral from the far reef. I want two stalks of the orange one."
      "Consider it done." Aouli turned and made to leave the cave.
      "Wait!" Ulani's voice stopped him.
      Aouli looked over his shoulder at her. "What is it now?"
      "You're still blaming me for getting us lost. That's why you don't visit me anymore."
      Aouli just dropped his gaze. "I know it's not your fault. I just hope you can understand why I don't want to be spending so much time around you."
      "I didn't know what the visions meant at the time." Ulani's hands clenched into fists at her side. "I had never gone far from my cave before. I got us lost."
      Aouli sighed. "I don't blame you. We were still able to find my sister, remember? If it wasn't for you, she would have continued to risk her own health to stay by Mother's side." 
      Years ago, Aouli's mother, the former high chief, had gone out with Healani to introduce her to the neighboring village's chief. But on the way, the two of them had run into an oil spill.
      At the time, Aouli had been playing with the other children in the village. Ulani had been there too, and Aouli still remembered how she grabbed his arm and told him worriedly that she had seen that his mother was in trouble.
      Aouli had gone to his father and they all had quickly swam off with the rest of the village adults to search for their chief. They swam for hours to reach the sight of the spill, and then Ulani had done her best to navigate through the thick oil, but the area had been too large. By the time they found Aouli's mother and Healani, the damage had been done. To this day, Healani's vision was still damaged by the toxins, and she had never fully recovered from the trauma of the experience.
      Ulani had rarely been seen outside her cave since then. Some said that she was perfecting her vision abilities while others claimed that she had shut herself off from the world since she was too ashamed to face anyone.
      "I'll come to visit you more often." Aouli offered Ulani a small smile. "It's childish of me to be ignoring you the way I am. We're old friends after all, and my sister wants me to stay close to the town anyway. After I bring you the coral, I'll stop by more often."
      Ulani clapped her hands together. "I'll be looking forward to it!"
      After waving goodbye, Aouli made his way out of the cave. As he swam back to his sister's residence, the children who had been playing among the coral hurried over to him.
      "Was the sea witch frightening?" one of them asked with wide eyes.
      Aouli let out a laugh. "The sea witch isn't frightening. She's not really a witch either. She's one of your local healers. Remember that whenever one of you gets hurt and needs to get medicine from her. I've got to go get something for her now. Be good, all of you."
      "Bye-bye!" The children waved as Aouli swam off.
      After dropping off the bottle at his sister's residence, he started on his journey to the far side of the island where the orange coral grew. Accompanied by flocks of brightly colored fish, Aouli twirled through the waters. But as he neared the far side of the island, Aouli suddenly felt that something was right.
      Slowing his pace, Aouli looked around at his surroundings. Nothing seemed out of place. He cautiously proceeded on his way. As he moved forward, he found that the water was gradually getting more and more mirky, and the fine film of algae floating on the surface thickened until the sunlight struggled to break through.
      There were hardly any signs of life. No fish, no plants. It was completely dead. Silent.
      Aouli just stared at the emptiness. He had never seen anything like it before. The last time he had gone out to this side of the island hadn't been that long ago . . . Well, maybe it had been a few years. But what could have caused a dead zone to occur so quickly?
      A shiver ran down Aouli's spine, and he quickly swam upward. His head broke through the algae-covered surface. The murky darkness wasn't right. Blinking in the brightness of the sun, Aouli stared out over the ocean's surface. How far did this dead zone extend? He made up his mind that he didn't want to swim through it. He'd go around.
      Aouli eventually made it to where the orange coral was growing, and on his way back, he found himself so distracted he almost swam right past his village. Something about the water in the dead zone had felt so wrong. He had to tell his father. What if the dead zone spread? Would it reach their village?
      When he returned to Ulani's cave, the sign outside had been changed to "closed," and Aouli set the orange coral outside the entrance before swimming off.
      "Father." Aouli swam over to where his father was talking to a number of the other adults in the center of the village.
      "Aouli." Aouli's father blinked as he read the worried expression on his son's face. "What's wrong?"
      "I found something you might want to see," Aouli said grimly. "On the far side of the island, there's a patch of water where nothing grows. A patch of water where nothing lives. I'm worried it might spread. I'll only be able to stop worrying after you assess the situation for yourself."
      "Lead the way."
      Aouli pointed out the dead zone to his father when the two of them arrived at the far side of the island.
      Aouli's father closed his eyes as if he could feel the ocean itself. "The water here is out of balance."
      "What could have thrown the ocean out of balance?" Aouli asked quickly.
      "I think 'who' could have thrown the ocean out of balance is a better question." The high chief opened his eyes, and his expression was grim.
      Aouli looked up at his father. "The humans?"
      "Who else but humans has enough power to do such a thing? I need to arrange a talk with the islanders. They promised that we could live in peace with them. I want to ask them just what exactly is going on. And for the time being"-his father looked down at him-"I want you to stay close to the village. Don't wander off too far."
      "Shouldn't I try and help see if there's any more of these dead patches?" Aouli asked. "I want to help."
      The high chief let out a sigh. "Your sister will worry if she hears about this news. Let's not tell her about the dead patches for the time being. She's about to become the high chief, and I want everything to go smoothly. I'll speak with the islanders to clear things up. We'll leave finding the rest of the dead patches to the adults."
      "Alright." It was Aouli's turn to let out a sigh. The village was a lively place, but sometimes it was that very liveliness that made Aouli want to swim out into the ocean-to swim through the clear waters among the colorful fish and plants. He wanted to sit on the rocks and sing. But it seemed that he would have to go back to the village. He didn't want to go against his father's wishes, nor did he want to trouble his sister.
      
~
      
      That night, Aouli went to visit his sister.
      "Aouli." Healani raised her head from the stone tablets she was looking over.
      "Father doesn't want me to go far from the village," Aouli said sulkily. "All the young children have gone home, Father's busy like always, and all I can do now is visit you."
      "What about everyone who's the same age as you?" Healani asked mildly. "I'm sure they'd love to hang out with you."
      "I prefer to be on my own. I want to explore the oceans, and everyone else just wants to stay in the village."
      "Have you asked them?"
      "Well, no-"
      "Maybe some of them would like to go with you."
      "What have you been up to recently?" Aouli changed the topic. "I hope you haven't been working yourself too hard."
      "I've been trying to find a husband," Healani said lightly. "It's my responsibility to take a husband once I become high chief."
      "A husband?"
      "This is what happens when you don't pay attention to the village rules."
      "I'm not going to be high chief." Aouli swam upward to watch the last rays of sunlight fade from above the surface of the water. "I don't see why I need to pay attention to every single rule. We've got thousands of them-I know about half, and I think that should be enough for me to get around without falling into any trouble."
      "Half?" A smile tugged on the corners of Healani's lips. "That's a lot more than I gave you credit for." When Aouli didn't respond, Healani swam over. Her sea-glass hair wafted around her as she turned to face him. "You look like you've got something on your mind. What are you thinking about?"
      Aouli looked over at his sister. "The human girl I saw this morning-she was singing a song. That's what led me to her."
      "A song?"
      "It was beautiful."
      Healani tilted her head to the side. "There's plenty of people here who can sing."
      "I want to see the girl again. I want to know what she was singing."
      "The humans don't speak our language," Healani said gently. "You won't be able to understand her words."
      "I know." Aouli looked away. "I just . . . "
      Healani brushed her long hair over her shoulder. "How about this: if you behave and stay in the village for the next couple of days, I'll talk to Father about letting you leave on your own again."
      "You'd talk to Father?" Aouli asked excitedly as he looked up at his sister.
      Healani nodded.
      Aouli swam in a circle around his sister. "Thank you!"

~

	As his sister had said, Aouli was able to travel beyond the village after a few days. The first place he went was the beach, and he stuck his head out of the water to look at it from afar. It was empty, and a cool wind cut through the morning air. This was just around the same time he had seen the girl before.
	Aouli didn't have to wait long before the girl with the deep-red hair appeared from around one of the large structures that lined the sand. Aouli watched as she made her way down the stretch of beach. She was looking out over the water, but Aouli had made sure he was far enough from the shore not to be noticed.
	Sinking beneath the water's surface, Aouli made his way closer. The girl was singing again.
	Aouli remained in the water, listening to the girl's song until she went back the way she had come and finally vanished from sight.
