    Chapter 6

	Mari sat up in bed as her phone buzzed on her nightstand. She rubbed the sleep from her eyes and blinked at the smudges of black ink that rubbed off on her hand.
	Grimacing, Mari rose to her feet, ignoring her phone as she made her way to the bathroom. She made quick work of wiping off her makeup and grimaced even more at the dark circles that seemed to have permanently etched themselves under her eyes.
	School was over for now. So why hadn't the circles gone away?
	Mari trudged back to her room, only realizing halfway back that she had lost one of her fuzzy socks somewhere along the way. After deciding it would be better just to leave it, Mari returned to her room and closed the door behind her.
	After taking a seat on her bed, Mari reached for her phone. 100 new messages, the screen read. She stared blankly at the screen for a long moment before unlocking her phone. Most of the messages had come from the comment and private message sections on her blog. Drawing her knees to her chest, Mari read through the messages.
      The first message was just a string of rude emojis. Only ugly women are feminists, another read. Don't be shy, show us your face so we all can have a good laugh.
	Tapping into the private message channel, Mari began to scroll through the messages there. 
	KILL YOURSELF BITCH, the first one read.
	Will you be my girlfriend? another one said.
	After scrolling even further, Mari finally tossed her phone to the side and curled up under her blankets. Her parents got back from work around four, and until then, it was just her alone in the house.
	Many summers ago, she and Ruby had hung out nearly every day. They had gone to the park with their guitars and played for everyone walking through it. And on other days, Ruby would come over to Mari's house, and the two of them would play computer games together. But now Ruby was in Hawaii. Mari was happy for her, if not a little jealous.
      Mari closed her eyes. She needed to ignore the messages. She needed to disable the private message feature on her blog. But she couldn't bring herself to do it. What if someone wanted to have a genuine conversation? It had happened a few times in the past, and Mari had made a number of great online friends from it. Reading the messages was like an addiction.
	Mari wasn't even sure how so many people had found her blog. No, that was a lie too.
	Mari had put her information on a the wall in the classroom where she held her meetings. Anyone in any of those class periods could have typed in the address to her blog. Anyone in any of those class periods could have scanned the QR code. It scared her that the messages being sent to her could be from the very people she walked by every day at school. Except she would never know who they were even if they were standing right in front of her.
	It wasn't just her blog that was getting spammed with comments; all her other social media promoting her blog were too.
	Mari hadn't told her parents. She hadn't told her friends either. When she had been in a similar situation back in ninth grade, Ruby had helped her out of it. But this year, Ruby had been so busy with classwork that Mari didn't have the heart to bother her.
	Mari knew she had to be able to stand up for herself, and she knew all too well that she wasn't handling her own situation very well. Reading the comments was a very bad habit, but Mari couldn't help it. Without access to the internet, she felt cut off from the world. Isolated.
	Her middle school years hadn't exactly gone the way she had wanted them to. After graduating from elementary school, she and Ruby had ended up going to different middle schools. While Ruby quickly befriended Grace and Tye, the friends Mari had made in sixth grade turned out to be superficial. After they caused her more grief than necessary, Mari chose to no longer associate with them for the remainder of her middle school years.
	Now Mari had friends again. She had Ruby as her friend again. But there was some sort of disconnect between them. The two of them no longer did things together the way they used to. Mari enjoyed hanging out with Grace, Tye, and Tomas. She and Grace had connected pretty quickly, but Mari still had yet to hang out with Grace one on one outside of school due to Grace's packed schedule. Tye was fun to be around as well, but sometimes she found him a little intimidating because of how good of a student he was.
	And then there was Tomas. Mari really enjoyed being around Tomas.
	Suddenly Mari's phone buzzed, and she nearly jumped out of her skin. After timidly picking it up, Mari glanced at the message glowing on the screen. It was from Tomas.
	Are you alright? Tomas's message read.
	Mari quickly unlocked her phone and typed back, I'm fine. Mari's finger hovered over the send button for a moment before she paused, deleted the text, and wrote instead, Would you like to hang out today?
	Sure! Tomas's reply came almost instantly. Where? What time?
	Do you want to come over? Around five? My parents should be back from work by then.
	Sounds good.
	Mari set her phone down and stood up. She walked over to her window in a daze, pulled back the blinds, and winced in the light that flooded into her room. Turning to her mirror, she tugged at her hair. If she was going to have a guest over later, she should probably freshen up.
	After taking a shower, Mari was back in her room. She absently made her bed and then walked over to her desk. She sat down in front of her laptop. After logging into her favorite game, Mari instinctively clicked open her friend list, and out of habit, scrolled down to where Ruby's player tag was listed. Rosey_Whispers, the line of text read. Last online 583 days ago.
	After wandering aimlessly around the map for a good ten minutes, Mari closed the game and open the folder of articles she had been combing through for the new paper she was drafting. Then she paused. Maybe she should just leave the paper alone. If she didn't post anymore, the commenters on her blog would eventually stop commenting. No, Mari quickly shook her head. If she stopped, she'd just be giving in to what they wanted.
	With her fingers floating over the keys, Mari determinedly started to type.

~

	"Is it alright if Tomas comes over?" Mari asked her parents once the two of them arrived home.
	"Tomas?" Mari's dad blinked. "Of course. When? Today?"
	Mari shuffled her feet. "In about an hour or so."
	Mari's mom nodded her head. "Tomas has been over a couple of times before. What do the two of you plan to do?"
	"Probably either play video games or guitar like we did before."
	Mari's dad walked over to take a seat on their living room couch. "Tomas is a good kid. You should tell him to come over more often."

	~

	Tomas arrived at exactly five o'clock, and Mari hurried over to the door to greet him. After dipping his head respectively to Mari's parents, Mari pulled Tomas up the short flight of stairs to her room.
	"I brought my laptop," Tomas said proudly as he took a seat on the floor of Mari's room.
	"Would you like to play a song first together before we go online?" Mari asked as she brushed her twin braids over her shoulder.
	Tomas smiled faintly. "Let's do that."
	"I used to always play duets with Ruby," Mari recalled wistfully as she took her guitar from its stand before sitting down across from Tomas. "Ruby always played the melody, and I was the harmony."
	"Have you ever wanted to sing the melody yourself?"
	Mari shook her head. "I didn't mind singing harmony. Besides, I didn't have the confidence to sing the main vocals."
	"I actually prefer your singing to Ruby's," Tomas said quietly. "Ruby is a great singer. The two of you just have very different styles."
	Mari laughed, but Tomas just shook his head.
	"It's true."
	"Do you want to play the guitar?" Mari held her guitar out to Tomas. "I can sing."
	Tomas nodded. He took the instrument from Mari, checking to make sure it was in tune before looking up. "What shall we play?"
	"I have a folder of old pop songs Ruby and I used to sing together." Mari climbed to her feet. She pulled open the drawer on her nightstand and returned to her seat with the folder in hand. "I guess we can start with the first one here."
	And so Mari sang. Her voice blended perfectly with Tomas's chords. Before she knew it, the two of them had played through all of the songs in the folder.
	Mari clapped her hands together. "That was fun!"
	"It was," Tomas agreed. "I'm serious, you should take the melody in one of our jam sessions."
	Mari just let out a weak laugh. Suddenly her phone buzzed from where it was sitting on her bed.
	"What else did you and Ruby do?" Tomas asked, drawing Mari's attention away from her phone.
	"Ruby and I used to paint each other's nails." A smile tugged on the corners of Mari's lips. "Would you be willing to let me do your nails?"
	Tomas dropped his gaze. "You could do my toenails."
	"Really?" Mari asked excitedly. "Stay right here-I'll go get the nail polish from the bathroom." When she returned, she let Tomas pick a color (he picked orange) and then skillfully got to work painting them.
	"I've missed this," Mari lamented as she took a seat next to Tomas. She put the bottle of polish back in her box as the two of them waited for the polish to dry. "I'm sorry, Tomas. I hope I didn't make this too awkward for you."
	Tomas offered Mari a smile. "I don't mind. Really."
	"Do we still want to try and clear a dungeon?" Mari asked. "It is getting later."
	Tomas grinned. "I've always got time to try and clear a dungeon."

~

	"Hello." Mari's dad knocked on the door before pushing it open and sticking his head into the room. "It's nearly ten o'clock, kiddos."
	Mari blinked. She had completely lost track of the time. Tomas seemed to have as well from the way he guilty ran a hand through his dark hair.
	"Would you like a ride home?" Mari's dad asked Tomas.
	Tomas shut his laptop. "I didn't realize it had gotten this late. If you don't mind, I'd appreciate it."
	Mari closed her own laptop. "I'll join you for the car ride."
	The three of them made their way downstairs, and in the car, they sat quietly. Mari watched the city lights blur by outside the window. The reds and greens of the traffic lights cut through the fog.
	When they reached Tomas's house, Mari turned to him. "Thank you for coming over today," she said softly.
	Tomas smiled. "Would you like to hang out again tomorrow?" Mari nodded her head, and Tomas continued, "We can meet at my house. You can come over for lunch if you'd like. Isabelle has picked up cooking recently and would be happy to show off her skills."
	"I'd love to." Then waving one last time, Mari watched as Tomas walked over to the door of his house. He opened it and vanished inside.
	On the ride back, Mari's dad looked over at Mari in the mirror. "Ever since you and Ruby stopped hanging out, I was worried you were feeling lonely. But knowing you have a friend like Tomas, I feel relieved."
	Mari smiled faintly. "Me too."

~

	"What do we want to do today?" Tomas asked after Mari entered his house.
	"We could play video games and then play some music," Mari suggested. "I brought my laptop."
	Nodding, Tomas led the way to his room. After pushing the window open to let a cool breeze into the room, Tomas and Mari took a seat on the floor and logged into their accounts. Mari had already cleared all the major dungeons, and now the two of them were making their way through the smaller ones.
	"Watch out!" Tomas called as his fingers flew over the keys. "The boss is attacking from the right!"
	Mari swiftly maneuvered away from the tree demon the two of them were fighting and ducked under the barrage of branches it whipped at her. "That was a close call."
	Tomas's avatar leaped forward and threw a flaming fireball to disintegrate the branches.
	"That's a new skill," Mari said excitedly, restoring her own health with a healing spell as she looked on.
	Tomas grinned. "I just maxed it this morning. I don't know how I'd ever be able to use any of the other classes. The wizard's skill set is something else."
	"The witch and wizard combination is quite powerful. I remember when I was first playing the game with Ruby, I decided to pick a magic class, and Ruby picked a non-magic one. We thought that would have been the best combination for a duo, but witch and wizard are much more efficient."
	There was a knock on the door, and Isabelle stuck her head in. "Hello, screenagers."
	"You're one to talk," Tomas addressed his sister without looking up from his laptop. "I swear when I pass your room at four in the morning, I can still see the glow of your computer from under your door."
	"I'm going to make lunch." Isabelle turned, and her voice floated back to them as she made her way down the short hallway. "Remember to rest your eyes."
	"Isabelle does have a point." Mari closed the lid of her laptop before rising to her feet.
	"Should we play some music, then?" Tomas suggested as Mari offered him a hand to help him up.
	Mari beamed. "I was thinking the same thing."
	In the basement, Mari picked up the guitar, and Tomas took a seat behind the keyboard.
	Mari turned to Tomas expectantly. "What do we want to play?"
	"I just finished the first draft of a new song. I wrote it as a guitar and keyboard duet and was wondering if you'd like to sing the short segment in the middle. I haven't written any lyrics yet, but the melody is there."
	"I'd be honored," Mari said as Tomas passed her a sheet of score paper. "One day you're going to be famous, and I'll be able to say that we were friends!"
	
~

	After playing through Tomas's song a few times and helping him record a demo, Mari followed Tomas back upstairs. Isabelle had prepared lunch for them, and Mari found it very amusing to see Tomas's sister out of the natural environment that was her bedroom. It turned out that Isabelle was quite a good cook. Mari and Tomas returned to the latter's room to kill time after the two of them helped Isabelle with the dishes.
	"Shall we go back online?" Tomas asked. "We've still got a few more bosses to get past before we've cleared the dungeon."
	Mari logged back into her own account. "We've got this-the bosses don't stand a chance against our combined powers!"
	"The flame giant is the first one," Tomas pointed out. "Let's go."
	Colors flashed across the screen as Mari and Tomas pelted the flaming giant with magic. Suddenly, Mari froze as her eyes fell on something just beyond the screen of her laptop. "Spider!" Mari jumped up as if struck by lighting.
	"Spider?" Panic laced Tomas's voice as he too jumped up to scan the room.
	"Look, look!" Mari pointed wildly at the tiny spider scuttling around on the carpet.
	"It's coming towards us!" Tomas panicked and hurried backward onto his bed as if the spider couldn't get him there. "Over here!"
	Mari jumped onto the bed next to Tomas. Her eyes were still glued to the spider. "Good thinking-I don't think it can get us here."
	"Oh no!" Tomas exclaimed as he pointed to the laptops the two of them had discarded in their haste. "Look, the boss is killing us."
	Mari sighed. "It's fine. Look at us, defeated by a tiny spider."
	Tomas turned to Mari, seeming to get over some of his initial shock. "I didn't know you were afraid of spiders too."
	Mari let out a weak laugh. "I didn't know you were afraid of spiders either."
	"I've had some bad experiences with them." Tomas eyed the spider on the carpet. "Isabelle really hated them when the two of us were younger, so whenever she found one in the house, she'd make me take them outside. At the time I didn't really mind them. But then one day, one of those spiders crawled up my sleeve when I was trying to take it outside. When I couldn't find it, I started to panic. I woke up in the middle of the night with it crawling on my head, and since then, I've refused to go near spiders."
	"Oh no!"
	"It was definitely an unpleasant surprise. Anyway, we should probably figure out a way to get it outside."
	"Is there anything we could use to scoop up the spider? Like a book or something?"
	"Here." Tomas leaned forward to reach under his bed. He pulled out the first book he could reach. "What about this one?"
	"Perfect." Mari took the book (Taking Chord Progressions to the Next Level, Book 2) from Tomas before sliding off the bed to slowly tip-toe toward the spider.
	"Be careful," Tomas called.
	Gingerly bending down, Mari held the book in front of the spider until it had uncertainly scuttled onto the surface. Then hurrying over to the open window, Mari shook the spider off into the bushes beyond.
	Tomas was at her side in an instant and pulled the window shut. "It must have come in through the window." He frowned at the glass. "I'm going to talk to my moms about getting some kind of screen for it."
	The two of them just stood there in front of the window for a long moment before simultaneously bursting out into laughter.
	"And we've defeated the most difficult boss yet!" Tomas laughed.
	"The boss was no match for our combined powers," Mari said proudly.
	Tomas was smiling as nodded in agreement.
	"Do we want to go for a walk?" Mari suggested. "We've been sitting for hours."
	After saying goodbye to Isabelle, Mari and Tomas exited the house. They made their way up the block and slowly made their way toward the top of the hill.
	"Have there been any changes in your mom's situation at the office?" Mari asked lightly.
	"One of her co-workers reached out to her," Tomas informed her. "Apparently said co-worker had seen what was going on and finally mustered enough courage to tell my mom that she was not alone. My mom's getting ready to leave, and that co-worker has been doing some research into their boss's background. Turns out he's had a history of trying to get favors from female workers in exchange for promotions."
	"It's good that she's going to leave that place. I can tell that she isn't happy there. What sort of new work has she been looking at?"
	"More office tech jobs. She's got to put her degree to use somewhere."
	The two of them reached the top of the hill and looked out at the rows of houses in front of them. After a while, they turned to look at the buildings in the opposite direction that rose up from the ground to touch the sky.
	"Apparently cats eat spiders," Mari said absently as they watched the distant sun cut through the fog. It reflected off the glass windows of the skyscrapers.
	"If that's the case, I need a cat."
	"I've always wanted a cat, but my dad's allergic to them."
	Continuing on their way down the hill, Mari and Tomas turned to return to Tomas's house. Isabelle had disappeared back into her room by the time they arrived, and the house was quiet.
	"What happens now?" Mari asked as the two of them stood in the living room. But then her phone vibrated in her pocket.
	"You don't have to look at that if you don't want to," Tomas said quietly.
	Mari sighed. "I know. I had blocked a bunch of the spammers, but they always have their ways of coming back." Then she trailed off. "Wait, how did you know that I've been getting spammed?"
	"It wasn't hard to see that something was going on online," Tomas pointed out.
	"Was it that obvious?"
	"It's the same thing that happened in ninth grade, isn't it." Tomas held out a hand. Mari gingerly passed her phone over to him.
	"You knew it early on, didn't you." Mari blinked as it suddenly struck her. "Back at school, you were always trying your best to distract me from reading the messages."
	"I've seen the comments people have been leaving on your blog," Tomas admitted. "Some of them are quite nasty, and I've reported a good number of them."
	"I didn't know you followed my blog that closely." Mari stood next to Tomas and looked over his shoulder as he scrolled through the comments. "I remember that Ruby stopped looking at it a year or so after I launched it."
	"I've been reading it." Tomas looked up from the glowing screen to meet Mari's gaze.
	Mari walked over to take a seat on the couch and absently tugged on one of her twin braids.
	Tomas frowned. "Some of these are really awful."
	"Are you looking at the private messages?" Mari asked lightly.
	"I'm deleting these for you," Tomas said stiffly.
	"Go ahead."
	"Here." Tomas finally handed Mari's phone back after a good five minutes of silent scrolling. "I've disabled all comments and the private chat. I think it's for the best. When they realize that they can't send any more hate, they'll leave and focus their attacks on someone else. Then once they're gone, you can turn the comments back on."
	"Thank you," Mari said softly as she took her phone back. "I shouldn't have let things get this far-I should have blocked all of them ages ago. I think for the rest of the summer I should try not to spend as much time on my phone. It's really starting to drive me crazy."
	"I started to feel the same way whenever I spent too much time scrolling aimlessly through social media," Tomas said knowingly. "Then I uninstalled them all, and life's never been better."
	Mari let out a breath. "Maybe I should do that too."
	Both Mari and Tomas's phones vibrated at the same time. Tomas sat down next to Mari and showed her the message that had flashed across it. "Look, it's Tilden."

    Chapter 6.5

Tomas Quevedo: Tilden!!

Tomas Quevedo: Is today the day you'll finally send us a picture of San??

Tomas Quevedo: I won't tell you then.

    Chapter 7

	Tomas sat alone in his room, staring down at the different endings he had written for his song. Even though his laptop lay on his bed beside him, Tomas still preferred to write everything out by hand and then copy it over later.
	Mari had left no more than ten minutes ago, and Tomas hoped that, for her sake, she would try to stay off her phone as much as possible in the upcoming days. While reading through the private messages on Mari's blog, he had been disgusted by what he had seen. The most unsettling part about the messages was how some of the senders seemed to know quite a lot about Mari-even more so than she had put in her profile.
	Looking through his papers again, Tomas carefully decided on the proper ending. He walked over to the window and looked out at the wall of the neighbor's house. Maybe one day if he became a successful musician, he'd have enough money to rent an apartment somewhere where he could see the sky from his window.
	Tomas let out a humorless laugh as he turned away from the glass. If he really chose the path of a musician, he would undoubtedly be living at his parents' house for the rest of his life. Tomas could see himself in the future working an average desk job during the day. When he returned home late at night, he would have a short amount of time to play his instruments as quietly as possible to avoid waking and angering the neighbors.
	Tomas didn't want that to be his future, but he'd be foolish to hope for a better one. It had been something Tomas foolishly hoped for and fantasized about back in middle school. One day I'll have my name in lights, and then I'll have lots of friends, had been Tomas's thought process at the time. Sometimes, it was still something Tomas thought about, but more in a wistful sense than a serious one.
	Now Tomas had friends. Four very wonderful friends. But Tomas knew that his time together with them would come to an end eventually. They only had one more year before they were all off to college. Grace wanted to go to New York to pursue her dancing, Tye had his eyes on the Ivy Leagues, and Ruby was unlikely to stay in San Francisco. As of now, Mari still wasn't sure where she wanted to go.
	Tomas sat down on the floor of his room and stared absently at the posters covering the walls. He had put them up back in middle school when he started getting serious about music and hadn't changed the decorations since.
	Ever since Tomas entered high school, his social life had taken a turn for the better. He was fortunate to end up in several of the same classes as Ruby. After learning about Tomas's passion for music, Ruby quickly introduced him to her brother. Meeting Tilden was one of Tomas's best memories in ninth grade. Tilden had acted as an older brother to all of Ruby's friends, humoring them and helping them through school. Tomas hadn't met anyone with the same passion for music that Tilden possessed at the time, and it had been very inspiring.
	But the memory of ninth grade that Tomas treasured the most was the one of meeting Mari. Tomas had just finished his last class of the day and was heading to band practice when he heard the sound of singing coming from one of the practice rooms. The voice was accompanied by the strumming of a guitar.
	Tomas had lingered in the hallway for a minute, listening to the singing. When he finally forced himself to continue on his way, he passed the practice room and glanced inside to see Mari. He still remembered how Mari had stopped singing and how her hands stilled over the strings of her guitar as she looked up at him in surprise. Tomas still remembered how he had panicked and hurried away down the hall like an idiot.
	It had been a week after the incident that Ruby introduced Mari to Tomas. Mari had enthusiastically pointed to Tomas the moment she saw him, exclaiming that she had seen him before, and Tomas hastily explained that he was also a music student.
	The more Tomas got to know Mari, the more he realized that he enjoyed her company. As of now, things had gotten to the point where Tomas wasn't sure what life beyond high school would look like without Mari's presence.
	Tomas enjoyed listening to Mari talk and watching the way her eyes would light up when she spoke about the research she had done for a new article or discussed a new strategy that could be used in their gameplay. Ever since that first day Tomas had heard Mari sing, a year had passed until he heard Mari sing again. When they formed their own band, Mari had eagerly nominated Ruby for the position of singer, and Mari herself hadn't started to sing the harmony until just earlier this year.
	Tomas hadn't consciously realized that he might like Mari as more than just a friend until Tye had pointed it out.
	Did he like Mari in a way beyond just being friends? Tomas himself still wasn't completely sure. What would happen once high school was over would be a different story, but for now, Tomas still had one more year with to spend her. One year was plenty of time, he reassure himself. And maybe within that year, he'd get his feelings sorted out. If the two of them weren't meant to be, Tomas hoped that they could part on a good note.
	"Everything alright in here?" Isabelle popped her head through the open doorway. "It's kind of stuffy . . . how about we open the window?"
	"No," Tomas said quickly as he jumped to his feet. "No, let's not."
	"Alright, then," Isabelle said, but her brows were raised nonetheless.
	"I think I'm going to head back down to the basement. I want to make another demo recording."
	"Relax." Isabelle stepped aside to let Tomas pass through the doorway. "It's summer. You should play something for yourself, yes?"
	Nodding, Tomas made his way to the basement and took a seat behind the keyboard. Lightly placing his fingers on the keys, Tomas looked up at the sheet music he had left on one of the stands in front of it. It had been something he had been looking at for the jazz band. Tomas removed the stack of papers from the stand and transferred them to the boxes he had been meaning to sort through for many weeks now.
	Letting his mind drift, Tomas let his hands glide over the keys as he played through all the scales and arpeggios stored in his brain. After that, he played through a couple of the pieces he had previously memorized before spending the rest of his time improvising.
	He wasn't sure how long he had been playing, but when he finally looked up, Isabelle was leaning against the doorframe in her usual laid-back manner. "Moms are back," Isabelle informed him. "We're going out to dinner tonight."
	"Did something happen?" Tomas racked his brain for any possible birthday or holiday they could be celebrating, but ended up drawing a blank anyway. "What's the occasion?"
	"Mami resigned," Isabelle said in satisfaction. "She reached out to a number of other companies, and it turned out most of them got back to her pretty quickly with their offers. She just had to take her pick."
	Tomas jumped up. "She did? That's great!"
	Isabelle grinned. "Come on. We're going to go celebrate."

~

	During the car ride to the restaurant, Tomas looked out the window to watch Ruby's house pass by. All the lights were off, and the curtains were drawn over the windows. Come to think of it, Tomas wasn't quite sure what it was exactly that Ruby's dad did for a living. All he knew was that in the more recent years, Mr. Zhang had gained a lot of money very quickly. And for what Mrs. Zhang did for a living, Tomas knew even less.
	When they arrived at the restaurant, Tomas sat quietly after they ordered and listened to the conversation between his moms and Isabelle.
      "Everything alright?" Isabelle turned to him, taking note of Tomas's silence. "You seem really spacey today. More so than usual."
      "I'm fine," Tomas reassured her with a faint smile.
      "Are you thinking about college stuff?"
      "I'm trying not to think too much about the future right now."
      "Worst comes to worst, you could also get a degree online like me."
      "Yeah, at least that's always an option."
      "Your food is here." Their waiter came over to the table. "Please enjoy."
      Once the waiter had walked away, Tomas shook his head in an attempt to clear it. He didn't need to think about the future right at this moment.
      Smiling, Tomas joined the conversation with his moms as the sky outside the restaurant windows slowly faded to night.
      
~

	By the time Tomas returned home, the fog had cleared, and the moon shone brightly in the sky-but still not as brightly as the city lights. After spending an hour or so watching a movie with his family, Tomas headed off to his room to get ready to go to bed.
	Standing alone in the dark room, Tomas's phone gave a soft buzz. Tomas pulled it out and the light from the screen illuminated his face. It was a text from Mari. Would you like to hang out again tomorrow? the text read. Or maybe you wouldn't since we already hung out yesterday and the day before . . . 
	Quickly opening the chat, Tomas typed back, I'd love to hang out. What place? What time?
	Oh good, good, Mari's message came almost instantly. I was worried I was starting to be a bother.
	You're not a bother, Mari, Tomas typed. How about we go to the park? There's going to be clear skies tomorrow.
	Perfect! I'll see you there then.
	Weren't you trying to spend less time on your phone?
	This is the first time I've looked at it since I left your house, don't worry! Anyway, Goodnight Tomas!
	Goodnight Mari.
	Tomas reread their conversation before turning his phone. The room fell into darkness once again, and Tomas set his phone down on his desk before making his way over to the light switch.
	He had to admit that it still felt weird to have so much free time for himself. The stress of finals was finally over, but now there was a sort of emptiness in a way. The summer was long, and at the end of that tunnel was twelfth grade-the last stop before he had to finally step off the train of his childhood. What the next stop looked like-what adulthood looked like for him, Tomas could only speculate.
	He once had goals for the future and for his music. But the more he looked at things from a realistic perspective, the more unrealistic those goals seemed to be. The larger the scale of the goals he set, the less likely he was to meet any of them. So instead, he decided to focus on the small things. Tomas changed into his pajamas, climbed into bed, and hoped that he wouldn't find any spiders in his room when he woke.

~

	"Ruby and I used to go to the park a lot," Mari said as the two of them walked along the sidewalk. "At that time, we'd go every weekend, but we couldn't spend much time there due to the fact Ruby always had a piles of Chinese homework to finish."
	"Sometime after Ruby gets back from Hawaii, you should give her a call and ask her if she wants to go to the park."
	Mari shook her head as she offered Tomas a sad smile. "She wouldn't want to go to the park anymore. It's been too long now."
	"You never know. Look over there-doesn't that cloud look a little bit like a lion?"
	"Where, where?" Mari asked eagerly. Tomas pointed, and Mari quickly followed his finger to the group of fluffy white clouds.
	"You're right!" Mari laughed. "I can see the head and mane!"
	Tomas smiled at Mari's enthusiasm as he pointed to a smaller cloud that had broken away from the large cluster. "What do you think that one looks like?"
	"The little one over there?" Mari squinted against the sun, narrowing her eyes. "A turtle maybe?"
	"I can see it being a turtle." Tomas nodded in agreement. "The round part on the top is the shell, and then the head, tail, and legs stick out."
	"Exactly," Mari said proudly. "It's been a while since we've had clear skies. It finally feels like summer. You know what would make it feel even more like summer? Ice cream! I brought some money in case we decided to get anything today. It will be my treat."
	"Do you have any specific place in mind?"
	"If I remember correctly, there should be one just a few blocks from here. It's on the way to the park."
	"What's your favorite ice cream flavor?" Tomas asked curiously.
	"Sorbets are always good," Mari said thoughtfully. "Strawberry sorbet is good-not strawberry ice cream, though. Strawberry ice cream tends to taste off . . . but I think I like lemon the best. Ruby would always get the mint-chocolate chip. I remember never really liking the mint-chocolate chip."
	"I'm not particularly fond of mint-chocolate chip either," Tomas admitted. "And I'm glad that I'm not the only one who thinks the strawberry ice cream is weird. It tastes artificial. Almost reminiscent of the cheap cough medicine you can buy at the market."
	Mari clapped her hands together. "Exactly!"
	"It's my sister's favorite, though. Everyone has different tastes."
	"What about you?" Mari asked expectantly. "What's your favorite flavor?"
	"Vanilla."
	"Vanilla is good." Mari nodded her head approvingly. "Everyone loves vanilla-it's a classic."
	"Isabelle likes to poke fun at me because of it. I remember in elementary school when the class went on the last day of school to get ice cream, my classmates laughed at me for being boring."
	"Don't listen to them-vanilla is great!"
	Before long, the two of them found themselves outside the small ice cream parlor, and they got in line to order. Even though Tomas already knew what he was going to pick, he looked up at the chalkboard of flavors anyway. Cotten candy and birthday cake had been added since the last time he had gotten ice cream, and Tomas found himself eyeing the flavors wearily.
	When he and Mari arrived at the counter, Mari motioned for him to order first. "One cone of vanilla, please."
	"What?" The woman standing behind the counter leaned forward. The combination of the chatter in the store and Tomas's already quiet voice had seemed to render him completely inaudible.
	"We'll have two cones of vanilla, please." Mari beamed up at the women. Nodding, the woman shuffled off to scoop the ice cream.
	Tomas looked over at Mari. "You're getting vanilla too?"
	Mari just smiled. "I don't see why not. I used to really enjoy it as a kid. Talking with you today made me remember how much I miss it."
	When the woman returned, Mari handed over a ten-dollar bill, and the two of them left the shop after Mari dropped the handful of change into the plastic tip jar.
	"Summer at last," Mari sighed as they continued on their way to the park with their ice creams in hand. Then she smiled as she turned to Tomas. "This feels a little bit like a date, doesn't it?"
	"A date?"
	"Like in the movies."
	"If this was a date," Tomas started slowly, uncertainly, "what would you make of it?"
	Mari looked up at the sky. "I've never been on a date before." Tomas watched her-watched the way the sky reflected in Mari's brown eyes. "I fell like dates are more of a thing adults do."
	"Yeah." Tomas nodded his head, unsure of what kind of response he had expected. Should he should tell Mari how he felt about wanting to spend more time with her even beyond high school? No, what if he put a strain on their friendship? The two of them were friends-just friends. And that was fine. As long as Mari was happy, Tomas was happy. And if that meant continuing to be Mari's good friend, that was what he'd continue to do.
	When they arrived at the park, they sat down on the grass, chatting as they finished their ice cream.
	"You know"-Mari clasped her hands together behind her back once she had finished the last of her waffle cone-"I sometimes wonder what will happen to all of us once we graduate high school. Once we graduate college."
	Tomas smiled faintly at Mari. "You want to be a journalist. You're going to have a great future awaiting you."
	"I don't know about a great future, but I do know that once you're a famous musician, I'll stop by to write articles about you. By then, you'll probably have become so famous that you won't remember me."
	"I'll always remember you," Tomas said quickly before he realized he was voicing his thoughts out loud.
	"You're sweet, you know that?" Mari lowered her gaze from the sky to meet Tomas's. "I'm not sure what I did to deserve a friend like you. I-I think I'm really going to miss you after high school."
	"If we end up going to schools on different sides of the country, you can always send me a text. I will respond."
	"You're right." Mari let out a weak laugh. "No matter where anyone is in the world, we can still keep in contact with them. I think I've just been worrying too much."
	"What are you worrying about?"
	Mari sighed. "I've been in a place where I didn't have any friends before. You know as well as I do that it's difficult to get through school without friends. College will be the same as well, as work after it. In elementary school, I had a great friend. But it was only after I entered middle school without her that I realized I had taken that fact for granted. Making friends there was difficult-I couldn't connect with any of them the same way I did with Ruby. I know you had a similar middle school experience."
	"We're not in middle school anymore, though," Tomas said. "We don't have to go back there ever again."
	Mari dropped her gaze. "School is difficult sometimes. The hours feel long. Endless. But what happens when it does end? We've only got one more year, Tomas. But . . . I like the way things are now. I like the way things are with Ruby and Grace and Tye and you."
	Tomas let out a sigh as a cool wind picked up. "I feel that way too. The future is always an unknown. And the unknown is frightening."
	Mari tugged on one of her twin braids. "But it's also alluring in a way. What if we really are able to go out there and make names for ourselves? You know, let's not think about the future right now. We still have the present, don't we?"
	Tomas nodded. "Hey, did you hear that we're going to get a new limited-time level with special drops?"
	"Really?" Mari's eyes lit up. "Oh, that's right! There's always limited edition stuff in the summer. I wonder what it is this time? Cosmetics like last year? Or something actually useful?"
	"Here, let me show you the announcement." Tomas pulled out his phone and scrolled to where he had bookmarked the page.
	Mari frowned at the text glowing on the screen. "New dyes for hair and armor? I get that some people obsess over those things, but I still remember how two summers ago they introduced all of those new weapons. The hype surrounding the game then was more than I'd seen it in a very long time."
	"It's been too long since they've given us a chance to get new weapons," Tomas lamented. "It seems like cosmetics always make them the most money, so that's always the way they go."
	"We should try to get some of them anyway. That way we could sell them at the marketplace for a high price later. The longer we wait after the event ends, the price will just keep going up and up."
	"That's a good idea. We're getting short on potions anyway. The money will be useful."
	Mari clapped her hands together. "It's a plan! I hope you don't regret it since now we're going to be spending a lot of time together this summer."
	"I'm looking forward to it."

	That night, Tomas sat alone in his room with the screen of his laptop glowing up at him. He squinted at the tiny letters and blinked as the words swayed before his eyes. Maybe this was a sign-a sign that he either needed glasses after all, or he needed to go to sleep.
	Opening a new tab, Tomas typed, How to know if you're falling in love with someone. His finger hovering over the enter key, Tomas paused. What was he even doing? Tomas moved his fingers over to the delete key instead, but found himself hesitating again.
	Pressing the enter key, Tomas scrolled through the results and scanned the links. No, this was no good. After quickly closing the tab, Tomas shut the lid of the laptop. He hadn't practiced yet today. That was what he'd do.
	Tomas sat in front of the keyboard in the basement. He stared absently at the wall, deep in thought. Even though it was summer and he actually had time to access his feelings, Tomas still found himself drawing a blank.
	After standing up again, Tomas turned and hurried back to his room. He'd ask Tye for advice. Tomas picked up his phone and scrolled to Tye's contact. No, it was late. Tye probably wasn't even awake anymore. Maybe Ruby would have advice. Ruby always had advice. Tomas scrolled down to Ruby's contact instead, but then it struck him that Ruby was in Hawaii and still hadn't gotten her phone back.
	Finally, Tomas set his phone down, climbed into bed, and pulled the covers over his head.

    Chapter 8

      Over the past few days, Ruby had returned to the beach every morning. In fact, she spent the majority of her time on the beach, apart from when she would wander down the road and explore the numerous stores. Every morning, her dad left Ruby some cash before he left for his meetings, and once Ruby saved up enough, the first thing she did was rent a bike.
      Now that she was in Maui, Ruby wanted to make the most of it. Since her parents didn't have the time to take her sightseeing, she would do it herself. It was at times like this that Ruby wished she had a driver's license. A number of her classmates had one, but she had always been too busy to get around to it.
      Ruby let out a soft sigh as she sat on the fine sand of the beach. Her flip-flops lay discarded some distance away. Singsing ran over to Ruby. The puppy was panting, and her paws were caked with sand.
      "I'm glad you go to come along. Am I crazy, Singsing? I could have sworn I saw something the first day I came down here," Ruby mused more to herself than the dog. "It was something glittery. Could it have been some sort of sea animal? Some sort of hidden treasure?" Ruby tipped her head back to breathe in the warm, humid air. Had she really thought that by coming out to the water each day, she'd really see what had shimmered there in the water? For all she knew, it could have just been the light reflecting off the water's surface.
      Ruby rested her chin on her palms. She wondered how her friends were doing. Would they see the same brilliant blue sky as her? Or would the colors still be hidden behind a blanket of fog?
      Even though Ruby had been to beaches back in San Francisco, the waters hadn't been nearly as vibrant as the ones here in Hawaii. They didn't have the same turquoise hues. The islands were so bright and colorful. The island wasn't bustling in the same way as San Francisco, but it was busy in a different sort of way-busy in how the birds were always the first to wake, chirping relentlessly even long after the sun had risen.
      Singsing started barking. Ruby blinked and looked over at the puppy in surprise. Singsing rarely made any noises, but the dog was fixated on something in the distance-fixated on something in the water.
      "What is it, girl?" Ruby asked as she rose to her feet. A turtle maybe? "Hey, wait!"
      Singsing had dashed off into the water and was now paddling out into the ocean. Sprinting after the puppy, Ruby waded into the water. She carefully reached out for Singsing, but whenever her hands were about to close around the puppy's soaking fur, Singsing would paddle faster and slip out of her reach.
      Furrowing her brow in concentration, Ruby found herself having to tread carefully over the slippery rocks. And before she knew it, she was up to her waist in the water, but Singsing was still paddling forward.
      "Where are you going?" Ruby asked in exasperation as she made another attempt to snatch up the puppy. It was a good thing the water was warm.
      Suddenly, a pair of hands reached up from the water. They carefully closed around Singsing, and Ruby looked on in shock as a boy around her age emerged from the waves with Singsing safely cradled in his sun-kissed arms.
      "I-" Ruby just stared at him. She must have been so focused on catching Singsing that she hadn't noticed the boy at all. Judging from his bare chest, he must have been swimming in the water and caught Singsing's attention.
      The boy just smiled and held Singsing out to Ruby.
      Ruby stared before finally snapping back to reality and took the puppy from him. The most curious thing about the boy was how his long hair was the color of sea-glass. But then Ruby almost let out a laugh. What was so curious about his hair color when she had dyed her own hair deep red?
      "Thank you," Ruby said gratefully.
      The boy just blinked at Ruby before he shook his head.
      "You don't speak English?"
      The boy just looked at Ruby blankly.
      Singsing was still in her arms, so with some difficulty, Ruby pressed her hands together in a gesture of gratitude as she bowed her head.
      This time the boy seemed to get what she was trying to say and offered Ruby a smile. Then he raised an arm and pointed first to Ruby and then to the sandy beach behind her.
      Ruby turned to look over her shoulder. The boy seemed to be telling her to go back to the shore. Ruby nodded her head and took a step back, but she paused when the boy himself didn't move.
      The boy's sea-glass hair was plastered to his brown skin as he shook his head. He pointed to Ruby again, then pointed at the beach. He pointed at himself and shook his head.
      He wanted Ruby to go back to the beach. But the boy himself wasn't going to go back. Maybe Ruby had interrupted his swim and he planned to keep going until he reached his destination. After offering him a smile, Ruby lifted a hand in farewell as she took another step toward the shore.
      The boy raised one of his own hands before gesturing again for Ruby to go back to the beach.
      Turning, Ruby carefully waded back through the water. When she reached the powdery sands of the beach, she set Singsing down and threw her hands in front of her face as the puppy shook out her white coat.
      "You swam all the way out there for a swimmer?" Ruby asked with a sigh. "I've never seen you get this worked up before."
      Singsing just let out a whine as she stared out at the water. Ruby turned to follow the puppy's gaze to find that the boy had vanished.
      If Ruby was going off the boy's appearance alone, he looked like he could be a local. If she ever saw him while she was off exploring the island, she'd make sure to wave.
      "Do you think he's who I noticed the other day?" Ruby wondered aloud as she made her way back to the house. She had one hand holding her flip flops, and the other was in her windswept hair. "Maybe it was someone swimming in very reflective swimwear?"
      When Ruby arrived at the house, she quickly rinsed the sand from her feet with the spout by the back door before hurrying inside to change her clothes. Even though it was a warm afternoon, Ruby was beginning to feel the bite of the wind through the waterlogged fabric of her shorts.
      After she changed, Ruby made sure Singsing was comfortably asleep in the living room before heading outside to take a bike ride to the shopping center. She relished the way the wind kissed her face and set her hair flying out from beneath her helmet as she peddled down the road.
      Ruby arrived at the shopping. Instead of buying lunch like she had the previous day, this time after Ruby parked her bike, she spent time going from shop to shop to pick out some small souvenirs for her friends. But before she had picked out something for all of them, Ruby found herself getting sidetracked by all the fun little things the stores had to show.
      In the end, Ruby ended up spending hours trying on clothing and looking through baskets of refrigerator magnets. When she was finally satisfied with her selection of souvenirs, Ruby returned to her bike. Even after all that looking, she really hadn't bought much of anything.
      The sun was beginning to set, and the brilliant blue of the sky faded into shades of deep pink and orange before finally touching on an even darker purple. Ruby walked her bike down the sidewalk. Being here in Hawaii . . . it really did feel like summer.
      Even the nights here on the island felt different. The night was clearer, and there were stars glittering in the sky. Ruby inhaled, and the warm night air filled her lungs. The air itself felt cleaner.
      By the time Ruby returned to the house, her parents' rental car was back in the driveway. She entered the house to find the two of them sitting at the dining room table finishing their dinners.
      "Have you eaten yet?" Ruby's mom asked as she looked up at her daughter. "Your dad and I got take-out on the way back from his conference. It's on the kitchen counter."
      Ruby made her way to the kitchen and dished herself out a plate of food. But by the time she returned to the dining room table, her parents had already finished and left the table.
      Ruby ate her dinner alone. When she was done, she washed her plate and then made her way upstairs. After setting the bag of items she had bought on the desk in her room, Ruby rummaged through it for the small item she had bought for herself. It was a small bottle of turquoise nail polish. The color had reminded Ruby of the ocean.
      Ruby took a seat on the floor. She painted her toes first and then skillfully did her fingers. When she finished, she made her way to the desk, blowing lightly on her nails as she gazed out the window at the night sky. Once her nails dried, she would write another letter, and in this one, she would talk about the boy who had helped her catch Singsing. Meeting the boy had definitely been the most interesting thing that had happened all week.

	Ruby awoke to the sound of raised voices arguing downstairs. After rolling out of bed, Ruby made her way to the staircase to listen to what the fuss was about.
	"The nerve of him!" Ruby's dad as saying angrily in Mandarin. "Stevenson claimed that he couldn't make it to the meeting because his flight was delayed, but apparently he arrived on the island two days ago! Our conference has been postponed because of him! Who does he think he is?"
	"Calm down," Ruby's mom replied in Cantonese. "You know what kind of character Mr. Stevenson is. Ever since he joined the company, he has been competing against you. He's trying to make your life difficult. Don't let him do that."
	"He doesn't care about the company. If he's promoted, all the hard work we've put in over the years will go down the drain!"
	Ruby's mom sighed. "You just need to prove to the higher-ups that you're more dedicated to the company than he is. Anyone can see it."
	"The conference starts in two days." Ruby's dad seemed to deflate. "Stevenson couldn't have shown up late without a reason. I've always been suspicious of that man. He can't be up to anything good. You don't know him the way I do. He doesn't like me. And he makes that point very clear. He makes fun of me, and what am I supposed to do about it? I put up with it. I've been putting up with him for too long now."
	"If he's really that horrible, why hasn't he been fired yet?"
	"Oh, he knows how to put on a good act in front of the higher-ups alright. They all think he's brilliant."
	So it was Mr. Stevenson they were talking about. Ruby had heard the name come up before during discussions back at home, and whenever Ruby's dad was talking about his co-worker, his expression was always sour. From the way he ranted about him, Ruby hoped she wouldn't have to deal with someone like Mr. Stevenson for a very long time.
	"Ruby," Ruby's dad called as he seemed to realize that Ruby was lurking by the staircase.
	"Are you off to talk to your co-workers again?" Ruby asked as she made her way into the living room to join them.
	Ruby's dad nodded. "I'm leaving again in half an hour or so. This was supposed to be a fun family vacation for us. I'm sorry the conference isn't over yet."
	Ruby nodded and took a seat at the dining room table.
	Ruby's mom walked over to stand next to her daughter. "Your dad and I have decided to give you your phone back. We only wanted the best for you, but we've come to realize that both sides are at fault, not just you, Ruby. There was a lack of communication."
	Ruby just stared in surprise as her mom set her phone down on the table. Ruby continued to stare at it for a long moment before reaching to pick it up. She gingerly pressed the power button, but the phone's screen remained dark. The battery was completely drained.
	Suddenly, the sound of a phone ringing cut through the air. Ruby turned to watch her dad pick up his phone from where he had left it on the kitchen counter. "I've got to take this." He sighed, and the glow from the screen illuminated his face. "Ruby, go on and eat without me. Hello? Yes, that's me. Who's calling?"
	Ruby turned back to the table and the dead phone in front of her. They were right-there had always been a lack of communication. When Tilden had left, it had also been due to a lack of communication. Ruby just hoped that they'd come to understand that Tilden would rather live his best life as a poor musician than wondering from some office what he could have been if he pursued his path in music.
	Ruby's dad returned with a crease between his brows. "I've got to head out early. I'll take all of us out to dinner tonight, how about it?"
	Ruby nodded as she watched her dad quickly tug on his polished shoes and grab his coat from the coat rack. Ruby's mom followed him, and now alone in the house, Ruby finished her breakfast in silence before heading upstairs to find a charger. After plugging in her phone, instead of waiting around, Ruby woke up Singsing. They'd go down to the beach again. And maybe if they were lucky, they'd see the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair.
	Ruby trudged down to the beach and slid off her flip-flops the moment she reached the powdery sands. The ocean glittered with shades of blue and green, and the wind filled Ruby's vision with flashes of her own deep-red hair as it whipped around her face.
	Suddenly, Singsing barked and took off down the stretch of beach at a run.
	"Woah!" Ruby hurried after the puppy. "Slow down, girl!" But even with that said, Ruby couldn't help but feel excited. Had Singsing sensed the presence of that boy again?
	Ruby followed Singsing down the beach. The ocean waves creeped close and then fell back with the tide as she splashed barefoot through the shallow waters. Finally, Singsing came to a stop. Ruby dropped to her knees in the sand, clutching a stitch in her side as she gasped for breath. She wasn't sure how long she had been running, but when she turned her head to look back, the line of houses that bordered the sand had completely vanished.
	Frowning, Ruby turned back to the ocean only to find that Singsing was barking at something in the water's midsts.
	"Do you want me to go in there?" Ruby asked when she had finally caught her breath. "Are you sure? Something doesn't look right about that patch of water." It was true-while the surrounding ocean was a deep turquoise in color, the section in front of her was a murky green. It was almost as if a film of algae had covered the surface, blocking the sun's rays from reaching the ocean floor.
	Singsing barked at the water again, jumping around as if she could scare the water away.
	Sighing, Ruby wadded out into the water. Her skin prickled at how the dead bits of algae clung to her bare legs. The water here was still-still in a way Ruby couldn't quite put her finger on.
	Turning back around to face the beach, Ruby looked up at the rocky slope above it. There had to be some sort of farm up there. Human activity-especially the run-off from farmland into water could cause a explosion of algae. And when there were that much algae covering the surface of the water, the life that relied on the sun was starved.
	Suddenly Singsing was barking again and running back down the beach.
	"Singsing!" Ruby called in exasperation as she splashed out of the water and back to the sands of the beach. "A warning! Please!"
	Glancing back over her shoulder at the rocky slope, Ruby took note of its location. She'd be back here once she was able to calm down her dog.

~

	That night, Ruby sat at the table across from her parents. Her dad had been in a foul mood ever since he had returned to the house, and he had taken a few hours to finally cool off. Now in the restaurant, Ruby could still feel the tenseness in the air between them as they sat in silence, waiting for their food to arrive.
	"Are you still thinking about Mr. Stevenson?" Ruby asked in an attempt to break the silence. "How bad would it be if he gets the promotion instead of you?"
	Her dad's gaze darkened. "He'll do everything he can to get me fired. Hell, he's already doing everything he can to get me fired." Ruby's mom placed a hand on her husband's arm as he continued. "Who does he think he is? He's not even a San Francisco local! His main argument is that if I get promoted to CEO, my face will look bad when we start advertising. In front of me, he's openly racist in the things he says trying to get under my skin. I don't let myself lose my cool in front of him, but he knows very well if he just continues on the way he is, who knows-maybe I'll snap eventually."
	Ruby wrinkled her nose in disgust.
	Her dad clasped his hands together on the table in front of him as he went on, "He sees that we're a steadily growing company and wants it for himself. Out of all my friends there, I'm the only person of color. Stevenson seems to think I'm an easy target because of it. But if he thinks it will be easy for me to lose face, he'd better think again!"
	Ruby nodded in agreement, but before she could open her mouth to add on, their food arrived.
	"Let's leave it here for tonight." Ruby's dad sighed as he pulled his plate toward him. "I don't want to think about Stevenson right now. Let's talk about something else, shall we?"
	"How's the beach, Ruby?" Ruby's mom leaned forward. "Your dad and I haven't been down there yet, but from what we can see from outside the window, it looks lovely."
	Ruby nodded. "It is quite lovely. Singsing certainly likes it there-I've been taking her down to the water for walks every day."

~

	After they finished their dinner, Ruby and her parents walked back to the house from the restaurant. When they arrived at the house, Ruby's mom fumbled for the keys, but Ruby placed a hand on her arm and smiled as she led the two of them past the house and down to the beach.
	Standing there on the stretch of sand, Ruby watched her parents' faces as they gazed out over the water in awe. The sky was painted with streaks of orange and purple, and the sun was slowly sinking into the turquoise waves.
	Ruby grinned. "So, what do you think?"
	"It's beautiful," her dad breathed as he took a deep breath of the island air. "Now this is what a vacation should be like-relaxing and enjoyable."
	Smiling to herself, Ruby stood next to her parents, and the three of them watched as the sky faded to a star-flecked night.
