tyedyemaster_2000: It was a lucky guess.

Tomas Quevedo: I'm just so confused. What even are feelings?

tyedyemaster_2000: As much as I want to say that you've come to the right person, I'm not sure how much I can actually help you.

Tomas Quevedo: I guess you don't have the answers to every problem then.

tyedyemaster_2000: Of course I don't. I'm not a god. I'm just an overworked high schooler.

Tomas Quevedo: Don't take so many classes, Tye. Give yourself a break.

tyedyemaster_2000: I might not have an answer right now, but I do happen to be very good at brainstorming. How do you feel when you're around Mari?

Tomas Quevedo: I feel like I all I want is to see her happy.

tyedyemaster_2000: Yup. Sounds to me like you're in love.

    Chapter 9

	Aouli wasn't sure whether he should tell his sister about what was going on in the dead zone. Seeing the ocean like that already sickened him. The ocean was supposed to be a place full of life-not death and emptiness.
	When Aouli had gone down to the dead zone the previous day, he had noted how the highest concentration of emptiness was in the sections closest to the shore. Whatever was causing the dead zone was coming from the land. But with that being the case, that meant there was nothing he could do about it. His investigations ended at the beach.	
      His father claimed that he would speak with the humans, but Aouli got the feeling that his father would rather silently hope that the problem would resolve itself instead.
	Maybe this called for another visit to the so-called sea witch. If anyone could do something about the dead zone, it would have to be her. Aouli wasn't entirely sure what exactly the extent of Ulani's abilities were, but something told him they went beyond just making medicine. If there was a way she could heal the ocean-wouldn't that be perfect?
	Aouli swam through the clear waters of the village, navigating between fish and bright coral as he rushed toward Ulani's cave. "Aouli!" The village children swam over to him. "Where are you off to in such a hurry?"
	"I'm off to see my friend," Aouli explained.
	"The sea witch?" one of the children piped up.
	Aouli sighed. "I'll play with you all later. I've got important work I need to do."
	"You haven't played with us in a few days," the children said disappointedly.
	"Once my sister becomes the high chief, I'll be able to relax and come out here more."
	Finally breaking away from them, Aouli slowed down once he reached Ulani's cave. The sign in front of the entrance read "closed," and Aouli frowned. He swam back and forth in front of the entrance for a long moment before finally calling out, "Ulani? Are you here?"
	"Aouli!" Ulani's voice echoed out from the depths of the cave. "Are you here to pay me a visit? Come in!"
	Aouli quickly swam inside to find Ulani mixing a cauldron full of clear liquid. The cauldron itself was perched on a pile of rocks, elevated out of the surrounding water that filled the cave.
	"You seem to have swam here in a hurry," Ulani said lightly as she swiveled to face Aouli. Her hair flowed out around her as she slid off her rocky perch and entered the water.
	"Do you know about the dead zone?" Aouli asked. "Is that why you sent me in that direction the last time I came to see you?"
	Ulani blinked. "Dead zone? This is the first time I'm hearing of any dead zone."
	"Are you sure?"
	Ulani just nodded her head.
	"This one is less than an hour's swim out from the village. Generations have lived in this village-this is our home. I don't want our home to become like that."
	"And what do you propose to do about it?" Ulani angled her head to the side, and her milky eyes watched Aouli's.
	"That's why I came to you, actually. I was wondering if you had some sort of way to bring back the life-to restore the ocean."
	Ulani folded her arms over her chest. "I can't just magic the ocean back to life. You're thinking too highly of me. If you really want to prevent the dead zone from spreading, you're going have to figure out what's causing it-get to the source of the problem and fix it."
	Aouli shook his head in discouragement. "Whatever's causing the problem is coming from on land."
	"So then what do you propose?"
	"What about that human girl?" Aouli said suddenly. "What if I can find a way to ask her to investigate?"
	"Ask the humans?" Ulani pressed her hands to her mouth as she lowered her voice. "Are you sure that's a good idea?"
	"I-" Aouli started, but then he trailed off.
	"If you really want to do something about it," Ulani said slowly, "there is a little something I could do."
	"What is it?"
	"I could turn you into a human and let you investigate on land."
	Aouli just stared blankly at Ulani. "Turn me . . . into a human?"
	Ulani smiled. "It would only last about three days give or take. That should be enough time for you to find out what's causing the dead zone and stop it, right?"
	"There has to be a better plan than that."
	"You just don't want to be a human," Ulani observed. "But maybe once you're a human, that girl on the beach can help you with the rest."
	Aouli opened his mouth to reply, but then he frowned. "Wait, I don't remember ever telling you about the girl on the beach."
	"Healani stopped by."
	"My sister stopped by?"
	"She came to tell me to look out for you." Ulani swam a circle around Aouli before returning to the thick liquid she had been mixing in her cauldron. "She wants you to be careful around the beach and the humans."
	"Then isn't that even more of a reason not to become one myself?"
	Ulani just motioned for Aouli to take a seat on the rocks next to her. Aouli hesitantly swam over, and his hair stuck to his head and neck as he broke through the water's surface.
	"Want some?" Ulani asked as she used a ladle to spoon the liquid from the cauldron into a bowl.
	Aouli looked at the bowl. "What is it, may I ask?"
	"It's soup," Ulani said matter of factly. "I was planning to make it for the village children, but then I remembered that they want nothing to do with me."
	"I'll have a bowl." Aouli reached out, and Ulani placed the bowl in his upturned palm.
	"This is nice." Ulani said as she swished her tail through the water. "The two of us together here just like old days."
	"You don't need to stay in your cave all day, you know. You could go to the reef. There normally isn't anyone there."
	"If you were to go with me, maybe I'd consider it."
	"What's the cost?" Aouli set his now empty bowl down on the rocks next to him. "If I became a human, what would the cost be? You always are sure to name your prices."
	Ulani offered Aouli a smile. "You're my friend. I'll give this one to you for free. Besides, this is my home too. I don't want to see the ocean slowly die. But," Ulani paused, "if you do decide you want to become human, I have to ask for something from you to complete the transformation process."
	"And what's that?" Aouli asked slowly.
	"Your hair," Ulani said simply.
	"My hair?" Aouli absently lifted a hand and ran it through his long hair. It was a custom in the village that the only time hair was cut was during times of war with other villages-which Aouli was proud to say hadn't happened in decades.
	At this point, Aouli wasn't sure he could even do anything even if he became a human for three days. What could he even do in three days? Maybe it would be better to try and get a human on their side to help.
	The girl on the beach was there every morning, and Aouli had even met her face to face. Aouli wasn't sure whether the girl had realized he wasn't a human. In fact, Aouli wasn't sure why he had shown himself to the girl. But the fuzzy white animal that swam out into the water in the first place . . . it had led the girl to him. Maybe he had met the girl for a reason.
	"Aouli?" Ulani asked. "You seem like you're thinking very hard about something."
	"I'm going to talk to the human girl," Aouli said as he met Ulani's gaze.
	"My offer still stands if you change your mind." Ulani shrugged lightly before taking Aouli's bowl and placing it on a growing pile of other used dishes. "If you need anything-anything at all-just ask me." Ulani slid off the rocks and back into the water. "You should go. Find that human girl, restore the dead zone, and return as the protector of our village."
	"You make it sound easy." Aouli joined Ulani beneath the surface, and his hair billowed out around him as he turned to look at the light at the end of the tunnel. "It's dark in here. I'll take you sunbathing some time, how about it?"
	"I'll be here waiting for you."

~

	The next morning, Aouli was out at the beach, scanning the sands from a distance. And then there was the girl walking down to the water with the same small animal accompanying her.
	Aouli quickly swam forward, cutting through the clear waters. The small white animal at the girl's feet was barking at him again. He stuck his head out of the water, and the girl's eyes widen in surprise as they fell on him.
	Aouli offered what he hoped was a friendly smile as he waved at the girl.
	The girl waved back.
	Aouli pointed to a stop further down the beach and motioned for the girl to follow him there. He wasn't sure if the girl understood what he was trying to convey, but he sunk back down under the water and swam in the direction of the rocks.
	When he stuck his head out of the water again, he found to his relief that the girl was following his movements on the beach. As he waited for the girl to arrive, Aouli leaped out of the water and took a seat on one of the rocks. The scales of his tale glittered in the sunlight, and his sea-glass-colored hair was plastered to his body.
	The girl appeared around the corner, and her mouth fell open in shock as her eyes fell on his tail. She blinked, once, twice.
	Aouli just slid back into the water and motioned for the girl to follow him again. He wasn't sure how much time had passed when they finally reached the dead zone, but the sun had shifted in the sky, and the humid air was even warmer than before. Stopping just outside the dead zone, Aouli lifted his head out of the water again and pointed at the lifeless stretch in front of them.
	The girl on the beach looked from Aouli to the dead zone and then back again. She nodded her head quickly. She had seen it before.
	Aouli gestured to the cliff-like slope just off of the beach and pointed up. The girl followed his finger and raised her head to look up at the slope. She turned back to Aouli, and her eyes were wide in a silent question.
	Aouli lifted his tail out of the water and motioned to himself in a way he hoped conveyed that he couldn't go onto the land. Then he pointed to the girl and pointed to the slope.
	Her eyes were still wide, but the girl nodded her head. She turned to the slope and felt around on the rocks before she finally found a spot where she could climb up. Aouli watched from the water as she scaled the rocky wall. She eventually reached the top and disappeared from sight.
	As he waited, Aouli swam closer to the shore. The small white animal that had been trailing after the girl was staring at him in confusion. Aouli just stared back. He had never seen such an animal before, but there were a lot of things about the human world he didn't know. All he knew about the humans was that they occupied the lands in the same way the people of the sea occupied the waters.
	Aouli let out a sigh, but then he blinked as the small white animal on the beach hurried into the water and began paddling toward him. Judging from its tiny limbs, it certainly wasn't fit for swimming.
	After swimming over to the small animal, Aouli picked it up and returned to his rock to set the animal down next to him. The animal just stared up at him for a long moment before shaking its furry coat. Water droplets sprayed everywhere, and a laugh escaped Aouli as he threw his arms up in front of his face.
	After some waiting, the red-haired girl finally reappeared and climbed back down the rocky slope. Aouli quickly swam over to her with her little white animal safely in his arms.
	The girl just shook her head in defeat. The girl took a seat on the sand, deep in thought. She was frowning, and her brows were knitted together.
	The girl rose to her feet, gestured to Aouli, and pointed to the shimmering ocean.
      Aouli just blinked at her in confusion.
      The girl tried again by pointing to herself and then to the slope. Then she pointed to Aouli and the beach. Aouli slowly nodded his head. Was the girl trying to tell him that she'd keep looking on her own?
      Still slightly confused, Aouli set the white animal down on the sand before sinking back under the water and swimming a few paces away. He popped his head back out of the water and looked at the girl again.
      The girl just nodded her head as she motioned for Aouli to swim even further.
      Sighing, Aouli turned and swam off. He'd trust the girl. Maybe if he was very lucky, she'd end up solving the problem for him. But . . . there had been something about her expression when she had sat on the sand, staring out over the ocean deep in thought that stuck with Aouli. It was the expression of someone who had just discovered something they didn't like.
      Aouli swam aimlessly through the water and found himself at a small cluster of rocks far away from the land. When he was not exploring the oceans, this was where he liked to spend his time, sitting on the rocks under the sun. This was the place he offered to take Ulani if she was willing to come with him.
	Ulani. That was right, now that the human girl was helping him, he wouldn't need to take on her offer. Taking a deep breath of the humid air, Aouli tipped his head back and let the warmth of the sun beat down on his face. Everything was going to work out.


    Chapter 9.5

      Dear Tilden, 

      First off, how are you doing? I hope you have been able to find some time to relax, even though I know you well enough to assume that you've probably signed up for all the summer classes you could fit in a day.
      It's been a while since I've written letters by hand. Don't laugh! Can't you tell that I've been working on my handwriting? Anyway, you don't have to worry about me. Ba and Ma don't have me grounded anymore, and I have plenty of free time to wander. They've given me my phone back, but I wanted to write this one final letter. So how do I put this? Some things are better said on paper. But of course I'm going to text this to you too anyway-I'll have long returned home by the time this letter will even get to you.
      I'm still angry at our parents for dragging me to Ba's business meeting in Hawaii without any input, but all that initial frustration has subsided now, because guess what? This is a summer I'll never forget! I've been spending all my time outside on the beaches, and you'll never believe who I met.
      I met a merman.

      I hope you'll visit us back in San Francisco soon. I want to tell you everything in person.
      Your sister, Ruby

      P.S.
      Singsing is a puppy, not a replacement sibling. Ba and Ma still love you.

      P.P.S
      Who is San???!!!

    Chapter 10

      Zooming down the road on her bike, Ruby found herself repeatedly looking over her shoulder. The crystal-like waters glittered in the afternoon sunlight. She still couldn't believe what she had seen. The boy she had met the other day . . . He was a-a merman?
      Ruby let out a laugh as the wind continued to beat at her face. She couldn't believe it. But he had been there right in front of her. She couldn't have been dreaming. Her knees were still covered in scrapes from when she had climbed the slope.
      She wasn't sure what had come over her to climb up there, but the merman had been asking her-her!-for help. She couldn't just stand back and do nothing. Besides, she had been wondering about the dead zone herself. And what Ruby had seen . . . her prediction had been right. There was indeed farmland up there. It wasn't particularly close to the cliff, but she could see it very clearly in the distance. There must have been pipes somewhere . . . pipes transporting contaminated water and sediment into the ocean.
      After coming to a stop at the side of the road, Ruby pulled out her phone and quickly brought up a map. Even though she was heading in the general direction of the farm, from the land, she didn't know its exact location.
      Squinting against the glare of the sun, Ruby looked over the map for a good minute before finally finding the location of the farm. It was a sugar farm. Hopping back on her bike, Ruby continued to peddle down the road.
      When she reached the main building of the farm, Ruby gingerly climbed off her bike. Now that she was here, she wasn't quite sure what to do. As she paced back and forth outside the entrance, debating what her next move would be, Ruby suddenly heard the sound of a car pulling to a stop in front of the farm's main building. Ruby whirled around to watch a middle-aged man climb out of the car. The man's eyes immediately fell on her, and Ruby just stared at him for a long moment before she hurried forward. "Sir"-Ruby looked up at him-"do you work here?"
      The man frowned distastefully. "What if I do?"
      "Do you know that the way you're farming right now is harming the ocean?" Ruby asked quickly. "There's a dead zone not that far from-"
      "This is none of your business, girl." The man cut Ruby off. "Now leave before I call the cops on you."
      Ruby just stared at him as he turned and walked over to the building's doors. He typed in a code, and the doors swung open. The man disappeared inside the building without a backward glance.
      Frowning, Ruby shuffled back over to her bike. She'd come here again later. She needed a more solid plan anyway.
      When Ruby arrived back home, she found her parents waiting for her.
      "Ruby." Ruby's dad stood up from where he had been sitting at the dining room table. "Remember how I asked you to pack a nice outfit for special occasions? Our company is holding a dinner tonight," he explained. "Everyone's families are invited, and it's a time to eat good food and socialize. All three of us should go tonight."
      "What time? I'll go get ready."
      "The dinner is at seven o'clock," Ruby's mom answered. "At least take a shower before we leave."
      Ruby nodded as she made her way past her parents and climbed the stairs to her room. Crouching down next to her suitcase, Ruby carefully lifted out the dress she had packed. It was a pale golden-yellow in color with thin straps that crisscrossed over the back. It was also one of those dresses that took Ruby forever to differentiate the arm holes from the head one once she pulled it over her head.
      Ruby sat down at her desk and pulled a piece of lined paper toward her. She set her phone down next to it and slowly but surely began to sketch a map. She copied the little lines that made up the streets and roads from her phone, but once she got to the farm, she closed her eyes. She recalled how the main building and the fields of sugar cane looked.
      When she was done, Ruby sat back to admire her work. Then leaving the map on her desk, Ruby made her way to the bathroom. She'd do what her mother had wanted her to and take a shower.
      
~

	That night, Ruby sat next to her mom. Her dad's company had rented out an entire restaurant for the night, and the employees and their families were happily mingling as they waited for everyone to arrive.
	Ruby sat there, talking to her dad's co-workers whenever they came over to compliment her on her hair and dress. Ruby was in the middle of a conversation with one of them about college options when something caught her eye. A man with thinning hair and hazy-blue eyes had just entered the restaurant.
	Ruby inhaled sharply. It was the same man who had threatened her to leave the farm's premises. He seemed to notice her watching him because he turned his head, his eyes narrowing as they fell on her. Ruby refused to back down from his gaze, and he finally turned away.
	"That's Mr. Stevenson," Ruby's dad said darkly as he followed Ruby's gaze.
	"That's Mr. Stevenson? Ba," Ruby said quietly as she got over her surprise. "When we get back to the house, I have something to tell you. It has something to do with Mr. Stevenson."
	Ruby's dad turned to her. His brows were raised in a silent question. Ruby just shook her head. She'd tell him later.
	Ruby found herself much quieter than usual as she sat through dinner. The food was good, but she found her mind drifting when she had finished eating. Did her dad know about the contaminated water?
	Even in her spaced-out state, Ruby almost felt as if someone was watching her. But when she looked around, everyone was busy either chatting with each other or finishing up their meals. Ruby frowned to herself, trying her best to ignore the prickling sensation that seemed to tingle down her spine.
	Ruby pulled out her phone and tried to distract herself by reading through her group chat and catching up with old messages. When she had unplugged her phone the other day from the charger, the first thing she noticed when the screen flickered to life was the notification informing her that she had over a hundred unread messages. That was to be expected, but it had given Ruby a momentary shock nonetheless.
	"Ruby," her mom hissed, and Ruby reluctantly put her phone away. The feeling of the eyes on the back of her head returned. What started out as a good dinner had turned into something she hoped would end as quickly as possible.
	When it was finally time to head back to the house, Ruby climbed into the back seats of the rental car, glad to be out of the restaurant. As they drove, Ruby looked at her dad's face reflected in the rearview mirror.
	"Did either of you get the feeling that we were being watched?" Ruby asked quietly.
	"Watched?" Ruby's mom swiveled around from the passenger seat. "Watched by who?"
	"I don't know who it was," Ruby admitted. "But I could have sworn someone was watching me."
	"It must be that hair of yours," Ruby's mom said as she turned back around. "Of course it's going to attract attention."
	Ruby fell silent. Back at school, it was true that her red hair had turned many heads, but she had never gotten that sense of hostility that she had tonight. Ruby clasped her hands together tightly on her lap as she looked out the window, watching the stars in the night through the reflection of her own face.
	Once they arrived back at the house, Ruby followed her parents through the front door. "Ba," Ruby started. "I've got a few things I'd like to ask you."
	Her dad blinked. "What is it?"
	"Your company has farmland on this island, right?"
	"That's correct."
	"Is it the sugar farm about a half an hour's bike ride from here?"
	"I'm not sure how long it takes to bike to it, but that sounds like it could be possible."
	"I went there the other day," Ruby explained, watching her dad's face. "I saw Mr. Stevenson there."
	"Mr. Stevenson?" Her dad asked quickly. Now Ruby had his full attention. "What was he doing there?"
	Ruby angled her head to the side. "Was he not supposed to be there?"
	"No. We're only allowed to check it out on the weekend, and he only arrived on the island earlier this week."
	"He went inside the main building," Ruby continued. "He saw me there and told me to leave. I don't know what he did after he disappeared."
	"What is he up to this time?" Ruby's dad muttered darkly, more to himself than to his daughter.
	"Also," Ruby said slowly, "I think there's a problem with the farm."
	"A problem with the farm?"
	"Well, not with the farm itself, but the runoff from the farm is contaminating the water-it's contaminating the ocean."
	"I didn't know about this." Ruby's dad looked worried, and a crease formed between his brows. "Do you have evidence? Do you have pictures?"
	"I don't yet, but I can take some pictures when I go down to the beach tomorrow."
	"Send them to me. I'll talk to the higher-ups. When we bought the farmland, we had all promised that we would be careful and not harm the surrounding environment."
	Ruby let out a breath of relief. It looked like her dad was on her side after all.

~

	Ruby sat on her bed with the lights on dim as she scrolled through the messages on her phone. In the beginning, there had been a number of messages directed to her both in the group chat and in private ones, but once her friends realized that she wasn't getting her phone back, they had gone back to chatting with each other instead.
	As for the most recent messages, it looked as if Mari was back online-though not as much as she used to be-and Ruby was saddened to see that Grace had injured herself.
	Ruby looked at her phone for a long moment before typing, Hi everyone, I felt like I was being watched by some unknown person today. What should I do?
	Ruby stared at the message for another long moment before pressing the delete button. She replaced the message with, I've got my phone back! I've missed you guys! After hitting the send button, Ruby let out a sigh. She set her phone down and stared up at the ceiling.
	
~

	When Ruby left the house with Singsing the following morning, she immediately felt a prickle down her spine. The eyes were back.
      Ruby casually scanned the area around the house so as to not alert whoever was watching her, but again, there was no one there.
      Singsing let out a whimper, and Ruby looked down at the puppy. Singsing seemed to be more on edge as well. It felt reassuring that Ruby wasn't the only one who had sensed something was off, but also worrisome that the feeling wasn't just in her head.
      Instead of walking around the side of the house to the beach, Ruby began to walk down the main road to the shopping center instead. The eyes followed. If she really was being followed, the last thing she'd do would be to lead whoever was following her to the merman.
      Pulling out her phone, Ruby pretend to be adjusting her hair as she used the camera as a mirror to examine the street behind her. There-there nearly halfway down the block was a man she had never seen before.
      After walking for another ten minutes down a zigzag of different streets, Ruby pulled out her phone again and pretended to look at her hair for a second time. The man was still there. Ruby quickly snapped a picture of him in her selfie camera before tucking her phone away.
      On her way back to the house, Ruby made sure to go down all the streets that had at least a few other people walking down them. Ruby was really starting to get creeped out now. Should she submit the picture she had taken to the police? But it was a blurry picture, and no matter how much she zoomed in on the image, she couldn't make out the man's face.
      Ruby quickened her pace as she returned to the house. Once she was inside, Ruby hurried over to the windows to carefully look outside. The man had vanished.
      Ruby placed a hand over her heart to find it beating a little too quickly. She was alone in the house now, and all she could do was lock the doors. But it seemed as if the man had no interest in following her inside.
      After hurrying upstairs to her parent's bedroom, Ruby looked out at the road to see the man disappear down the street. He was gone. For now.
      Letting out a breath, Ruby hurried back downstairs. She made sure Singsing was alright by herself before hurrying to the front door. Ruby paused with her hand hovering over the handle. She turned and hurried instead to the back door that lead straight to the beach.
      The wind hit Ruby in the face the moment she exited the house, and she hurried down the gentle slope to the beach. At the water's edge, Ruby scanned the waves for any sign of the merman. Something shiny caught her attention, and her gaze fell on the merman as he waved to her from the water.
      Ruby felt her face melt into a relieved smile as she waved back and quickly hurried over to him. The merman pointed in the direction of the dead zone when Ruby reached him. Ruby let out a sigh, and her smile faded as she shook her head. She tried to gesture that she needed some more time to investigate, but gave up when the merman just looked at her in confusion.
	Motioning for the merman to follow her instead, Ruby jogged down the beach, away from the houses and main road. Once she was sure she was hidden from the sight, Ruby crouched down and drew in the sand with her finger.
	The merman swam over and angled his head to the side as he tried to make sense of the crudely drawn map. Then Ruby almost let out a laugh. What was she doing? Reaching into her back pocket, Ruby pulled out her phone and opened a digital map. She had gone for so long without her phone that she had completely forgotten about it.
	Ruby waded out into the water, and she stood next to the merman to show him the glowing screen of her phone. With her free hand, she did her best to shield it from the glare of the sun.
	The merman just stared at the phone for a long moment as if he couldn't believe what he was seeing. Ruby brought up a map of the road and showed the merman the main building of the farm. Ruby pointed to it and then pointed in the direction of the dead zone.
	The merman slowly nodded his head. So far he seemed to be following.
	Ruby pointed to herself again and made a gesture with her fingers that mimicked walking. I went there, was the message she was hoping to get through. Ruby zoomed in on the picture of the main building and pointed to the tall fence that surrounded the farmland.
	The merman nodded again, quicker this time.
	Ruby sighed as she pocketed her phone. The turquoise water lapped against her knees. That was right-Ruby suddenly remembered. Her dad wanted her to take pictures of the dead zone.
	Ruby pointed in the direction of the dead zone. The merman nodded and swam parallel to Ruby as the two of them made their way further from the houses.
	When they arrived at the dead zone, Ruby made sure to take a number of pictures. She even dipped her hand into the water to take a picture of how much algae her fingers picked up. Ruby showed these pictures to the merman. The merman looking on, impressed.
	After spending a while trying to explain what her plan was, Ruby was now making her way back down the beach. As she walked, Ruby sent the picture she had taken earlier of the man who had been following her to the group chat along with a message asking for advice. Maybe they'd have some ideas of what she should do.
	Stopping at the back door to the house, Ruby carefully looked around to check for anyone who might be hanging out in the area. Once she determined that there wasn't anyone there, Ruby quickly unlocked the door and stepped inside. After quickly closing and locking the door behind her, Ruby climbed the stairs to her room.
	When she reached her room, Ruby turned to look out the window, gazing out at the ocean. She was in Maui. She didn't know anyone here except for her parents. Who would try and follow her? What would they get out of following her? Had she merely caught the attention of some creep, or was there more to it? The only other person she had run into on the island was Mr. Stevenson. Ruby didn't want to jump to conclusions, but could it have been Mr. Stevenson watching her?
	No. The build of the man following her had been different than Mr. Stevenson's. She could tell that much of a distance. But what if Mr. Stevenson had sent that man?
	Ruby pulled out her phone to find a flood of concerned messages from her friends. All of them came to the conclusion that she should get the police involved if she saw the man again. Sighing heavily, Ruby collapsed onto her bed. This was not how she had expected this trip to go. Not in the slightest.

~

	For the next couple of days, Ruby was on high alert for anyone who might be watching her, but to her relief, she found no one. Heading out the back door with Singsing at her heels, Ruby made her way down to the beach. She had sent the pictures she had taken of the dead zone to her dad, and he had taken one look at them before declaring that he would bring it to the attention of the higher-ups.
	With her dad now working on the issue, Ruby felt as if she could finally start to relax again. Walking down the beach, Ruby reached her hands into the air, stretching as the wind whipped her hair around her face. It had been some time since Grace had helped her dye it, and after a number of washes, Ruby could see that the color was starting to fade, if only slightly.
	Ruby was to meet the merman further down the beach, away from the houses. Ever since that man had trailed Ruby, Ruby had made sure that she changed her meeting spot with the merman.
	Suddenly, a bark from Singsing drew Ruby from her thoughts.
      "What is it, girl?" Ruby asked as she followed Singsing's gaze to the ocean. There was nothing there save for a small fishing boat bobbing gently in the distance. But it wasn't the boat Singsing was looking at. "Is the merman here?" Ruby tried again, scanning the water's surface.
	A flash of movement caught Ruby's attention, and she turned to find the merman waving at her from farther down the sandy beach. His sea-glass-colored hair was almost the same hue as the water.
	Ruby broke into a smile. She hurried over to him and took a seat on the rocks. She had tried her best the previous day to let him know that the issue with the contaminated water was going to be addressed soon, and it seemed as if Ruby's message had gotten across to him since the merman had become less anxious.
	Without having to worry as much about the dead zone, Ruby and the merman had started to work on humming songs together, which turned out to be a lot of fun.
	As they hummed a new tune, Ruby suddenly heard a loud splash from the water. She whirled around just in time to watch the small fishing boat reel in a large net. Turquoise scales glittered from behind the netting, and Ruby inhaled sharply as she jumped to her feet. The merman had turned as well, and an expression of horror painted his face. He instantly leaped into the water to swim toward the boat.
	Ruby ran along the beach. And as she got closer she got to the boat, it didn't take her long to confirm what she had suspected. The realization was like a punch to the gut. There was a merperson in the net.

    Chapter 11
(Earlier That Morning)

	Aouli returned to his sister's residence and placed the stack of stone tablets she had asked for on the ground. "Aouli," Healani called out as she gracefully swam over to him.
	"I got the tablets." Aouli gestured at the stack of tablets on the ground. "I've got somewhere to go now, so-"
	"Somewhere to go? Don't tell me you're off to see that human girl again."
	"What?" Aouli blinked. "What do you mean?"
	"Don't think I don't know what you've been up to these days," Healani said lightly. "All of these mornings, you've been off to see that human girl."
	"Yes." Now that his sister knew, it wouldn't do him any good to try and lie to her.
	"Why?" Healani's eyes were sad as she shook her head. "The humans are dangerous. You know that."
	Aouli held his sister's gaze. "Not all of them harbor ill intentions. The human girl has helped me."
	"Helped you? We can't even speak with the humans. How did she help you?"
	"There's a dead zone," Aouli explained as Healani inhaled sharply. "The girl is helping to address it."
	"How?" Healani asked weakly. "A dead zone? What-?"
	"How did you know I was speaking with the human girl?" Aouli asked instead. "Was it Ulani? Did she tell you?"
	"It was Ulani," Healani said stiffly. "She was worried about you, so she came to me."
	"Ulani . . . "
	Healani took Aouli's hands in her own. "You need to be careful. We've already lost Mother to the humans. I don't want to lose you or Father to them either."
	"It wasn't my intention to show myself to the human girl at the beginning. But then I found the dead zone. After spending some time investigating it, I realized that its source had to be coming from somewhere on the land. And since I can't go on land myself, I had to seak help from someone who could."
	"Why didn't you tell me about the dead zone earlier? Father must have known about it too . . . "
	"Father and I didn't want you to worry-you don't have to worry. The human girl is working to resolve it. She just needs more time."
	"You're off to see her now."
	Aouli nodded. "I'll be back later."
	As he swam off, Aouli found himself thinking that maybe he should have tried to do a better job of explaining. It was true that Healani didn't know much about humans-in fact, she had never really gone far from the village. Maybe once she became the high chief, Aouli could take her to see the human girl in the hopes that Healani could improve her own relations with humans.
	Besides, once Healani became high chief, she'd be the one communicating with the original humans of the island. There were a small group of humans who had lived on the islands for hundreds of years and understood the language of the people of the sea. Once a year, the high chief would meet with those humans and they would talk about ways to continue to keep the people of the sea protected.
	Lost in thought as he swam up to the shore, Aouli spotted the girl on the beach. He smiled and waved to her as his head broke through the surface of the water.
	The two of them made their way over to the rocks that they had determined as their main meeting spot. Time passed quickly as Aouli hummed a tune with the red-haired girl.
	And then suddenly there was a loud splash. Aouli's head snapped around to see a net being drawn out of the water. Sea-glass scales glittered from behind the netting.
	Without giving himself a moment to think, Aouli leaped into the water. He swam as quickly as he could toward the net and the boat hauling it away. As he looked up at the net from beneath the water, Aouli gaped in shock. That was his sister in the net!
	Aouli couldn't do anything but watch in horror as the net was heaved up onto the boat. What could he do? He had to be careful. If whoever was on the boat saw him, he'd be in a lot of trouble.
	Closing his eyes for a brief moment as he debated what to do, he decided in the spur of the moment to trail the boat from afar. If he could see where the boat was going-if he could see where his sister was being taken-maybe he could figure out what to do from there.
	Suddenly it hit Aouli. His sister had been following him! That was why Healani had come this close to the shore. Aouli gritted his teeth together. This was his fault.
      Aouli followed the boat, careful to stay deep under the water. The boat eventually came to a stop next to the land, and Aouli couldn't say for sure whether the humans were moving his sister somewhere or keeping her on the boat.
      Panicked, Aouli swam back and forth through the water. Maybe he could ask the human girl for help again? Aouli didn't want to leave his sister there on the boat, but his options were limited.
      Shooting through the water, Aouli swam back in the direction of the shore. But by the time he arrived, the girl with the deep-red hair had vanished. Running an agitated hand through his hair, Aouli dove back into the water. He needed to let his father know about this.
      Aouli found his father speaking with the village elders. His father turned to him, taking note of the panicked expression on Aouli's face. "What happened?" Aouli's father asked quickly.
      "My sister," Aouli said breathlessly, "she was captured by the humans!"
      "What?"
      "Healani has been captured by the humans," Aouli repeated. "Please, Father, you have to save her!"
      "How did this happen?" Aouli's father seemed to get over his initial shock. "Do you know where she is now?"
      "I followed the boat, but once they got to the land, I'm not sure if they moved her," Aouli said regretfully.
      "Show me."
      Aouli nodded and quickly swam off, his father following along behind him.
      "How did this happen?" Aouli's father asked again as they shot through the water.
      Aouli winced. "I went to the shore again, and I didn't realize that Healani was following me. Since she was watching me, she probably didn't see the humans until it was too late."
      "And what were you doing so close to the shore?"
      "You know I've gone there before-"
      "Yes, but Healani's never followed you before. Tell me what's going on."
      Aouli exhaled a stream of bubbles. "I was meeting a human there."
      "A human?" Aouli's father asked sharply.
      "She was helping me address the problem of the dead zone," Aouli tried to explain.
      "You do realize that if anything happens to your sister, you're going to be the one to take over the position of high chief instead."
      "What?" Aouli faltered. "I-I didn't want my sister to be caught! I don't want the position of high chief! I-"
      Aouli's father let out a sigh. "I know you don't. I know you weren't internationally setting a trap for your sister. But if for some reason we really can't get her back, you will become the chief in your sister's place."
      Aouli's blood chilled. They'd get Healani back. His sister had been studying for years while Aouli had been out exploring the oceans. If Aouli became chief . . . Aouli didn't want to think about what would happen.
      "If whoever captured your sister exposes her to the rest of the humans"-his father's voice brought Aouli back to reality-"we can no longer stay here. If the humans try to search for us, we'll need to move our village."
      "Move our village?" Aouli turned to face his father. "But-but our ancestors lived in this very village!"
      "We'll do what we have to to protect ourselves from the humans," Aouli's father said gravely. "Once they find us, we'll no longer be able to live in peace."
      Aouli fell silent as the gravity of the situation pressed down on him. He had just spoken to Healani this morning. Had that been the last conversation he'd ever have with his sister?
      "That's the boat." Aouli pointed when they finally arrived a short distance from the land.
      His father narrowed his eyes. "I'll send someone to keep an eye on it. I'll send one of our village warriors for the job." Then he turned to Aouli. "As for you . . . " Aouli dropped his head as his father continued, "You should go back to the village."
      Aouli nodded silently. Had he tried to solve one problem just to create a different one? Aouli didn't know what to do. All he knew was that he had to get his sister back no matter what.
      
~

	"Aouli?" Ulani blinked as Aouli hurried into her cave. "What brings you here in such a rush?"
	"Ulani." Aouli met Ulani's milky eyes with his own. "You already know what happened, don't you."
	"No." Ulani's eyes were wide as she shook her head. "Tell me quickly."
	"It's my sister," Aouli said hopelessly. "Healani's been captured by humans."
	"Humans?" Ulani let out a gasp as her hands flew to her mouth.
	"I'm a little surprised you didn't see that with your ability and all." Aouli blinked as that fact suddenly occurred to him.
	"I think I can only get those sorts of visions when someone's in mortal peril," Ulani said thoughtfully.
	"Does that mean that my sister's in no immediate danger?"
	Ulani furrowed her brows. "I'm not sure. I'd like to think so, though. What do you want to do?" She inquired as Aouli paced the cave, swimming back and forth.
	"I don't know." Aouli stopped in his tracks and pressed his hands to the sides of his face. "If we can't get my sister back, I have to become the high chief in her place. I can't let that happen. I don't want anything to happen to her either."
	"You could ask the human girl for help," Ulani suggested. "She was willing to help you before."
	Aouli shook his head. "She wasn't on the beach when I swam back there. This is my fault. I never thought my sister would follow me. All those other days I went to the shore there had never been a boat there-" he trailed off. That was right. There had never been a boat there before. How much of a coincidence was it that the fishing boat showed up the only day his sister decided to follow him?
	Come to think of it, whoever was on the boat couldn't have known that his sister existed. Aouli frowned as he recalled the details of the event. The net they had used . . . Aouli had never seen a net like it before. They certainly hadn't been out to catch fish. Especially not this close to the shore. Suddenly it struck him. Their target had never been his sister. And if it wasn't his sister . . . Were they after him? Aouli shook his head. If they really were after him, they didn't need to go so close to the shore and risk damaging their boat and nets on the rocks. They could have waited for him farther out in the water where their nets would have worked much better.
	There had only been one other person on the beach, and that had been . . . the girl with the deep-red hair! Whoever was on the boat was after her!
	"You seem as if you just realized something important," Ulani said as she watched Aouli's face.
	"Whoever was in the boat was never out to catch my sister," Aouli explained in a panic. "They wanted to catch the human girl!"
	Ulani blinked. "Catch the human girl?"
	"They wanted to catch her, but then they saw my sister and caught her instead."
	Ulani just stared at him. "I don't understand. Why would they want to catch the human girl?"
	"Maybe they don't like that she's investigating the dead zone." Aouli recalled the images of girl had shown him of where the contamination problem was coming from. Had she gone somewhere where she wasn't supposed to be? "She's in trouble because of me, too," Aouli said in a pained sort of way.
	"Talk to her tomorrow," Ulani suggested gently. "Maybe she'll have a way to help free your sister."
	"I think that would be asking for a miracle. Besides, I don't even know if Father will let me leave the village."
	Ulani flashed Aouli a smile. "I can take care of that."
	"What-? What do you mean?"
	Ulani winked. "Just leave it to me. Tomorrow morning? No problem, I can create an opening for you to go to the shore."
	"Thank you." Aouli held Ulani's gaze. "I mean it."
	Ulani let out a sigh. "I want to get your sister back as well. Your father is very cautious when it comes to humans-and that's a good thing. But if the human girl really can help us, well, I don't think he'd be willing to take advantage of such an opportunity."
	"I'll go tomorrow," Aouli said determinedly. "Tomorrow, I'll go get my sister back."

~

	The following morning, Aouli snuck out of the village only to find that there wasn't anyone guarding the area. Ulani had successfully led everyone away.
      The girl was already walking along the beach when Aouli arrived at the shore, and his head broke through the surface of the water as he scanned the fine sands. The red-haired girl saw him almost immediately, and she hurried over with a worried look on her face.
	Aouli pointed in the direction the boat had gone, and the girl nodded her head. She had seen the boat drive off with Healani.
	Suddenly, the girl motioned for Aouli to stay where he was before turning and hurrying away from the beach. Aouli watched and waited there in the water before the girl returned a few minutes later with a two-wheeled contraption.
	The girl gestured for Aouli to show the way. Aouli nodded and dove into the water.
	Aouli led the way through the ocean, and the girl with her wheeled contraption zoomed down the beach. When the sandy beach ended, the girl had to climb higher up onto the land. Aouli swam further out so the girl could still see him from the distance.
	The boat finally came into view. It was still there sitting next to the land.
	This was as far as Aouli could go. His father had one of his warriors watching the area, and if he was caught, Aouli would undoubtedly end up under watch back in the village.
	The girl seemed to realize that he couldn't go any further, and she nodded before drawing closer to the boat herself. Aouli waited there in the water again. When the girl reappeared, she gestured for Aouli to meet her back on the beach.
	When they finally arrived back on the beach, the girl was frowning, and a crease had formed between her brows. Aouli gave her a questioning look, but the girl just shook her head. She gestured that she couldn't tell whether Healani even was on the boat. But judging from her frown, something had concerned her.
	Their meeting ended with the girl motioning that she would go back and look at the boat again. As Aouli swam off, he found himself thinking if he was able to get close enough to the boat to call out to his sister, would she be able to hear him? Would she be able to tell him her location?
	Maybe it was a foolish idea, but Aouli had to try. He'd go in the middle of the night. At that time, there shouldn't be as many humans out, and even if one of them heard him, he'd be back beneath the dark surface of the water before any of them could see him. If his sister wasn't on the boat, that would make things a lot more complicated.

~

	When the sun finally dropped from the sky, Aouli was swimming out in the direction of the boat. Once he reached the location of the boat, he carefully navigated around where he had seen the warrior stationed by the boat. Making sure to keep a wide berth from the warrior, Aouli got as close to the boat as he dared. Then sticking his head out of the water, he took a deep breath, and the cold night wind hit him like a slap in the face. "Healani!" Aouli yelled.
	Aouli waited for a long moment. Time itself seemed to slow down as he stared up at the boat, hoping with everything he had that there would be a response.
	"I'm in here!" Healani's muffled voice called back a moment later. Aouli felt a rush of relief.
	"Don't worry, Healani!" Aouli shouted. "We're figuring out a way to get you out of there! Wait for us!"
	Suddenly, Aouli felt himself being tugged down beneath the water.
	"Hey!" The warrior frowned as Aouli struggled to break free from his strong grasp. Then he narrowed his eyes as he seemed to recognize Aouli through the darkness. "What are you doing here? Does your father know about this?"
	Aouli just shook his head. He had gotten caught, but at least now he knew that his sister was still on the boat.
	"Go back to the village," the warrior advised as he let go of Aouli's arm. "Quickly now. For your sister's sake, don't cause any trouble around here."
	Aouli turned away from the boat and swam back toward the village. Once the warrior let his father know that he had snuck out, he knew he wouldn't easily be able to leave the village again. Instead of returning to his residence, Aouli swam to Ulani's cave.
	The inside of the cave glowed with little lights, and Ulani floated in the middle of it as she held a jar up in front of her, examining the contents inside.
	"Ulani," Aouli spoke up. 
      Ulani turned, and her hair flowed out around her as she smiled. "Can the human girl help you?"
	Aouli nodded confidently. "She can. But I need to do my part too. She can't do it on her own, the same way I can't do it on my own either."
	"What are you suggesting, then?"
	Aouli took a deep breath. "Ulani, I want you to turn me into a human."
	"Are you sure?"
	"I can tell my father is already discontent with what I've been doing. Getting my sister back is the most important part. Once we get my sister back, I can deal with what the people from the village say about me later."
	Ulani nodded her head. "When do you want to become a human?"
	"Now."
	"Now?"
	Aouli sighed. "Once the sun comes up, my father won't let me out of the village. I have to do this."
	"Alright." Ulani offered Aouli a small smile.
	Aouli followed Ulani over to the large cauldron at the far end of her cave. He drifted in the water as he watched Ulani collect a number of bottles from her shelves and empty their contents into the cauldron. The liquid inside the cauldron was completely clear despite how many different powders had been mixed into it.
	Ulani finally turned to Aouli. "I will need your hair to complete it."
	"Take it."
	He could feel Ulani's presence behind him, and then his head suddenly felt much lighter. After slowly opening his eyes, Aouli turned to watch Ulani drop his hair into the cauldron. The liquid inside instantly turned a brilliant turquoise in color.
	Aouli absently reached up and ran a hand through his now very short hair.
	"It's ready," Ulani announced. "All you need to do now is to climb into the cauldron. Once you're submerged in the liquid, your tail will be replaced with human legs for three days. The stronger the spells, the shorter they last."
	"So you can do magic!"
	"Well, it's not really magic . . ."
	With a faint trace of a smile playing on his face, Aouli made his way over to the cauldron. Ulani helped him inside.
	"You only have this one chance." Ulani held his gaze. "Make the most of it."
	After nodding determindly, Aouli closed his eyes and submerged himself in the turquoise liquid.

~

	Aouli awoke to a spinning head. His body was shaking from the cold winds that savagely bit at his bare skin. Clenching his fists in the powdery sand, Aouli cracked an eye open to look up at the stars glittering in the night sky above him. He was on the beach.
	Aouli could feel the water from the ocean lapping up against him as he lay there. His body felt lethargic. But even in his tired state, Aouli could tell that his tail had vanished.
	Aouli let out a laugh as he lay there on the sand. Ulani had really done it.
	He was human now.

    Chapter 11.5

Ru?y Z: Tilden? Are you still awake?

Zhang T: It's not even the evening yet. Of course I'm still awake.

Ru?y Z: So... I've run into a little bit of a problem.

Zhang T: Oh? What sort of problem?

Ru?y Z: Well, I've got a situation.

Ru?y Z: You're not going to believe me when I tell you this, but I promise all of it is true.

Ru?y Z: I met a merman on the beach. I was trying to help him investigate a section of contaminated water, but me being close to him led to another merperson getting captured.

Ru?y Z: And now I don't know what to do. I think I know where the merperson is being kept and who it was who kidnapped them.

Ru?y Z: Tilden, I need to make it up to the merman and help free his friend. But I don't know what to do. I don't know how to do it alone. I need advice.

    Chapter 12

	Grace lay in bed with her injured leg propped up on a pillow, scrolling through her phone. Her foot had stopped hurting, but she got the feeling that now was not the time to try putting weight on it.
	When Grace had fallen on it, she was horrified. What if she had actually broken something? What if her dreams of studying dance on the East Coast had shattered along with her foot? But fortunately, that hadn't been the case. She just needed to stay home for a few weeks and heal. Once she had healed, she could get back to dance. But the waiting . . .
	Grace set her phone down and let out a sigh. She wasn't used to being home this much. At least now she had something to look forward to: Ruby's brother was coming to San Francisco for a visit.
	Then Grace blinked. On the topic of Ruby, Ruby had gotten her phone back and had sent the group chat a message about being followed. Grace had been alarmed when she read the message. What if Ruby did have a stalker? Grace's mind had immediately jumped to the worst-case scenario; what if the stalker tried to kidnap Ruby?
	Grace quickly shook her head in an attempt to clear it. Ruby was fine. She had sent them a message just earlier in the day. But even then, Grace couldn't help but feel a little worried.
	After slowly getting out of bed, Grace reached for her crutches and made her way out of her room. She knocked once on her brother's door only to find that it wasn't latched. She gently pushed it open.
	Tye was fast asleep at his desk, with a pile of textbooks spread over the table in front of him.
	"Tye." Grace sighed as she hobbled over to him. "Tye," she tried again when he didn't wake. She shook her brother's shoulder with a hand.
	"Grace?" Tye blinked. He sat up and straightened his glasses, which were beginning to slip down his nose.
	"Did you see the message Ruby sent just a couple of hours ago?" Grace asked.
	"What message?" Tye blinked again as he pulled out his phone to scroll through the texts. "I just got home from the cram school an hour ago."
	Grace eyed Tye's textbook-covered desk. "You should take more breaks. You could try going to the gym like Mom keeps telling you to." Grace shrugged at the exasperated look Tye gave her.
	"Ruby has a stalker?" Tye turned back to the group chat. He enlarged the image Ruby had sent to view the man in the background of the selfie. "I thought going to Hawaii would be fun and relaxing. That's really scary."
	"I thought so too. Ruby definitely isn't relaxing now."
	Tye frowned down at the screen of his phone. "Are there any apps that can clear up blurry images?"
	Grace shook her head. "I don't think so. I did a search on it earlier. You only see those sorts of apps in movies."
	Tye let out a heavy sigh. "I wish there was something we could do. But we're all so far away from her now."
	"Her parents are there with her," Grace reassured her brother. "If there really is something serious going on, they'd do whatever they can to keep Ruby safe."
	"Now I'm really not in the right mind to study."
	Grace's phone buzzed. "Look, it's a message from Tilden!"
	"Tilden?" Tye looked over at Grace's phone, despite getting the same message on his.
	"He says he's just arrived in San Francisco."
	"Who did he end up deciding to stay with?" Tye squinted down at the message.
	"It looks like Tomas's place," Grace answered as she read through the block of text Tilden had sent. "He wants to caught up with Isabelle."
	"Do you think he brought San with him?" Tye asked lightly.
	"He didn't say," Grace said disappointedly. "He can't leave us hanging like this forever. Wait-" Grace blinked as a second message popped up on the screen. "What's this?"
	"Tilden is asking us if we'll be able to go join Ruby in Hawaii for a week?" Tye said in disbelief.
	"Do you think Ruby is in trouble?" Grace asked worriedly.
	Tye just stared at his phone. "Do think we could actually go?"
	"I'm not taking any classes right now," Grace said slowly. "I think at least I could go."
	Tye frowned. "I'm doing the cram school. But I guess if I do call in sick next week, I can always catch up on my own time."
	"Are you sure?"
	"If Ruby needs our help, it's a sacrifice I'm willing to take."
	Grace nodded her head. Before she could type back, a message from Mari popped up.
	I'm in! Mari's message read.
	Me too, a message from Tomas followed almost immediately.
	Tye and me as well, Grace typed, and she sent the message as Tye gave her a nod.
	I knew I could count on you guys, a new message from Tilden popped up. I'll cover the cost of the plane tickets. All I need is for you guys to get ready by tonight. I'll pick all of you up and drive you to the airport at seven. The flight leaves at 10pm.
	Grace turned to Tye with wide eyes. "We're leaving tonight?"
	"I guess we are," Tye said in equal bewilderment. "It must be urgent."
	"But why us?" Grace set her phone down, stunned. "Why not just go straight to the police?"
	Tye just shook his head, still in a state of shock. "I guess we'll find out. Now, how do we convince our parents just to let us go to Hawaii?"
	"We could say that we need to help Ruby with an internship," Grace suggested.
	"Even if that's the case, would they really let us go?"
	"It's worth a shot, isn't it? Besides, Tilden will be with us. Both our parents know Tilden. Back in ninth grade, he came over a lot, and our parents seemed to think very highly of him then."
	Tye nodded. "We can try."
	Grace wrung her hands together. "Ruby needs our help. When our parents get home at five, we'll ask them. For now, we can start packing our suitcases."
	"I'll go get a suitcase out of the closet." Tye made to leave the room before pausing in the doorway to turn and face Grace. "You should sit-your foot is still injured, and the doctor said to stay off it as much as possible."
	
~

	The wait for her parents to return home seemed to drag on infinitely. Grace was back in her own room, and she was sitting on her bed with her phone next to her. Finally, five o'clock rolled around. Grace made her way off her bed. She quickly grabbed her crutches and hobbled into the living room. Tye was already there, waiting for their parents to walk in.
	When the door swung open, Grace's mom blinked at them. "What are the two of you doing waiting for us?" she asked in surprise.
	"You know our friend Ruby?" Tye asked.
	"Of course," their mom said, giving Tye a look as if she was trying to figure out what he would say next.
	"Do you remember her older brother, Tilden?" Tye continued.
	"Tilden? Of course I remember him."
	"Tilden invited Grace and me to go to Hawaii to help Ruby with a summer internship," Tye said seriously. "It's only one week long, and the entire trip will be covered."
	"So you're asking if we'll let you go?" the twins' mother concluded.
	Grace nodded her head. "I don't know if we'll be able to get another opportunity like it."
	"You're still injured," Grace's dad added skeptically. "Are you sure you want to go traveling?"
	"I can walk with the crutches." Grace looked up at him hopefully.
	Grace's parents exchanged a glance. "When is this trip?" Grace's dad asked.
	"Tonight," Tye answered. "We need to let Tilden know whether or not to come and pick us up."
	"What about your summer class?"
	"I can make up the work on my own," Tye said determinedly. "I'm willing to put in the work."
	Their mom smiled faintly. "If that's the case, I don't see why the two of you shouldn't go."
	Their dad nodded along. "Neither of you has been to Hawaii before. It will be a fun experience. I hope you enjoy yourselves there."
	Grace beamed. "Thank you!"
	"Thank you!" Tye echoed with a wide grin on his face. "We'll go finish getting ready."

	"Tilden just texted." Tye hurried into Grace's room. "He's waiting for us downstairs."
	Grace rose from her seat, and with Tye's help, made her way down the stairs. Tilden had parked outside, and Grace could see that Mari and Tomas were already in the car with him. Grace climbed into the back to join Mari and Tomas, while Tye took the passenger seat next to Tilden.
	Tilden grinned as he swiveled around to look at the three in the back. "Off we go."
	"Tilden." Grace just stared at him after she fastened her seatbelt. The light from the setting sun painted the car in shadows. "You're actually back-you're actually here."
	"It's sweet of you to have missed me." Tilden laughed good-naturedly as his dark-brown eyes sparkled. Even though it had been a few years since Grace had last seen Tilden in person, he looked almost exactly the same as he had back in high school.
	"Are you coming with us to Hawaii?" Tye asked as Tilden set the car into motion.
	"Unfortunately not," Tilden said regretfully. "I'm just your ride to the airport. Ruby's got an interesting situation, and sending you over was the only thing I could think of to help her."
	Mari blinked from where she sat next to Grace. "I didn't know you weren't coming with us."
	Tilden sighed. "I don't know how my parents would react if I just suddenly showed up in front of them. My presence would probably only complicate things."
	A silence fell in the car, and Grace turned to look out the window to watch the buildings and shops blur by. The silence was broken when Tye suddenly sneezed. Once, twice.
	"Are you alright?" Tomas asked.
	Tye pinched the bridge of his nose. "Yeah."
	Grace blinked. "Have you caught a cold? I told you you shouldn't stay up that late studying-look what it's done to your health!"
	"I'm fine, really." Tye turned around to give Grace a half-reassuring, half-exasperated smile. "I haven't caught a cold, I promise."
	"On a different note," Tilden said, "how are you all enjoying being out of school for the summer? I know I haven't been very active on the group chat, but I have been reading all of your messages."
	"It's even better now that you're back," Mari said with a laugh.
	"Don't flatter me." Tilden was laughing as well now. "Do you really want someone as old as me hanging around you cool kids?"
	Tomas raised a brow. "Cool kids? Us?"
	Tilden's shoulders shook with laughter. "Come on. Admit it, won't you? Even back in ninth grade, you all had admirers."
	"That was only because you were with us at the time!"
	"Well, that I can't help. I was pretty cool . . ."

	"We appreciate that you were even able to take us this far." Mari smiled gratefully, and Grace nodded along.
	Tilden frowned slightly. "I'm not sure what time it will be in Maui when the plane lands. But even with the time difference, I think it will still be pretty late. Try and get some sleep on the plane if you can."
	"We'll try our best," Tye said as they came to a stop at the entrance to the airport. "We'll do our best to help Ruby."

They'll try and make it up to the four of you."

	After waving goodbye for a final time to Tilden, Grace followed her friends into the airport.

	"And now we wait," Mari echoed, clasping her hands together in her lap.

	Grace couldn't help but wonder just what sort of situation they were about to get themselves into. Was Ruby's stalker dangerous? Had she already been captured and was being held hostage? Did Tilden need them to go and help find Ruby?

	Grace turned to her brother. "Is it even worth trying to sleep? Now that I'm actually on the plane, I don't think I'd be able to sleep even if I wanted to."
	Tye sighed. "Me too. Tilden really made us worry."
	Mari leaned over. "Tomas wants me to remind us to set our phones on airplane mode."
	Grace pulled out her phone. "I almost forgot." Tye followed her lead and set his own phone to airplane mode as well.
	As they waited for all the passengers to finish boarding, Tye turned to address Mari. "You seem happy that Tilden's back."
	"Of course I am," Mari said confidently. "We all are, aren't we? It's been too long since we've seen Tilden in person last."
	"The way you were looking at him today was different than what I remember," Tye said knowingly.
	Mari blinked. "What do you mean?"
	"You used to be all shy around him," Grace added with a smile. "But that's changed now."
	Mari's face reddened. "I was a silly ninth-grader at the time. And he was a really cool upperclassman. I always felt a little embarrassed in his presence."
	"And he was good-looking?"
	"What-? He is good-looking, but that's not the point! He was always just an older brother figure-nothing more than that. And besides, Tilden's in a relationship now."
	"Do you have someone else you like now?" Grace asked playfully.
	Mari folded her arms across her chest. "Maybe I do."
	Just then, the intercom crackled to life, and a woman's voice filled the plane. "Welcome. Please fasten your seat belts. We're about to take flight."

	Even though she had tried, Grace wasn't able to get a wink of sleep on the flight. They had just landed, and she had to shake Tye awake. Grace wasn't sure whether Mari or Tomas had been able to get any sleep either, but as they shuffled off the plane, Grace could see that both of them looked tired.
	Grace almost winced at the time as she checked her phone. The morning was still hours off. The four of them made their way out of the airport. Even at night, the air was warm and humid, and the wind was tinged with the scent of the ocean.

	Grace looked around as well. "Ah-ha! The taxis are over there!"
	Mari clapped her hands together. "Perfect!"
	Once the four of them had joined the line of people waiting for taxis, Grace found herself glad to finally be outside again. Her neck, back, and legs were stiff from all the sitting. The sky here on the island was much different than the sky back in San Francisco. There were stars glittering in the night, and each glowing dot was bright against the inky backdrop.
      After lifting her phone up to take a picture of the sky, Grace frowned. Through the camera, she couldn't see the stars. But when she looked past her phone, there they were, glittering down at her. It seemed as if some things couldn't be captured in photographs.
      When it was their turn to board a taxi, the four of them loaded their bags into the back. There was silence as they drove down the otherwise empty highway. They'd see Ruby soon.

    Chapter 13

	When the taxi pulled to a stop in front of the house Ruby was staying at, after paying the taxi driver, Tye stood on the sidewalk with his friends, looking up at the house.
	"Should we send Ruby a text?" Mari asked quietly.
	Grace nodded as she pulled out her phone. "I just sent one," she said a moment later. "I told Ruby that we're outside the house."
      Tomas frowned slightly. "She might be sleeping. We might end up having to wait out here all night."
	Tye scanned the sky. "Morning's not that far off. Even if we do end up having to wait outside, it won't be all that bad. At least it's warm enough that we don't even need our jackets."
	Just as Mari took a seat on the pavement, hurried footsteps sounded from inside the house, and the door swung open a moment later to reveal a very disheveled-looking Ruby. Her eyes widened when she saw them, and her stressed expression melted into a grin.
	"Ruby!" Grace exclaimed in an excited whisper.
	"Grace," Ruby said weakly. "Tye, Tomas, Mari. How-? Tilden really was able to send all of you here?"
	Mari rushed forward. "We were all so worried about you! Just what exactly is going on?"
	"Let's go inside first." Ruby stood on her tiptoes to glance over her friends' shoulders. "A lot has happened in the past few days . . ."

	"My parents are still asleep upstairs." Ruby tugged at her deep-red hair. "I don't want to deal with them right now-I don't have the energy to deal with them right now. I'll have to figure out what to tell them in the morning. For now, try to keep quiet, okay? This way. There's already someone here I want you guys to meet."
	"Someone here?" Mari asked in confusion.
	Ruby sighed tiredly. "It's a long story. But long story short, I met someone on the beach. He came to me for help. I tried to help him, but I ended up making things worse. His sister got kidnapped because of me, and now I have to figure out how to get her back before anything bad happens to her."
	"What?" Tye said weakly.
	"Yeah . . ." Ruby winced. "It sounds pretty bad. It is pretty bad. The boy I met . . . he's here now. Oh"-Ruby turned to look over her shoulder at them as she stopped in front of a door-"I don't know if I mentioned this earlier, but this boy doesn't speak English. He used to be a merman. Well, until tonight that is. I don't know what happened, but now he seems to be a human. I know it sounds crazy, but it's the truth. Whether you believe the merman part or not, the fact remains that his sister was kidnapped. And not just by anyone; she was kidnapped by one of my dad's co-workers."

	Ruby shook her head. "I'm not sure. Now that he has an actual mermaid in his possession, I doubt he'll come for me again." After letting out another tired sigh, Ruby pushed open the door to the guest room.
      Tye stepped into the room after Ruby, only realizing he had been holding his breath once he crossed the threshold.
      A boy around his age sat on the bed, dressed in slacks and a button-down shirt that Tye recognized as belonging to Ruby's dad. But the most curious thing about the boy was his sea-glass-colored hair. It was short and jagged as if cut with a dull knife.
	The boy just looked at the four of them, unsure what to think of them. Ruby gestured to her friends, then pointed to herself in an attempt to convey to the boy that she knew them.
	The boy still seemed confused, but he nodded along anyway.
	Ruby pinched the bridge of her nose as if to ward off a headache. "Tomorrow I'm going to try and take him to where his sister is being kept. The only problem is he can't walk."
	"I have an idea," Grace said quickly. "I've got crutches-my own foot has healed enough that I don't really need them. Maybe he can try them."
	Ruby leaned against the wall. "I really need to go to bed. I've been running on caffeine all night, but now I really need a nap. At least two hours. I know the four of you only just got here and must have a million questions. I promise I'll try my best to explain everything tomorrow."
	"Don't worry," Tye reassured Ruby. "We'll take care of him. Go get some sleep."
	"Thank you," Ruby said gratefully before slipping out of the room.
	Tye looked over at Grace, and the two of them exchanged a glance. Maybe the boy in front of them really had been a merman. As ridiculous as it seemed, maybe this was why Ruby hadn't explained the situation over their group chat.
	Had Tilden known about the merman? Maybe this was why Ruby hadn't gone to the police. She couldn't go to the police. If she tried to explain that a mermaid had been kidnapped, the police wouldn't believe her. So . . . that was why she had to take matters into her own hands.
	"What happens now?" Mari asked. "Maybe while Ruby's sleeping, we can try and help the boy figure out how to walk?"
	Tomas nodded his head. "Let's try."
	Grace gingerly set her crutches down on the bed and motioned for the boy to pick them up.
	The boy just gave her a blank look.
	Tye let out a sigh. This was going to be a lot more difficult than he had first thought. The language barrier was one thing, but if the boy couldn't walk, how was Ruby supposed to take him to find his kidnapped sister?
	Turning back to look at the boy, Tye noticed there was something hopeless behind his eyes. But of course. The boy had just lost his sister and wasn't sure if she was safe. Tye turned to look at Grace from where she, Mari, and Tomas were all doing different gestures to try and communicate with the boy.
	If his own sister was kidnapped one day, how would he feel? Well, it wasn't something he wanted to imagine. If Grace was kidnapped, Tye would be devastated. Grace was his older sister-his twin sister. Grace had always been part of his life. He wasn't sure what he'd do if someone put her in danger.
	Tye didn't know how the boy had become a human or if he really had lived under the sea, but alongside the hopelessness in the boy's eyes, there was also determination. The boy wouldn't give up.
	If Grace was kidnapped one day and taken somewhere deep under the sea, Tye would also try and figure out a way to trade his legs for a tail to find her. And while Tye didn't believe in magic or miracles, the boy in front of him was an indicator that both of those things might very well be possible.
	Shaking his head in an attempt to clear it, Tye made his way over to join the others in their attempt to try and get the boy to stand up. The boy had seemed to realize what they wanted him to do, and to his credit, was trying his best to get to his feet.
	After some struggle, the boy managed to stand on his own. But it only lasted a moment before his knees buckled and he fell to the floor.

Together, the two of them helped pull the boy to his feet. He was standing now. Even if he was swaying slightly, he was standing.
      Grace quickly brought the crutches over and placed them under her own arms. Then she held them out to the boy and motioned for him to do the same. Still tightly holding onto Tye and Mari, the boy let Grace help put the crutches under his arms. Ever so slowly, he let go of Tye and Mari's hands to grasp the handles of the crutches. Tye stepped away as the boy stood there, clutching the crutches tightly.
	Mari stepped away as well, and there was a smile on her face as she clapped her hands together. "Good, good! This is good!" Mari's enthusiasm seemed contagious, as the boy's face relaxed into a smile as well.

	Tomas shook his head. "Ruby's parents will probably take the car during the day. Besides, Ruby doesn't know how to drive."
	"Do any of us know how to drive?" Grace asked, suddenly worried.
	"I do," Mari said proudly. "I actually have my license and everything."
	"Oh, that's right!" Grace's eyes lit up. "What if we rented a car for ourselves?"
	Mari pulled out her own phone. "I'll look up the cost of car rentals. Hopefully the closest one isn't too far from here. I remember seeing advertisements for them back at the airport."
	"We could also call another taxi to take us to the rental place if we need to," Tomas reassured her.
	After pocketing his phone, Tye stepped over to the boy. While the four of them had been discussing their plans on what to do next, the boy seemed to have tried to move around with the crutches on his own. 	Tomas checked the time. "We've still got a little while until sunrise. I don't know how many of us were able to get any sleep on the plane-I know I didn't. Maybe we should try and get some sleep."

	Tye turned back to the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair with a sigh. "I guess it's just you and me now."

	"But would he do it if it meant his sister could return home?"
	"Last night, before the four of you arrived, he kept holding up three fingers. I came to the conclusion that that meant he could only be a human for three-three something. I ruled out three minutes and three hours. Maybe he can only be a human for three days."
	"If that's the case, we really don't have a whole lot of time. Look!" Tye said suddenly from where he had been scanning the sidewalk. There were indeed tracks. Crouching down, Tye snapped a picture of the shoeprint.
	Ruby crouched down as well. "Are we sure that these belonged to that man?"
	"I don't know for sure, but let's follow them to where the dirt is the thickest," Tye said quickly.
	The two of them quickened their pace. They followed the shoeprints, all the while eyeing the shoes of everyone who walked past them.
	"They look like they come to a stop here." Tye pointed to the ground. "But there's nothing here."
	"This is the highway!" Ruby suddenly realized. "He must have been dropped off by someone."
	Tye furrowed his brow. "Have you gone that way before?"
	"I have," Ruby said, suddenly frowning. "When I went to visit the farm . . ." Her head snapped up to look at Tye. "Don't tell me he came from the farm?"
	"Farm?" Tye just blinked in confusion. "What farm?"
