    Chapter 14

	"That Mr. Stevenson . . ." Ruby crouched down by the side of the road. "I can't believe it. Would he really go that far to kidnap me just to get to my dad?"
	"Some people will do crazy things when they're desperate," Tye said, and Ruby looked up at him tiredly.
	Ruby slowly rose to her feet, and a wind picked up to set her hair flying. "The farm belongs to the company my dad works at. The ocean water was becoming contaminated from all the runoff, and that's why the merman came to me in the first place. He wanted me to help him figure out where the cause of the contamination was coming from. Was Mr. Stevenson angry about how my dad started looking into it and wanted to kidnap me to get back at him?"
	Tye motioned for Ruby to follow him back the way they had come. "If it really is Mr. Stevenson, at least now we know who he is. But something tells me that if we were to call the police on him here and now, we still wouldn't have the evidence we'd need to prove anything."
	Ruby let out a sigh. "Let's drive down to the boat where the merman's sister is being kept. I want to see what the situation is looking like."

~

	When the two of them returned to the house, Mari was the one who greeted them at the door.
	"Let's take a drive," Ruby said breathlessly.
	Mari nodded. "Alright."
	"Who else is coming along this time?" Ruby asked as she looked at the rest of her friends.
	"Maybe we should bring him along this time." Tomas gestured to the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair. "I can stay behind."
	There was silence in the car as they drove toward the dock. Mari sat in the driver's seat, and even though she didn't seem nervous, Ruby noted how her friend's knuckles had whitened from where she was grasping the steering wheel.
	Ruby sat in the passenger seat, instructing Mari which roads to take. Behind them, Tye, Grace, and the former merman sat in a row. The latter sat behind Ruby and was looking absently out the window. If he was fazed by the car ride, he didn't show it.
	"There," Ruby said quietly, pointing to the row of boats that were floating by the dock. "It's the white fishing boat."
	After driving past the docks, Mari parked the car a little distance away. They'd get out of the car and walk back around to check it. Well, Mari, Grace, and Tye would go and check it out. For now, it would be safer if Ruby kept a low profile. She'd stay in the car with the merman.
	After Ruby's friends left the car, she joined the boy in the back. Mari had started a video call and was showing Ruby the path down to the docks.
	"That's the fishing boat." Grace's voice floated out from the phone.
	"Does there look like there's anyone around it?" Ruby asked quickly. "Is there anyone watching the dock?"
	"Well," Tye said slowly, as the three of them passed the dock and headed further down the path, "I think we found the man with the dirty shoes."
	Ruby inhaled sharply.
	"Don't worry," Grace said quickly. "I don't think he seemed very interested in us. He's just kind of walking around. He's definitely guarding the boat-which means the mermaid has to be on it!"
	"Watch out!" Mari said suddenly. "He's heading toward where we parked the car!"
	Ruby's heart rate seemed to accelerate as she hurriedly slid off her seat and crouched down on the floor of the car. She gestured for the boy to do the same, and the boy didn't need to be told twice before he ducked down beneath the window as well.
	Ruby pressed a finger to her lips, and the boy nodded, understanding the universal gesture. As she shakily hung up on the video call, Ruby could hear the sound of her heart beating in her ears. 
Her skin prickled, and goosebumps ran down her arms despite the summer heat. Suddenly, Ruby pulled out her phone. Her fingers flew over the keys as she typed a message to her friends.
	While the man's distracted, would it be possible to get onto the boat?
	He won't be distracted for long, Mari's reply came almost instantly.
	What if we distracted him? Ruby sent another message. I could try and lure him away.
	It's too dangerous. What if he's armed? I'll lure him away.
	You? If he injures you somehow, how are the rest of us supposed to get away? You're the only one who knows how to operate our getaway car, remember?
	Grace is offering. When the man comes back, she'll try to lead him away. Once he's out of sight, bring the merman to the boat. Maybe he'll be able to sense his sister there.
	Ruby let out a sigh as she stared down at the screen of her phone for a long moment.
	He's coming back to the dock, a message from Tye popped up. I think you're in the clear.
	Ruby slowly rose and checked out the windows before motioning for the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair to rise as well. Ruby pushed open the door to the car. She held it open for the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair to exit as well. They made their way as quickly down the slope to the dock, and Tye and Mari beckoned them over the moment they saw them.
	"The three of you can go onto the boat," Mari said in a whisper. The rush of the wind carried her voice away the moment the words left her mouth. "I'll try my best to cover you from out here."
	Ruby hurried onto the boat, and Tye helped the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair. Even though the wind was strong, the water seemed fairly calm, and the boat didn't rock as much as Ruby thought it would. As she looked around the deck, Ruby quickly snapped pictures of everything she could.
	Tye found the stairs leading down under the deck, and he had vanished down them by the time Ruby turned back around. Moving swiftly, Ruby descended the steps only to find Tye and the former merman standing in front of a locked door.
	"That has to be where the mermaid is being kept," Tye said quietly, eyeing the lock.
	Ruby and Tye exchanged a glance. Something told Ruby that breaking down the door wasn't an option. The door look study enough that if either of them tried, they'd sooner be broken by the door than bust their way into the room beyond.
	Tye took a picture of the lock, making sure not to touch it with his hands. "Fingerprints," Tye said knowingly. "Don't touch anything with your bare skin."
	Ruby leaned forward to examine the lock as well. She felt a light tap on her shoulder a moment later, and she turned to see the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair looking at her expectantly. Ruby sighed defeatedly as she pointed to the lock on the door. She tried her best to motion that they couldn't get inside.
	The boy motioned to the door, and Ruby stepped aside to let him look at the metal. He gently tapped on the metal with the toe of his shoe before calling out. His words were in a language Ruby had never heard before, and it had just occurred to her that she had never him speak before.
	Suddenly, a faint voice called back from the other side of the door. The voice beyond the door belongs to a female, and the words were in the same musical language as the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair.
	"What should we do?" Tye asked quietly. "If we can't open the door, I'd suggest stealing the entire boat, but I don't even know how to drive a car, let alone a boat."
	"We can't just steal the boat. I think we're better off having someone watch the boat in case they try to move the mermaid. If they do move her, that will probably be our only opportunity to get her."
	Tye frowned slightly. "What if we tackled the man with the dirty shoes? Do you think he has the key?"
	"Do you really think we could take him?"
	"With all five of us? I'd say we'd have about a fifty-fifty chance of success."
	"And what happens if we fail?"
	"We probably end up at the police station. And if I'm being real with you, between messing with the police and not messing with the police, I'd rather avoid them."
	"Did you guys find anything?" Mari asked when they hopped back onto the land.
	Ruby pinched the bridge of her nose. "The mermaid is locked behind a door. Let's take turns watching the dock for now. I need to wait for my dad to get back. I think he can help us."
	"I can stay and watch," Tye offered.
	Mari turned to Ruby and the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair. "Let's head back to the car, then. Grace will meet us there later. I'm supposed to send her a text once we're all back in the car."
	Nodding, Ruby followed Mari back up the slope. They didn't have to wait long for Grace to appear. She was by herself, and the man with the dirty shoes was nowhere to be seen.
	"Where did you bring him?" Ruby asked once the car door had closed behind Grace.
	"I told him I lost my watch back down the path," Grace said lightly. "I had him help me look for it and managed to sneak some pictures of him." She held out her phone to Ruby and swiped through the images. "Now we have his face."
	"I can't say I've seen him before." Ruby enlarged the image on the screen. "If he does work at the same company as my dad, he probably isn't a very important figure. Maybe Mr. Stevenson bought him off."
	"I'll text these pictures to you. You should still show them to your dad just in case he knows who the man is."
	
~

	The waiting around was the worst part. Ruby wasn't sure how she felt about going outside in case someone decided to watch or follow her again. What if there had been more than one person watching her? What if the man with the dirty shoes wasn't the only one?
	Later in the day, Tomas took Ruby's bike to take over the position of watching the boat from Tye. So far there hadn't been any movement, but the man with the dirty shoes wasn't showing any sign of leaving.
	"I don't know if he plans to stay there all night," was the first thing Tye said when he came in through the front door. "That man just won't leave."
	After what felt like ages, Ruby's parents finally returned to the house.

	"Grace did," Ruby explained.

	That's because he found something even more profitable. Ruby closed her eyes for a brief moment.
	"What was Mr. Stevenson doing on the farm in the first place?" Ruby's mom asked.
	"The higher-ups put him in charge of it," Ruby's dad said darkly. "They liked the way he was working it. He always had a way of producing the most amount of goods with the least amount of money. But his methods have always been shady, and someone's always getting hurt because of him. All these years he's been trying to hide it, but now with what happened at the farm, we have enough proof to keep him away from the position of CEO for good."
	Ruby looked at her dad. "So you're going to become the CEO, then?"
	"I am." Her dad's expression melted into a brief and satisfied smile. "Stevenson didn't even try to defend himself. I think he realizes he's at the end of the line he himself threw."
	Ruby held her dad's gaze. "Ba, I need your help."
	"My help? What's going on?"
	"I'm afraid Mr. Stevenson might be up to something bad. He kidnapped someone."
	"He-he what?" Ruby's dad stared at her in disbelief.
	"He kidnapped someone," Ruby repeated. "He had sent someone to follow me, and I witnessed it."
	"We need to go to the police," Ruby's dad said, turning to make his way to the door. 
	"No." Ruby swiftly moved to block her father's path. "We can't go to the police about this."
	"Why not?" Ruby's mom asked faintly.
	"I didn't want to tell you in case you went to the police, but now I realize that I have no choice but to ask for your help. Please, just let me explain."
	Ruby's dad walked over to the couch. "Tell us everything. And after you've explained what's going on, then we'll decide whether or not it would be for the best to go to the police."
	Ruby let out a sigh. "It's a complicated situation. In fact, the person who was kidnapped isn't exactly a person-she's a mermaid."
	"What?" Ruby's dad just stared at her.
	"Believe it or not," Ruby said firmly, "just please don't go to the police. No one knows about her existence. And that's why Mr. Stevenson is adamant about holding onto her."
	"I-" Ruby's dad stuttered, at a loss for words. "What?"
	"You don't have to do anything about the mermaid situation," Ruby cut him off. "All I'm asking is if you can try and go after him for the contaminated water. The more time he's preoccupied with something that isn't the mermaid, the better."
	"It's true that Mr. Stevenson was let off a little too lightly for nearly tainting our company's name . . ." Ruby's dad seemed to recover from his initial shock. "And while I wouldn't mind seeing him struggle to defend himself, you don't think the mermaid story is a little too unbelievable?"
	"What Ruby's saying is true," Mari piped up. "I believe Ruby. At first, I was skeptical, but then I thought, 'why can't merpeople exist?' Just because we've never seen them before doesn't mean they aren't out there somewhere."
	"She's right," Tye added. "If Mr. Stevenson exposes the mermaid to the world, the merpeople will never be able to live in peace again. There's a reason why they don't make their presence known to humans."
	"If Mr. Stevenson exposes the merpeople to the world," Grace said softly, "he'll become famous. And isn't that what he wants?"
	"We can't let that happen," Ruby's dad said darkly. "Mermaid or not, he can't go around kidnapping people. Tomorrow I'll bring up the issue of the contaminated water again and see if we can call Mr. Stevenson in. He's been ignoring our summons recently . . ."
	"Thank you," Ruby breathed. Then she blinked. "Oh, Ba, one last thing. Do you have any pictures of Mr. Stevenson on your phone? I don't think my friends know what he looks like."
	Ruby's dad pulled out his phone. "He's got a couple on the company website. I'll send you the link."
	Ruby nodded, and her phone vibrated as it received the message.
	"Where's Tomas?" Ruby's mom looked around, seeming to realize that Tomas was absent.
	"He's keeping an eye on the boat where the mermaid is being kept," Ruby explained.
	"Could you show me where this boat is?" Ruby's dad asked weakly. "I need to confirm for myself whether Stevenson really is doing something that can get him in a big pile of trouble. Maybe this will be my chance to get him out of the workplace once and for all."
	"I can show you the way." Ruby rose to her feet, and her dad followed her lead. She looked over her shoulder at her friends before slipping outside. They'd take care of the boy with the sea-glass-colored hair in her absence.
	There was silence in the car, save for Ruby's quiet instructions of "right" and "take a left there." When they arrived at the parking lot above the dock, the two of them got out of the car. Ruby spotted Tomas almost instantly. Tomas seemed to spot them just as quickly, and his brows arched in a silent question.
	Ruby just beckoned Tomas to come over to them. "My dad wants to assess the situation," Ruby told him quietly when he came to a stop beside her.
	"I've realized that by standing over there"-Tomas pointed to where he had previously been looking out over the water-"the man with the dirty shoes can't see us. There's something about the way the grass covers the slope that makes it nearly impossible to be spotted from down on the dock. I found it by accident, but I've been taking advantage of it ever since."
	"It's brilliant," Ruby whispered as the two of them watched her dad make his way down to the dock. "Let's go over there and watch."
	Crouching down behind the tall grass, Ruby looked down at the sand and the wooden dock below. Her dad had made his way over to the man with the dirty shoes and seemed to have struck up a conversation with him. Finally, Ruby's dad turned and made his way back up the slope. His expression was grim.
	"He's really got someone on that boat," Ruby's dad muttered as he climbed back into the car. Ruby followed him, leaving Tomas to continue watching the dock.
	"What do you propose to do?" Ruby asked cautiously.
	Ruby's dad drummed his fingers on the car's steering wheel. "I'll try and talk to Mr. Stevenson."
	"Would talking to him really make him release his prisoner?"
	"I'll put together an argument to present to the higher-ups about why Stevenson should be fired," Ruby's dad said darkly. "Let's see how confident he is once he's lost his job."
	"But wouldn't that-?"
	Ruby's dad looked over at his daughter. "Once his pride has been injured, he'll do something rash-he'll make a move. That will be our chance to catch him."
	As they drove back to the house, Ruby looked out the window and watched the clouds in the vibrant blue sky. "We know where the mermaid is being kept on the boat," Ruby said after a while. "She's below deck in a locked room."
	"You've been on the boat?"
	"Yeah . . . we sneaked on."
	"Is freeing a mermaid really worth your safety? If you're caught sneaking around in places you shouldn't be, you could be caught by the police."
	"Isn't freeing the mermaid the right thing to do? I-we need to protect them. If other people find out about them, they'll be forced to leave their home here and will always be on the run from humans." Ruby let out a sigh as they pulled into the driveway. "Ba, there's someone I'd like you to meet."

    Chapter 15

	Mari sat on the ground, her chin resting on her hands as she gazed out at the dock. Just a week ago, Mari had been ready to spend the majority of her summer in her room, trying to ignore the messages from random people on the internet whom she could never seem to fully block out. She never had expected this from her summer vacation.
	Mari absently watched the man with the dirty shoes as he pace back and forth. She wondered how much he was being paid to stand there all day. He had to leave eventually, didn't he?
	Suddenly, there was movement from the far side of the dock. A man in tropical-patterned shorts and a matching shirt was walking toward the man with the dirty shoes.
	Mari quickly set her phone to record. From the pictures Ruby had shared with them of Mr. Stevenson, the man in the colorful outfit looked just like him. Mari couldn't hear their conversation, but the man with the dirty shoes kept pointing at the boat. She could tell he was getting more and more exasperated as they spoke, his gestures becoming increasingly impatient. Finally, their conversation ended, and Mr. Stevenson walked away.
	Mari zoomed in with her phone camera on the man with the dirty shoes. He was grumbling as he glared after Mr. Stevenson. Mari stopped her recording and sent it to the group chat before quickly typing, Man with the dirty shoes doesn't seem to always get along with Mr. Stevenson. Could that work in our favor?
	Then Mari's fingers stilled over the keys, and her head snapped back to Mr. Stevenson's retreating figure. Mr. Stevenson had finally shown himself. This was an opportunity that couldn't be wasted. Scrambling to her feet, Mari hurried to trail after him, typing a new message as she went. I'm going to follow Mr. Stevenson. Someone else might want to watch the dock in my place. Tucking her phone away, Mari quickened her pace. Fortunately, Mr. Stevenson was very easy to spot in his colorful attire.
	Eventually, Mr. Stevenson reached a flight of steps built into the rocky slope leading up to the main road, and Mari made sure to fall back to leave a block's worth of space between them. The further she went from the dock and the house where Ruby and her family were staying, the more uncertain Mari began to feel. What if she got caught? What if she got lost?
	Mari wasn't particularly worried about getting lost-she had her phone on her, after all. But then again, Mari had only been on the island a day, and the buildings and trees had yet to look familiar.
	After some time, Mr. Stevenson came to a stop at a cafe. He entered the building and vanished from sight. Mari lingered at the entrance for a good minute or two before entering as well. The chill of the air conditioning hit her full in the face the moment she stepped through the door.
      Mr. Stevenson was waiting in the line at the counter, and Mari quietly joined it as well. Mari watched as Mr. Stevenson ordered a coffee and then sat at one of the tables.
      Glancing up at the menu, Mari decided to order a fruit smoothie for herself. It would look suspicious for her to be hanging around in the cafe otherwise. After she had placed her order, Mari took a seat at the table directly behind Mr. Stevenson's. She pulled out her phone and pretended to be busy scrolling through her social media.
      Even after Mr. Stevenson's coffee arrived, he seemed too focused on typing on his phone, and the drink went untouched. Mari glanced over and caught a glimpse of Mr. Stevenson's screen. The tiny letters were too small to make out.
      Mr. Stevenson finally reached for his coffee and rose to his feet. Mari gave him a thirty-second start before she exited the cafe after him.
      This time, Mari walked closer to Mr. Stevenson. He seemed to be on a call with someone, and his voice was growing progressively louder. It seemed like whoever was on the other end of the phone wasn't liking what he was saying.
      "I told you to get the press out here as soon as possible!" Mr. Stevenson hissed into the phone. "What do you mean I need to get permission from the higher-ups? They've already permitted it! What? Now you're asking me for proof? What more proof do you need? You'll regret it if you don't show up! I'm warning you-hello? Hello?"
      Cursing, Mr. Stevenson angrily looked down at his phone. His pace had increased, and Mari had to quicken her own to keep up. After dialing a new number, Mr. Stevenson put his phone back to his ear.
      "Hello? Yes, I'm Mr. Stevenson. Did you get the email I sent you? The pictures I enclosed? What do you mean I'm playing a joke? This is not a scam." Mr. Stevenson's voice was calm even though Mari could see his free hand clenching and unclenching. "Just send a couple of people out. A couple of people are all we need. I promise you I'm speaking nothing but the truth. Yes, call me back once you've thoroughly considered the offer."
      Mari only realized she was holding her breath when her lungs began to strain. Coughing, she took a drink of her smoothie. She walked faster and passed by Mr. Stevenson. Now in front of him, she could feel his eyes on the back of her head as she pulled out her phone, pretending to check her text messages.
      Mari wasn't sure how far away she was from the dock now-it felt as if she could have been tailing Mr. Stevenson for hours. Looking down at her phone, Mari really did check her messages this time. All of her friends had sent her messages warning her to be careful and that following Mr. Stevenson could be dangerous.
      After reassuring them that she was alright, Mari quickly typed down everything she had overheard about Mr. Stevenson wanting to get the press out as soon as possible. If Mr. Stevenson really did get the press to come out, they'd most likely show up the following morning. So that meant . . . if they wanted to free the mermaid, they'd have to act tonight.
      Mari's phone buzzed, and she squinted to see the screen against the glare of the sun. She slowed and let Mr. Stevenson pass her back up. The message was from Tomas. Mari, Ruby's parents are taking us out to dinner, Tomas's message read. What time do you think you'll be back? We'll wait for you.
      Don't wait for me, Mari typed quickly. I still want to follow Mr. Stevenson a little longer.
      Grace and Ruby went to the locksmith with a picture of the lock. Tomas informed her. Turns out the lock itself isn't a very complex one. They were able to get a key. Once night falls, we'll try and make a move. Ruby's parents are helping us now. I think we might have a chance.
      
~

	Mari had followed Mr. Stevenson to several different buildings. One of them was a restaurant, where he spent a good hour inside. Mari had lingered outside the entire time. She had undone her hair, hoping that under the cover of night, she'd look different enough that Mr. Stevenson wouldn't start suspecting anything. Or maybe he already had begun to suspect her. She wasn't completely sure.
	Finally, Mr. Stevenson walked into a house. Mari lingered around the premises for a good ten minutes, and after snapping a picture of the address, she turned around and hurried back the way she had come. Night had fallen, and as Mari walked, she began to get the feeling that someone was following her. But whenever she snuck a glance over her shoulder, she couldn't see anyone through the dark.
      Starting to feel a little uneasy, Mari picked up her pace. She was far from the house Ruby was staying at . . . a little too far. Mari was speed walking now as her heart pounded a little too quickly in her chest. Why had she followed Mr. Stevenson for so long?
	Suddenly feeling not very confident anymore, Mari felt her spine prickle, and then a moment later, she collided with someone. Mari nearly let out a cry as she staggered. Before she could topple onto the pavement, a rouge hand caught her by the arm and set her upright.
	"Are you alright, miss?" a man's voice asked.
	"Yes," Mari said shakenly as she dropped her gaze. "I'm so sorry-I didn't mean to run into you . . ." Even in the dark, she recognized those shoes caked with dirt. It was the man from the dock. Mari looked up, thunderstruck. The man had left the dock? "I'm sorry," Mari repeated again, quicker this time. "I got to go!"
	Sprinting off, Mari could feel the man's eyes lingering on her back. Mari hurried onward past the dock. The ocean was painted in shades of rippling silver, and the entire world was enveloped in the color of the night. There was something beautiful about it, and if Mari hadn't been in such a rush, she would have stood there on the street to gaze out at where the ocean met the sky.
	Mari finally arrived at the house, and she nearly blinked at the time when she checked her phone. It was ten o'clock. Still clutching a stitch in her side, Mari rang the doorbell. The door opened a moment later to reveal a very worried-looking Tomas.
	"Mari!" Tomas quickly stepped aside to let Mari cross the threshold. "You didn't respond to any of our messages-we were starting to get worried something had happened to you."
	"I'm fine," Mari panted. "I found out where Mr. Stevenson is staying. And then-and then on my way back, I ran into the man who was watching the dock. Now thinking about it, he wouldn't stay there all night, would he? There shouldn't be anyone on the dock right now!"
	After closing the door behind Mari, Tomas walked over to where the others were sitting on the couch. "Where are your parents?" Mari asked, realizing that Ruby's parents were absent from the picture.
	"My mom went to bed early," Ruby explained. "My dad left again to talk to his co-workers about Mr. Stevenson. He should be back soon."
	"Should we go?" Grace asked uncertainly.
	"This might be our only chance," Ruby said grimly. "Now we have a key."
	Tye looked at them. "Shouldn't we wait until it gets later? There could still be other people around the dock."
	Ruby pressed her hands to the sides of her face. "I don't know. None of us are watching the dock anymore. What if the mermaid is moved?"
	"Let's wait an hour, then," Tomas suggested. "Mari still hasn't had anything to eat."
	Mari blinked. That was true. She hadn't realized how hungry she was until her stomach let out a grumble.

~

	Mari stood next to the car as her friends quickly climbed out and hurried down the slope. Mari looked on worriedly. It was dark, and if they weren't careful, someone was going to get injured.
	The five of them had left the merman back at the house. He had fallen asleep, and he had seemed so exhausted that none of them had the heart to wake him.
	Mari tugged on one of her braids as she squinted into the dark. By now, all of her friends should have arrived at the bottom of the slope. Now it was her turn.
	As they made their way through the sand and then over the wood of the dock, each footstep sounded like a cannon blast in the stillness of the night. Mari couldn't help but get an uneasy feeling as the five of them easily climbed onto the boat.
	After hurrying down the stairs to the locked door, Ruby fumbled with the keys in the dark. "I can't see anything," she said with a grimace.
	Suddenly a light flickered to life. Mari whirled, and the brightness blinded her as she turned directly into it. From next to her, Mari could hear Tomas inhale sharply.
	"Does this help?" a voice asked.
	Mari squinted past the light to the man silhouetted behind it. She grabbed Tomas's arm in a panic. "That's Mr. Stevenson!"
	"What are you kids doing on my boat?" Mr. Stevenson asked.
	"Why did you send someone to follow me?" Ruby countered. She handed the key to the door to Tye before stepping up to stand in front of her friends.
	"Me?" Mr. Stevenson just let out a good-natured chuckle. "Send someone to follow you? What kind of nonsense are you talking about?"
	Ruby angled her head to the side. "So you won't admit it? Even when we have proof?"
	"Proof?" Mr. Stevenson asked sharply. His composure melted for a brief moment. "What proof?"
	Ruby placed a hand on her hip. "We have photos."
	"That still doesn't answer the question of why you kids are on my boat." Mr. Stevenson folded his arms over his chest. Mari shrunk back into the darkness. They were practically deer in headlights. And with Mr. Stevenson on the top of the stairs . . . would he let them pass? Would he escort them off the boat? Or was he trying to stall for time?
	"Oh, I've already called the police." Mr. Stevenson was smiling now. "You kids should know better than to try and run. You should be mature enough to take responsibility for your actions."
	"And what about your actions?" Ruby countered calmly. "You contaminated he water. Your company could get in serious trouble for that. Would you shoulder the blame yourself?"

	Ruby ignored his remark. "My dad was never wrong when he complained about you."

	"We know who you're holding behind this door." Mari stepped back up to stand next to Ruby. "Just let her go-this isn't right."
	"Why should I be afraid of a bunch of kids like you?" Mr. Stevenson said unpleasantly. "What are you all anyway? Some sort of gang? A gang threatening me with violence?"

	Mr. Stevenson sneered. "Oh, but the police are already on their way."
	"You're despicable," Tomas said. Even though his voice was quiet, it was anything but weak.
	"And you're a bunch of kids." Mr. Stevenson brushed him off.
	Ruby folded her arms over her chest. "You know what? We'll stay right here until the police arrive. When we open this door and they find what you've been hiding inside, you realize you'll have a lot of explaining to do."
	"Open the door?" Mr. Stevenson chuckled. "But what if I told you there was nothing behind it? I'm not hiding anything."

I'm not going to let anyone take that fame away from me. Just wait until the press gets here Thursday morning-then everyone will know what I've found."

	"Don't do this." Ruby held Mr. Stevenson's gaze. "Do you know that you'll ruin their lives by showing them to the world?"

	Tye frowned. "We wouldn't."
	"And that's why I'm going to be famous, and you kids are going to jail."
	Ruby opened her mouth and then closed it again as Mr. Stevenson walked away, laughing. The police cars had pulled into the parking lot, and the police themselves had their flashlights out as they hurried down the slope.
	The police arrived at the boat a moment later. One of them grabbed Ruby and Mari by the arms and dragged them up the steps. Mr. Stevenson stood off to the side. "These kids trespassed onto my boat. When I told them off, they even threatened me!"

	"I'm disappointed in you." Ruby stared at him in contempt. "You had to resort to this all to get a minute of fame."

Let's give it an hour or two, and then we'll all meet back at the house to continue brainstorming."
	"Who's going to be the one going alone?" Grace asked uncertainly. "The last time Ruby was out alone, she was almost kidnapped by the man with the dirty shoes."
	"I could be the one going alone," Tye offered. "Besides, I won't be completely alone. I'll take Singsing with me." He gestured to the puppy for emphasis. Singsing was watching them almost resentfully from the corner of the room. The puppy wasn't used to being this ignored.
	Grace leveled her brother a look. "I'll go with Singsing. Ruby was the original target, remember? I know I'll feel better if the two of you go together."
	"We'll do it that way, then."
	Mari turned to look at the former merman. "What about Aouli?"
	Ruby closed her eyes for a brief moment. "I think he'll be fine here by himself. I'll go leave him a quick note just in case. I hope this communicates that we've gone out for a short time." When Ruby finished her drawing, she set it down on the coffee table in front of Aouli. "Stick figures are the ultimate universal language, no?"

~

	"So far we've got two people who are going to attend for sure." Ruby counted off on her fingers. "And five people who will think about it."
	"And then quite a lot more who declined entirely," Tye said with a sigh.
	"Well, expecting everyone we ask to show up would be a little unrealistic. Look"-Ruby pointed to a group of preteens standing in front of an ice cream truck. "What do you say we ask them next?"
	Tye followed Ruby's gaze to the kids. "You can do the talking this time. Everything I say tends to goes over the heads of anyone younger than me."
	Ruby walked over to the preteens. "Hello, would you care to join us in a peaceful protest against environmental harm?"
	"When it is?" one of the preteens asked at the same time a second said a very blatant "no." The two preteens blinked as they looked at each other and then back at Ruby.
	"When is it?" the first preteen asked again.
	"Tomorrow morning," Ruby explained. "A businessman who just got busted for contaminating the water around the island is going to be interviewed by the press for his achievements. We can't let them overlook the harm he's done. If you'd like, you can scan the QR code on my phone for more information."
	The preteen nodded before scanning Ruby's phone and scrolling through the information.
	"Should we make signs?" the preteen asked.
	"Signs?"
	"Yeah, it's a protest, right?"
	"If you want to make signs, by all means, go ahead."
	The second preteen tugged on the first's sleeve. "Are you really going to go?"
	"We weren't going to do anything tomorrow anyway," the first one remarked. "Haven't you ever wanted to be part of something bigger? Something important?"
	"No," the second said flatly.
	Ruby smiled at the first preteen. "I'm really happy that you'll be there."
	The preteen grinned back, and Ruby gave the two of them a wave before heading off back to where Tye was standing a short distance away.
	"One last thing!" the first preteen called out. Ruby paused and looked over her shoulder expectantly. "Your hair is super cool!"
	At that, Ruby burst out laughing. "Thanks!"
	"Is he your boyfriend?" the second called and pointed at Tye before the first smacked the second's hand away.
	Tye sighed as the two of them waved to the preteens before continuing on their way. "You do better with the younger kids than me. I always find them a handful to deal with."
	"At least now we've got another person that might show up," Ruby said lightly. "We've still got another twenty minutes or so before we're supposed to be back at the house. "Let's see if we can get at least three more."
	"Three might be asking for a lot." Tye looked around the shopping center they had just arrived at. "There are fewer people here than I thought there would be."
	"We just missed the lunch crowd," Ruby observed. "It's fine though. Look-there are some people in the parking lot."
	Tye picked up his pace. "Quick, let's get them before they run away."
	Laughing, Ruby hurried after him.

~

	"I got twenty people," Grace said proudly. Singsing was sitting on her lap as the five of them sat on the living room floor.
	"Twenty?" Mari stared at her, clearly impressed. "How did you get twenty?"
	Grace giggled. "They were attracted to Singsing. Almost everyone I passed asked me if they could pet her, and while they were captivated by Singsing's charm, I asked them if they'd want to show up to the protest. Quite a lot of them said yes."
	Ruby stared at the puppy. "Maybe we should go out again with Singsing later. Lucky dog indeed."
	Mari held up her fingers to count all the people they had gotten combined. "We've got a little over forty people who will show up," she announced.
	Tye blinked. "That's actually pretty good. Forty people would be a sizable crowd."
	Mari beamed. "And that's not including those Mr. Kekoa is getting. I think we can call this half of our plan a success."
	"Now we just need to go back to thinking of ways to get onto the boat," Ruby said tiredly. The crease between her brows returned. "Even if we can get onto the boat, how would we know where the mermaid is? How do we know security won't just throw us off?"
	"You know what," Mari said suddenly, and everyone turned to look at her. "Uh"-Mari hesitated at all the sudden attention-"he's waiting for the press to go onto the boat. What if we just pretend to be part of the press?"
	Ruby blinked at her friend. "Would that work?"
	"I don't see why not," Tye said slowly. "If we can somehow disguise ourselves enough, it might be our best option."

~

	As she stood by the dock, Ruby was starting to feel her nerves. Surprisingly enough, she had actually been able to get a full night's sleep the previous night. Now the tiredness of the previous few days had washed away to leave Ruby with a very anxious sort of feeling.
	She had already split up from her friends; Mari had met the protesters in front of the boat with a sign of her own. There actually was quite the crowd, and Ruby had to hand it to Mr. Kekoa for going above and beyond with his part.
	Right now, Ruby was waiting in line with a group of people from the press. Aouli stood next to her, looking just as nervous as Ruby felt. The two of them had arrived at the docks very early in the morning, accompanied by Ruby's dad. A couple of people from the press were already there setting up. And after a lot of talking, Ruby's dad had managed to convince them to let Ruby and Aouli tag along.
	The protesters had started to show up at the dock about an hour later, and all of them were waiting for Mr. Stevenson to make an appearance. Mr. Kekoa himself was in the crowd of protesters, and had swapped his police uniform for casual clothing.
	Ruby's dad would be watch from his car in the parking lot. He was stationed there just in case something went wrong and he needed to drive off to find help. Grace, Tye, and Tomas had joined a different group of reporters, and the three of them were waiting somewhere out of Ruby's line of sight.
	As she looked over at the faces of the people that had gathered, Ruby recognized a number of the people she and Tye had spoken to.
	Now staring out over the turquoise water, Ruby followed the waves to the horizon and her ink-black hair whipped around her face. The previous night, to complete their disguises, Ruby had taken a quick drive with Mari to buy the cheapest temporary hair dye they could find. Grace had helped Ruby dye her hair and then had done Aouli's as well. At first, the former merman had been a little apprehensive of the process, but when Ruby had shown him that the color washed out once it came into contact with water, he had let Grace go ahead.
      Mr. Stevenson would be here any minute now . . . There! Ruby's head snapped up as she caught a glimpse of movement out of the corner of her eye. A car was driving up to the dock, and after it parked a short distance away, the back door swung open to reveal a very confused-looking Mr. Stevenson.
	"That's him!" Mari's voice called from the crowd.
	And then the protesters brandished their signs at Mr. Stevenson and calls of, "What do you mean by polluting the waters of our island?" filled the air.
	"Who are all these people?" Mr. Stevenson demanded. His question was directed at the man climbing out of the car from the driver's seat, and Ruby recognized him almost immediately as the man with the dirty shoes.
	Regardless, the crowd parted for Mr. Stevenson as he matched toward the boat. They weren't here to cause trouble-Mari had made sure to make that part very clear.
	"Oh good." Mr. Stevenson looked in the direction of the camera crew Ruby and Aouli were blending in with. "The press is here. Quickly now, this way." Mr. Stevenson motioned for them to climb onto the boat after him.
	Ruby shuffled over with the rest of the camera crew, and Aouli followed close behind. Once they had boarded the boat, Ruby glanced around the deck. There was still no sign of the mermaid.
	"Let's set up the cameras here, shall we?" Mr. Stevenson was saying. "Wait-hey! No!"
	Ruby turned to watch Mr. Stevenson wave his hands angrily at the people from the press. Instead of setting up on the deck like he wanted him to, they had gone straight to the edge of the boat and set the cameras up to capture the protesters looking up at the boat from the dock.
	"You'll get your turn," the head camerawoman said cooly.
	"What?" Mr. Stevenson sputtered, stunned into silence. He just opened and close his mouth for a moment before he seemed to finally regain his voice. "How unprofessional! Who sent you people?"
	As Mr. Stevenson continued to try and fail to get the camera crew's attention back to him, Ruby and Aouli silently slipped off to the side. Ruby hurried around the outer deck, looking for any sort of door or room where Aouli's sister could be hidden inside. Finally, Ruby arrived at the very back of the boat. A single door stood in front of her.
	After taking a deep breath, Ruby reached out and tried the handle. The door didn't budge.
	"Are you looking for this?" a voice said. Ruby whirled around to find the man with the dirty shoes was standing in front of her with a key in his hands.
	"Is that the key to the door?" Ruby asked as innocently as she could. "Would you mind opening it for us?"
	"Are you Ruby?" the man asked as he eyed Ruby up and down.
	"Yes."
	The man held the key out to Ruby. "The key's all yours."
	"Seriously?" Ruby just stared at the man.
	"Take it."
	Cautiously, Ruby reached out and took the key from the man. "Why are you helping me?" Ruby asked as she carefully inserted the key into the lock. There was a soft click, and then the door swung open to reveal a flight of steps leading downward.
	"Your dad found me," the man with the dirty shoes admitted. "The police were there too. The police told me that Mr. Stevenson was about to get in a lot of trouble, and if I didn't want to go down with him, I had to do what they said. Besides, your dad offered me more money than Mr. Stevenson did."
	Ruby arched a brow. "You don't want to keep the mermaid?"
	"I do," the man said simply. "But I'd rather not spend the rest of my years in jail for a brief moment of fame."
	Ruby stepped aside. "If you're really helping me, bring the mermaid out."
	"Fine." The man with the dirty shoes sighed. Ruby watched as he stepped through the doorway and descended down the steps. Ruby let out a breath. If she had gone down those stairs by herself, she was half certain that the man with the dirty shoes would lock her inside.
	The man with the dirty shoes returned a moment later, dragging a pile of nets with him. Ruby hurried to help him, and together they carried the tangled mermaid up onto the deck. Aouli let out a strangled noise when his eyes fell on the heap of nets that encased his sister, and he dropped down next to her.
	The mermaid appeared to be unconscious, and red marks were all over her body from where the netting had dug into her flesh a little too tightly. Her skin was dry and flaky, and her hair was in tangles.
	Ruby turned to the man with the dirty shoes. "We need to get her into the water, quick!"
	He nodded, and together the man and Ruby tried to lift the mermaid up and over the railings of the deck. The only problem was that the mermaid probably weighed as much as Ruby, if not more, and with all the netting, it was difficult to get a firm grip on her. Even with Aouli trying his best to assist them, the three of them were struggling to lift the mermaid off the ground.
	Suddenly, there was the sound of hurried footsteps. Ruby froze, and her eyes widened in surprise as Grace, Tye, and Tomas rounded the corner.
	"Help us!" Ruby desperately mouthed to them.
	The three of them didn't need to be asked twice before they hurried over to help lift the mermaid.
	"We came here to warn you," Tye said through gritted teeth as the six of them began to lift the mermaid off the ground, "Mr. Stevenson's coming this way with the cameras!"
	"Hurry!"
	Lifting with all their might, the mermaid was heaved into the air, and with one final shove, the six of them pushed her over the railing. There was a splash as the mermaid hit the water, and her scaled tail glittered briefly in the light before she vanished beneath the crystal surface.
	"We did it!" Grace said in an excited whisper. "Now let's leave!"
	Nodding, Ruby hurried after Grace as her friend took off at a run back around the deck. But then a moment later, Grace froze. Ruby staggered to a stop as well.
	Mr. Stevenson stood in front of them, and his eyes practically burned with anger. The camera crew stood behind him, all sporting surprised expressions.
	"You!" Mr. Stevenson pointed widely at Ruby. "I should have known you'd be here!"
	Ruby folded her arms across her chest. "My work here is done. I've already transported your little surprise far away."
	"How dare you!" Mr. Stevenson's face with white with rage. "But the door-the key!"
	"You mean this key?" Ruby held out the key to the door. "That's right, I have it."
	"You've ruined everything!" Mr. Stevenson shrieked. And then he was shoving Grace out of the way as he charged toward Ruby.
	Ruby stagged backward in shock, and her hands went up instinctively to block her face as Mr. Stevenson's fists came flying toward her. But the blows never hit.
	Ruby blinked in surprise to find Aouli standing in front of her with Mr. Stevenson's fists stopped with his own. And then Mr. Stevenson was moving again. Even though Aouli actually appeared to be stronger than him in terms of physical strength, the former merman still wasn't completely accustomed to walking. His legs buckled, and he hit the railings of the boat as he tried his best to steady himself.
	Mr. Stevenson seemed to notice this and took the opportunity to lunge forward. One moment, Aouli was leaning against the railings, and the next, he was toppling backward, falling off the boat, down, down, until he hit the water with a splash.
	Ruby's feet were moving on their own as she flung herself against the railing. She leaned over to look down at the water. Aouli had to be alright. He was a merman after all. But he wasn't a merman anymore-at this moment, he was still a human. And as a human, he had never learned how to swim.

    Chapter 18

	The moment Aouli's head hit the water, the world went dark. Water flooded his lungs. He was choking, and his head spun. The ocean was his home. It had always been his home-his friend. But now, as the water pressed down on him, all he could feel was panic.
	Aouli thrashed out with his arms and kicked with his legs. But without his tail, he couldn't swim. And now here he was, being suffocated by the ocean.
	Aouli opened his eyes and watched the black ink from his hair drift in the water around him as he sunk down, down, down. In the distance, the sunlight glittered. The rays breaking through the water's surface were out of reach. They had been so close to the shore too . . . Why was the water so deep? Why was it so cold?
	Aouli's head felt light. His sister was safe now. The girl with the deep-red hair-Ruby-had helped free her. Aouli would forever be grateful for that. When the angry man had run at her, Aouli had found himself moving on his own. He had been too rash again. What did he think he could have done when he couldn't even walk properly? He was indebted to Ruby, though. She had done so much for him.
	Then Aouli blinked. His eyes were stinging from the water. That was right-his sister had to be around here somewhere. But as he turned his head, he couldn't see anything through the water. This vision was starting to blur . . .
	Suddenly, there was a splash, and then something was shooting through the water toward him. Aouli blinked again, squinting through the water.
      It was Ruby.
	She was swimming toward him, and the black dye in her hair was streaming off her to reveal the deep red beneath. Ruby stretched out her hand toward Aouli. Aouli didn't hesitate before he reached up. His fingertips strained against the heaviness of the water, and then his hand was in Ruby's. A moment later, he was being pulled upward, out of the water and back toward the surface.
	Aouli's head broke through the surface, and he found himself gasping for breath as icy wind stung his face. Ruby gently tugged on his arm and guided him toward the shore. Aouli let her help him onto the stretch of sand a short distance from the docks. Ruby's friends hurried up to meet them. All of them were speaking, but Aouli still couldn't understand their words. He just lay there in the sand.
	Suddenly, Aouli sat up. His sister was still caught up in all the netting. She was hurt.
	Ruby turned to look at him in concern, and Aouli pointed to the water, trying his best to gesture that his sister was still in the ocean. Ruby just looked at him in confusion before her eyes widened in understanding. She said something to her friends, and then one of them hurried off.
	Completely exhausted, Aouli flopped back down onto the sand and stared up at the cloudless sky. Exhausting. These past couple of days had been nothing but exhausting. Well, that wasn't entirely true. It had been thrilling in a way to live a different kind of life from the one he was used to. He just wished the circumstances had been different.
	Ulani had told him that he had about three days as a human-which meant that tonight he would be transforming back. Even though he felt relieved that Healani was out of the grasp of that troublesome man, she was still floating somewhere in the water near the boat. Aouli couldn't help worry that if anyone checked the waters carefully, his sister would easily be recaptured.
	He had no way to get in touch with his father or even the people from the village now. Aouli just hoped Healani would be able to make it until he could transform back and bring her to the village.
	There was the sound of footsteps, and Aouli looked up to see the man who had introduced himself as Kekoa.
	"My sister," Aouli's lunges were still heavy as he coughed out. "She's still in the water."
	"I've sent people to watch the area," Kekoa informed him with a faint smile. "With them there, you don't need to worry about her."
	Aouli let out a breath. "Thank you."
	Kekoa took a seat on the sand next to Aouli. "Ruby's asking if you're alright. All your friends here had quite the fright when you were pushing into the water."
	"I'm fine now." Aouli turned to Ruby and offered the red-haired girl a smile. Kekoa translated his words, and the girl smiled back with relieved eyes.
	"What happened to the angry man?" Aouli asked, turning back to Kekoa.
	Kekoa frowned slightly. "I'm not too sure. I didn't see him get off the boat. He's probably in a lot of trouble now. There were a lot of witnesses, after all. No matter what his excuses are, he's not getting off easy."
	"Can he get Ruby and her friends in trouble for sneaking onto the boat and freeing my sister?" Aouli asked worriedly.
	"Technically, Ruby and her friends were allowed on," Kekoa said thoughtfully. "As for freeing your sister, there were very few people who knew about her existence in the first place. We humans will find it very hard to believe him if he continues to rant that he captured one of the sea people. Even if he has images of her, they still won't believe him."
	"Good." Aouli looked out over the water. "That's good."
	"What do you plan to do now?" Kekoa asked lightly.
	Aouli gazed off at the horizon. "I still have until nightfall before I turn back. I supposed I should make the most of my last hours with my new friends."
	Kekoa smiled. "Go have some fun. I promise the angry man won't be going anywhere near your sister."
	Aouli nodded gratefully.
	"I should be going now." Kekoa rose to his feet and dusted sand from his legs. "I've got to take care of the angry man."
	"Wait." Aouli looked up at him. "Do you think I'll see you again? I still have some words I'd like you to pass on to Ruby and her friends for me."
	"I'll stop by to visit in the evening," Kekoa reassured him. "Don't worry."
	Aouli watched Kekoa's retreating figure until he disappeared from sight. A moment later, there was someone else hurrying toward them. Aouli recognized the man as Ruby's father. He was hurrying down the stretch of sand. He skidded to a stop in front of his daughter, and despite her soaked state, threw his arms around her in a tight embrace.
	Ruby's expression was one of surprise as she blinked over her father's shoulders. Ruby's father finally drew away, and his tone was worried as he spoke to her. Ruby's expression melted into a reassuring smile, and her own tone was comforting as she tried to calm her father down.
	Ruby's father just brushed sand from his daughter's hair, still shaking his head as if he couldn't believe what had happened. When he finally seemed to calm down, he motioned for everyone to follow him back to the car. Ruby herself helped Aouli to his feet and helped him sling an arm around her shoulders for support.
	The crowd of people in front of the boat were now angrily yelling up at it and waving their signs in the air. As Aouli watched, the angry man was escorted off the boat with his hands chained in front of him.
	When they arrived back at the house, Ruby's mother was waiting outside to greet them. Her face was pale and her voice was anxious. Ruby quickly explained what had happened to her, but whatever she had said seemed to make her mother even more horrified.
	After some more talking, they entered the house, and Ruby led Aouli and her friends upstairs. Ruby and her friends chatted excitedly together for a while. Aouli sat there, listening to their voices. Even though he couldn't directly communicate with any of them, they had felt like his own friends since the first day he met them.
	Eventually, one of Ruby's friends, the girl with the light hair, pulled out the little rectangular device all five of the friends seemed to have. After some more talking, Ruby smiled, and her friends all hurried behind her. Ruby gestured for Aouli to join them, and he scooted over expectantly.
	All of their faces were reflected back at them from the screen of the device, and when the girl with the light hair tapped it, the image froze. Aouli blinked as the girl showed the image to him. That was the six of them-their faces forever captured in that brief moment of time. Aouli looked down at it in awe. It was almost like magic.
	But speaking of magic, Ulani's magic was about to come to an end. Outside the window, the sun was beginning to drop closer and closer to the horizon. Aouli rose to his feet and pointed at the sky outside.
	Ruby seemed to understand what he was saying and nodded her head. The six of them headed back downstairs, and after Aouli had bid Ruby's parents farewell, they were making their way outside.
	In the distance, someone very familiar was walking toward them. Aouli pointed, and Ruby's friends followed his gaze to the figure-it was Kekoa.
	Ruby and her friends waited for Kekoa to reach them before they made their way down to the beach together.
	"I don't have long now before I transform back," Aouli told Kekoa as they all stood barefoot by the water, letting the waves wash over their feet as the sun continued to drop in the sky. The world was painted in shades of deep orange and magenta, and the clouds had taken on the same hues. Aouli closed his eyes and breathed in the ocean air. When he opened his eyes, he turned to Kekoa. "Do you think you could ask Ruby if I'll see her again?"
	Kekoa nodded and turned to relay the message to Ruby.
	"Ruby says that she will be here on the island for a little longer," Kekoa informed him of Ruby's response. "But she also says that she won't be able to stay here forever. She had to go back to her own home."
	"So she's just a visitor here." Aouli looked out over the water. All the colors of the sunset were reflected in its calm mirror.
	Kekoa smiled faintly. "Ruby does say that she will come back to visit, though. It doesn't have to be goodbye forever when she leaves."
	"I don't mind waiting." Aouli tore his gaze away from the water to look at Ruby. "I'll be looking forward to seeing an old friend again. Speaking of friends . . ." For the longest time, he had been avoiding one of his oldest and closest friends back in the village. Ruby wasn't the only one who had helped him out-Ulani had also always been there looking out for him.
	Once he got back to the village, he'd try to make it up with Ulani. He'd fix their friendship and do his best to restore the bond the two of them once had.
	Day slowly melted into night, and the stars flickered to life. The ocean itself had taken on a silvery sheen, and the clouds turned invisible in the darkness.
	Aouli looked over at Kekoa. "I guess I should be off." As much as he wanted to spend his last moments as a human with his new friends, he could tell that they too were exhausted from the day's events.
	Aouli turned to look at his friends, offering each of them a wave. He looked at Ruby last and gave her a smile.
	Ruby smiled back as she raised her own hand in a gesture of farewell.
	This wasn't goodbye, Aouli had to remind himself as he waded out into the water. He might even be able to see Ruby and her friends the following day.
	Up to his shoulders in the water, Aouli turned and watched as Ruby, her friends, and Kekoa make their way toward the house. Aouli smiled faintly to himself as he watched them. He raised his own hand in a gesture of farewell even though he knew they couldn't see it.
	When they had vanished from his sight, Aouli got to work removing his clothes. He'd bring them back to Ruby the next time he saw her-they belonged to her father, after all.
	Then looking up at the sky, Aouli waited there for what could have been either minutes or hours before he felt a tingling sensation creep up his body. It only lasted a few seconds, and when it faded, Aouli could sense instantly that his tail had returned. The sea-glass-colored scales gleamed in the moonlight, and Aouli let out a joyous laugh before he dove into the water.
      After stashing the clothes in a safe place, Aouli shot through the water toward where his sister had fallen. When he finally arrived at the dock, he didn't have to look around for long before he spotted her. But she wasn't alone.
	"Ulani?" Aouli blinked in surprise as he swam over to join his friend.
	"Aouli!" Ulani beamed up at him.
	"What are you doing here?"
	"I got a vision that you were in danger," Ulani said seriously. "I swam as quickly as I could to find you, but when I arrived, you were gone. I found Healani here instead and thought I should try to cut her free."
	"Any success?" Aouli asked quickly.
	"None." Ulani shook her head sadly. "She's been unconscious all this time too . . . I left all my medicine and things back at my cave, but I've been a little hesitant to leave her. I'm so glad that you showed up."
	"What have you been using to try and cut the net?"
	"This." Ulani held out a sharp-edged rock to Aouli.
	Aouli gingerly took the rock from her and tried his hand at sawing away at the nets binding his sister. But after much struggle, he too was unsuccessful. Aouli took hold of one of his sister's arms. "Help me take her back to the village. My father will know what to do."
	"Maybe we've been looking at this incorrectly this entire time," Ulani said after a while as the two of them swam through the dark water. "If we can't cut the net off, can't we take it off some other way? Find the edge of it and pull it off that way?"
	"It's worth giving it a shot."
	Together, Aouli and Ulani let Healani go. As she floated in the water, the two of them searched for the edge of the net. Ulani found it first, and Aouli swam around to help her untangle it. And a few minutes later, Healani was free.
	Aouli looked down at the net in his hands. "We should find some way to dispose of this later." Aouli and Ulani swam the rest of the way back to the village with Healani pulled limply along between them.
	When they neared the village, despite it being late into the night, there were quite a few villagers still out. They seemed to notice Aouli and Ulani almost instantly and quickly swam over to greet them.
	"Aouli!" One of them looked at Aouli as if she couldn't believe her eyes. "The high chief is worried sick about you!"
	Aouli sighed. "I shouldn't have left the way I did without telling him. That was my mistake. Where is my father anyway? I've brought my sister back home."
	"Healani is back!" Another one of them blinked as if they had suddenly just noticed the limp figure being carried between Aouli and Ulani. "What-what happened to her?"
	"She's unconscious," Aouli said grimly. "We should send her over to the village healers immediately."
	"I can take her there," Ulani offered. "You should go find your father and tell him the good news."
	Aouli nodded his head. He made sure his sister was safe hands before swimming off to his father's residence. When he finally arrived, he found his father pacing back and forth outside it. His hands were clasped behind his back, and he had dark circles under his eyes. "Father." Aouli hesitantly swam over to him.
	Aouli's father whirled around to face his son. "Aouli?"
	Aouli hung his head. "I'm sorry for leaving without telling you. But I managed to get my sister back with help from my new friends, and-" But before Aouli could continue, his father cut him off with a laugh. Aouli just stared at his father as he laughed and laughed and laughed. "Father?"
	"You don't know how glad I am that you're back," his father said. "You don't know how glad I am that you're safe. Your sister, too. I was so worried that you had been captured as well-so worried that I had just lost both of my dear children."
	"I didn't want to make you worry," Aouli apologized. "I was just desperate at the time and knew of a way I might be able to free Healani. But I also knew you wouldn't approve, so I had no other choice than to go do it on my own."
	His father's smile faded. "You should have at least left a note of some sort. I asked everyone if they had seen you, and you can imagine how worried I was when no one had. I went as far as asking your old friend Ulani, and even she wouldn't tell me where you were."
	"She didn't want you to worry either."
	"So the two of you were working together. Just what exactly was it did you do?"
	"I asked Ulani to turn me into a human," Aouli said truthfully. "I didn't want to do it initially, but we needed to get Healani back."
	Aouli's father opened his mouth but then closed it again when no sound came out. Instead, he just shook his head. "Where's your sister now?" he finally asked.
	"Ulani took her to the village healer. I can take you there now."
	Aouli's father just nodded, and the two of them turned and swam through the waters.
	When they arrived at the healer's place, a crowd of people had already gathered around Healani. Glowing shells and rocks illuminated the space, casting everyone's faces in an assortment of interesting shadows.
	Healani floated in the water in the middle of all of them, and as Aouli looked on, he was pleased to say that Ulani was working alongside the elderly healer.
	"How is she?" The crowd parted for Aouli's father as he swam over to his daughter.
	"She's in no critical condition," the healer explained with a faint smile on her face. "She was rendered unconscious for being out of the water for too long, but now that's she back, she should wake in a couple of hours."
	"Just what happened to her?" Aouli's father looked on at the red marks from the netting that covered Healani's body. There was something like heartbreak in his voice.
	"It was the nets," Ulani explained sadly. "The humans didn't bother to try and be gentle."
	Aouli's father's eyes darkened. "Those humans."
	"Father," Aouli said quickly, "not all the humans are bad. The humans are actually the ones who help me free Healani."
	Aouli's father sighed heavily. "Humans are dangerous, Aouli."
	Aouli looked over at his father. "Yes, I know. But not all of them. They're also kind. What about the humans who have been protecting us for generations? Haven't they always been helping us?"
	Aouli's father sighed again. "Maybe I have been too quick to judge them all as a whole."
	"Humans are always going to be here living alongside us," Aouli continued. "If you always live with that distrust, you'll miss the opportunities to make peace."
	Suddenly, there was movement from where Healani was floating in the water, and her eyes slowly fluttered open.
	"Healani!" Aouli was at his sister's side in an instant.
	Healani blinked, and her voice was weak. "Aouli?"
	"You're safe now." Aouli's face melted into a smile. "You're home."
	Healani looked at Aouli. "I heard you call out to me from the other side of the door on the boat. Even when I was moved-you knew where to find me."
	"I wouldn't just leave you there at the mercy of that angry man," Aouli reassured his sister. Then he turned to face his father. "The angry man was the one who kidnapped Healani. He wanted to expose us to the human world. Fortunately, we stopped him before he could do that."
	Aouli's father exhaled. "Things could have gone very badly. It looks like we still have the gods on our side, after all."
	"I think it all comes down to trust," Aouli said knowingly. "If you can find the right person, you'll have a friend for a lifetime. I met a number of people like that, and they were willing to help me free Healani even at the expense of their own safety. For that, I'm forever in their debt."
	"What happened to your hair?" Healani blinked as if she suddenly realized the change.
	Aouli looked around at the crowd gathered at the healer's residence. "It's a long story. Shall I start from the beginning?"

~

	By the following morning, everyone in the village knew of how Aouli had become a human and how he had freed his sister with the help of his human friends. All of them knew about Ruby, the brave girl with the deep-red hair. All of them knew about the little white creature that followed her everywhere. They all knew about Kekoa.
	"Aouli, Aouli!" The village children swam up to him as he made his way toward Ulani's cave. "Off to see Ulani?"
	Aouli turned to offer them a grin. "I am, in fact."
	"Can we come with you?" one of the children asked excitedly. "I don't think I've ever seen Ulani before. My brother told me that she has white hair and white eyes!"
	Aouli arched a brow. "You don't think she's scary?"
	"We think she's cool!" The children all nodded their heads in unanimous agreement.
	Aouli laughed. "Alright, then."
	When he finally reached Ulani's cave with his new entourage, Aouli motioned for them to wait out outside before swimming in to find Ulani.
	"Aouli!" Ulani appeared in front of him with a bright smile on her face. "You came to visit me."
	"You have a lot of visitors this time." Aouli inclined his head in the direction of the cave entrance. "Would you like to meet them?"
	Ulani clapped her hands together eagerly. "Of course! Let's let them in."
	"You heard her." Aouli turned to call out to the children listening in from just beyond the cave entrance. "You can come in."
	The children didn't need to be told twice before they were swimming inside.
	"You're Ulani?" One of the children looked up at Ulani. "You're the sea witch?"
	Ulani smiled. "That would be me."
	"I knew you wouldn't be scary!" the child said proudly. "If anything, you look a lot like my big sister! Come on, come play with us!"
	When Ulani turned to Aouli, he just shook his head with a smile. "You can go on ahead. This was only going to be a brief visit anyway. I promise I'll meet up with you later, but before that, there's one other person I need to pay a visit to first."
	"We'll be waiting for you." Ulani gave Aouli a wink before following the children out of the cave.
	Smiling, Aouli took off toward the direction of the shore.
	After arriving a short distance away from the sand, Aouli let his head break through the surface of the water. He looked out over the powdery sand, and there she was.
	Ruby spotted him almost instantly. She stood up from where she was sitting with her friends to wave at him, smiling widely. Aouli smiled back and swam over to join them.
      Maybe the following day, he'd bring Ulani with him to meet them. While Ulani normally didn't go far from her cave, she had swam all the way out to watch over his sister. And now she had even gone off to play with the village children. Maybe one day, Aouli would even be able to introduce his father and sister to Ruby and her friends.
      His sister was going to become the high chief in a matter of days, and everyone in the village was starting to make preparations for the ceremony that would take place in Healani's honor. This was the best ending Aouli could ask for.
      Today, Ruby and her friends were singing a song. It was the same song Ruby had been singing the day when Aouli had first seen her. It was a song of youth and friendship. A song of the ocean and sky. And even though Aouli didn't know the words, he found himself humming along as well.
      As a soft wind picked up and sent waves washing over the glittering scales of his tail, Aouli knew with certainty that this was a summer he would never forget.

    Chapter 18.5

Ru?y Z: And then Mr. Kekoa even gave me his personal phone number saying that I could call him if I ever needed anything!

Zhang T: Wow. If I got the phone number of a police, I'd feel honored. And a little bit scared.

Ru?y Z: Oh come on. Mr. Kekoa isn't scary. Did you read any of the messages I've been sending you?

Zhang T: I know, I know, I'm just kidding.

Zhang T: I've been reading all of them very intently. Isabelle and San wanted to know everything as well, so I've been reading them out loud to them. You should be proud of me-I'm doing the voices and everything.

Zhang T: If you're going to blame anyone for my slow replies, blame the two of them.

Ru?y Z: So, Tilden, who's San?

Zhang T: Hahaha thought you could catch me off guard now, did you? You're coming back home in a few days. Patience, little sister.
