    Chapter 19

	The plane ride back to San Francisco flew by so quickly that, before Ruby knew it, they had already landed at the airport.
	"We're back!" Mari exclaimed and waved her arms energetically as they stepped off the plane. "Even the sun and clear skies are here to greet us!"
	"It feels like only yesterday that we were flying out to Maui," Grace lamented. "I'm going to miss the warm weather and sandy beaches."
	"I'm going to miss our new friends," Tye said with a sigh. "We really had something going there, you know."
	Ruby gave Tye and knowing smile. "We'll see them again. One day."
	"Look," Tomas said quietly after scanning the people meandering through the airport. "There's Tilden and Isabelle."
	"Hello." Tilden smiled when all of them reached him. "Had a nice trip, did you now?"
	"I can't help but feel jealous of all of you," Isabelle added lightly. "Do take me along with you next time."
	Tilden elbowed Isabelle in the arm. "When you're not busy with summer sessions, I'll buy you a ticket too. Anyway"-Tilden turned to address Ruby and her friends-"the car can fit three of you. I hope the other two of you don't mind riding with my parents. Am I going to drop you guys off at your houses or-"
	"Let's go to Tomas's house," Mari said eagerly. "Today's the day we finally get to meet San!"
	"Is that fine with you?" Tilden turned to look at his parents, and after the two of them had nodded their heads, Tilden turned on his heel. "The car's this way."
	"Who wants to go with Tilden?" Ruby turned to her friends. "I think it would make sense for me to ride back with my parents."
	"I can join you," Mari offered. "The rest of you can go with Tilden and Isabelle."
	Nodding, Grace, Tye, and Tomas went to follow Tilden. Ruby and Mari stayed behind.
	"This reminds me a little bit of the past," Ruby's mom commented as the four of them climbed into the car after loading their bags into the trunk. "I remember when the two of you had playdates, we'd be driving you girls all over the place."
	Mari smiled wistfully. "It does a little bit." She scoped Singsing onto her lap. "Some things have changed, but some things have also stayed the same-we're still great friends, and now we have three other wonderful friends with us too."
	Ruby turned to Mari as the car rolled into motion. "We should hang out more. During this past school year, I felt like I've been so busy I haven't been able to fully involve myself in your club activities or follow your blog."
	Mari shook her head hurriedly. "You don't have to do either of those things. I-"
	"I know I don't have to. But I want to. Let's do some catching up, how does that sound?"
	"It sounds wonderful." Mari's expression melted into a smile, and Ruby grinned back.

~

	When they arrived at Tomas's house, they didn't have to wait long before Tilden's car pulled into the driveway. "Try not to trash the place." Isabelle turned to Ruby and her friends as she stood outside the front door. "My moms won't be back from work until later, and I've got a class in an hour."
	"We know, we know."
	After shaking back her long black hair, Isabelle inserted the key into the lock and pushed the door open.
	"Hello?" Mari called out as she stepped over the threshold after Isabelle.
	Suddenly, there was a flash of motion from the hallway, and Ruby looked over in surprise to see a black-spotted cat pad toward them, curious about the commotion. But the moment the cat noticed everyone staring, it froze and looked in every direction except at the group huddled in the living room.
	"San!" Tilden laughed as he hurried over to scoop the cat into his arms. "Don't be afraid. These are your friends!"
	"San?" Ruby stared at the cat in disbelief.
	To her surprise, Tye had burst out into laughter. "I knew it!" he pointed wildly at the cat. "I knew it!"
	"You knew it?" Grace whirled to face her brother. "You knew San was a cat, and you didn't tell us?"
	"I had a suspicion after Tilden drove us to the airport," Tye explained when he finally stopped laughing. "You know I'm allergic to cats. Tilden must have had cat fur all over him."
	Tilden's eyes danced with laughter. "Looks like only one out of the five of you got me. Alright, kids, game over. Looks like I've won."
	Tomas turned to his sister. "Isabelle, you knew too!"
	 Isabelle tilted her head to the side. "It wouldn't be much fun if I spoiled the grand reveal."
	Tilden cradled the cat in his arms. "I stick to my word, though-San is the joy of my life."
	Ruby finally recovered from her state of shock. "Singsing is going to feel betrayed."
	"Really?" Tilden said mildly. "I think San and Singsing will be great friends."

~

      Ruby sat in her room, the screen of her computer illuminating her face as she scanned through various articles about the ordeal that had gone down on the dock. There were numerous video clips circulating of the moment when Mr. Stevenson had lunged forward to attack, how Aouli had intercepted him and was pushed off the side of the boat, and then how Ruby had leaped into the water after him.
	All the articles talked about who Mr. Stevenson was and how he had gone against the wishes of the company he worked for by polluting the waters behind their backs. Each article described Ruby and Aouli as high school interns working with the camera crew, and fortunately, nothing about Ruby's connection to Mr. Stevenson and the company had found its way into any of them. Her dad's company had spoken to the press themselves, explaining that they had fired Mr. Stevenson for his actions and had nothing more to do with him.
	Suddenly, Ruby's phone buzzed. It was a text from Mari to the group chat. I spent all day working on this digital photo album of our time together in Maui! Mari's message read. Check it out when you have time!
	Ruby smiled and tapped the link Mari had added. The album popped open on her screen, and the pages were decorated with little stickers and tape. As Ruby tapped through the pages, she hadn't realized Mari had taken so many pictures. There were pictures of the beach, the ocean, the house they had been staying at. There were pictures of the restaurants and shops and their friends.
      It was nice sitting there, flipping through the pages and reliving the trip. When Ruby reached the final page, she blinked down at the image. This was the picture Mari had taken with Aouli, and all six of their faces smiled up at the camera.
	Ruby looked at the picture for a long moment before a new notification appeared at the top of her screen. Her friends seemed to have just viewed the album as well and were complimenting Mari for her hard work. After sending her own praises, Ruby stood up and hurried out of her room to knock on the door to her brother's room.
	"What's up," Tilden said as the door to his room opened. San was draped around his shoulders like a furry scarf, and the cat looked very ready to fall asleep at any moment.
	"Did you see the digital photo album Mari sent?" Ruby asked.
	"I haven't." Tilden stepped aside to let Ruby into the room. "My phone's dead. Do show me."
	"What happened to your phone?" Ruby laughed as she looked around Tilden's room. His room was just as tidy as before, and his violin case was sitting on his desk as the perfect centerpiece.
	"San was sleeping on me," Tilden said simply. "I was watching cat videos on my phone, and when it died, the charger was too far away."
	"Right." Ruby shook her head, still smiling. "Well, someone's not practicing."
	Tilden waved her off. "Shh. Let's see this album."
	"Ruby, Tilden," Ruby's mom called up the stairs. "Dinner's ready."
	Ruby motioned for Tilden to follow her downstairs. "Come on. This is perfect-we can show Ba and Ma the album too!"
	Tilden nodded and untangled San from him as if the cat really was a scarf.
	"Coming!" Ruby called down the stairs as she waited for her brother. Tilden shut the door behind him, keeping San safely inside. As much as Ruby and Tilden hoped that Singsing would get along with San, the puppy's hyper energy was still too much for the poor cat. But if they gave the two some time, Ruby was confident they'd warm up to each other with a little coaxing.
	After hurrying down the stairs, Ruby took her seat at the table.
	"Here." Ruby's dad piled food onto his children's plates. "Have some vegetables."
	"Where's the meat?" Tilden jokingly complained. "Under all these vegetables, it's practically hidden!"
	"Look at how skinny you are!" Ruby's mom reached for the meat dish. "Here-" But before she could spoon a serving onto Tilden's plate, Ruby's dad put a hand on her arm.
	"Vegetables are good for you." Ruby's dad chuckled. "Have some more." Ever since Ruby's dad had been promoted to the position of CEO, his entire deminor was happier than Ruby had seen him in many years. But it wasn't only because of his new position-Mr. Stevenson being gone now also played a big role.
	As her family chatted and laughed together, Ruby grinned. She had gone on an adventure and then returned home to her family. There was no better way to spend the summer.

    Epilogue
One Year Later

	"That was just our last class of the day," Ruby said with a smile as she brushed her red-tipped hair over her shoulder. "Our last class of high school."
	Tye looked around the hallways at the flood of students slowly but steadily dispersing. "It feels almost surreal in a way. This will be our last time walking these halls."
	Ruby sighed. "It's only been, what, four years here? I wish we didn't have to spend these last hours with finals."
	"Oh, we're not finishing our high school experience with finals," Tye said knowingly. "We've still got the variety show, after all. Don't start worrying about how you did on the finals until we've basked in the glory of our performance."
	Ruby clapped Tye on the back. "I should be the one saying that to you." There was a thud as all the books in his backpack toppled over.
	"Oh look, now you've done it," Tye said, but he was laughing too.
	"Hi!" Grace said in an excited whisper as she hurried over to the two of them.
	"Mari and Tomas should already be waiting in the auditorium by now," Ruby noted. "Come on, let's go catch up."
	Nodding, the twins followed Ruby down the hallway.
	"How did your finals go?" Ruby turned to Grace as they made their way out of the academic building.
	Grace gave Ruby a small smile. "I'm feeling pretty good about them, actually. I'm more worried about my scores on the AP tests at this point."
	"I'm sure you did great on them," Ruby reassured her friend. "Last year you were worrying about them too, but you ended up getting fours and fives on all of them!"
	When the three of them arrived at the auditorium, they found Mari and Tomas waiting for them in front of the stage. The front seats were reserved for all the performers, and Mari jumped up to wave them over. Her brown hair was in its signature twin braids as always, and today she wore a special bright pink beanie for the occasion.
	Tomas rose to his feet as well-not that he had much of a choice since his fingers were still enterlaced with Mari's.
	"Ready?" Mari asked excitedly. "I'm so nervous-all five of us have been working so hard for this."
	"We're going to go out there and have fun," Ruby said determinedly.
	"Look," Tomas said quietly as he nodded in the direction of the audience. "We've already got a sizable crowd."
	Grace stood on her tiptoes to scan the sea of faces. "I can see my parents! Ruby, your parents are there too! And there's Tilden!"
	"Look, Tomas!" Mari pointed to the doors of the auditorium. "There's your parents."
	An announcement sounded, and the quiet murmuring that filled the auditorium subsided. "We need the first ten acts backstage. If you are performing in one of the first ten acts, please make your way backstage now."
	"That's us!" Ruby grinned. "Let's go!"
	
~

	Standing in the wings of the stage with her guitar in hand and her friends by her side, Ruby looked out at the dancers currently performing their own routine. She still couldn't believe that she was graduating. Time seemed to have gone by in a blink of an eye.
      Time was an interesting ocean full of twists and turns, bends and folds. An ocean where one could look back over their shoulder at the waters but never quite touch them. The waves were like memories, washing up and then fading away only to wash up again.
	Ruby had plans for the future now. Her friends all had plans for the future: Grace was going to New York to pursue her dream of becoming a professional dancer. She received the news of her acceptance the same week her dance instructor gave her a lead role in their production, and she called Ruby each time to ecstatically share the news. Tye, on the other hand, was going somewhere even farther than the East Coast; he was planning to spend a couple of years studying abroad in Europe.
	Mari would be staying in the area. Much to her delight, she had managed to get into the big university across the bay. At first, Mari had been looking at schools all over the country. Now that she and Tomas were in a relationship, both were willing to do long-distance since Tomas was planning to stay in San Francisco to study music. However, now they wouldn't be as far apart as they had first thought.
	And Ruby? Ruby would be taking a year off-a gap year. During that time, she planned to travel to Maui and intern at a marine biology lab. There was a certain somebody on the island Ruby couldn't help but look forward to seeing again . . .
	"And our next performers are Grace Benson, Tye Benson, Mari Fields, Tomas Quevedo, and Ruby Zhang!" the announcer's voice rang out.
	Ruby could feel her friends' eyes on her, and she turned to give them all a bright smile as she secured her guitar strap. This was their time to shine. This performance marked the end of their high school experience and the beginning of their journey into the world. Even though their paths were branching out in different directions, Ruby knew this wouldn't be their last performance together.
	There was applause as the five of them stepped out of the wings and onto the stage. They took their positions in front of the various microphones that had been set up for them. This time, Ruby and Mari stood side by side, with both of their microphones set up at the front of the stage.
	When the applause finally subsided, Grace counted off the beat, and then the music started. Ruby's fingers formed each chord with ease, and as the muscle memory started kicking in, she let herself get lost in the music.
      This song was a duet. It was a song of youth and friendship, of the ocean and sky. A song of secrets and truths. It was the song of the children they had been and the five young adults they had become.
	Grace's drums were like a lively dance, Tye's bass was a steady beat, and Tomas's keyboard work even more impressive than it had been the last time Ruby had heard it during their practice session.
	Then the last chord was hit, and as the sound faded, the audience erupted into applause. Ruby smiled out at the crowd. Her breathing was heavy, and her heart rate was quick from all the adrenaline. All the faces, familiar and not so familiar, were smiling back at her.
      As she turned around to look at her friends, Ruby couldn't help but smile and smile and smile. And together, they all joined hands on center stage and took a bow.
      This was the start of a new adventure.
